O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O ye, most precious sons, I have completed this book which is the following of the science of medicine, assembled and fulfilled by its completion, and made the end according to its explanations and by its declaration.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I will complete this with your help, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forced in our region and strange everywhere, so has been lost the science and forgotten, and there remains only from it that the small descriptions in books of the ancients which have been moved by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the folly, and are closed the intentions, and are far away the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will live and bring back to life the ordering of this treatment according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I came together with the forms of the cautery instruments, and with other tools of the work in conjunction with the joining of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there is no good master of hands to be found in our times, the art of medicine has been stretched.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary that he who enters into this practice should understand the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows how to measure the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and joints and the number of these parts, and the movement and the stillness, and from them their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because he says that the nose is very much with the skin, and the flesh is little; and it is the same in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	So we say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not familiar with the things said, will guard himself so as not to make a mistake and will avoid those men; just as I have wanted many times more from those who interrupt this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Because I saw a foolish doctor who lanced an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and cut open her arteries on the neck; because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who treated a stone from the bladder of an old man, and the stone was large; he took out with it a piece of the bladder, and died three days later in his own home.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had heard that they call it the treatment, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the wound, and I knew whether the patient would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another man who was treated for his wound by the Duke of our land, who had broken his leg and with the break got an infection; and the doctors, blinded by ignorance, bound the break on the wound with strong leather, and did not leave it alone to heal, and in that way I finished it, and he commanded him not to untie it; and he remained like that until the leg was completely swollen and the feet and came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie his leg; and when I saw it was dislocated, he was in peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread by the limb until the limb had lost all its vitality.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another method which destroys the pus and charms it, and then inflames with the evil of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a cancer when it is purified with melancholic humors does not require that it be touched with iron unless there is no chance to remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And dear son, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: it means to see if there is danger in more than one disposition; and I will show you in each book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because it is necessary that you take care of yourselves, so that the physicians may not speak ill of you. If you take your arms in your bed, and take your sick ones lightly and firmly, and use the best way, so by the grace of God you will come to health and be praised; and let fear of the dreadful diseases of illness depart from you, and put your armor away that makes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take medicine for bad illness, lest you be called a fool doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about cauterization of fire and cauterization with medicine, and the chapters are arranged from head to feet; and forms of dressings, and instruments of cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and wounds, and extractions of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are arranged in order and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twisting, and similar things; and it is ordered as follows: the head of each piece, just as a joint, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we remember the work, it is fitting to say what the quality of aid and the danger of each condition are.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and danger are the longest words and subtle knowledge and the secret responses; and those who are wise among the learned speak about these things and agree on them; and they are unwilling to hear my long words because I am too tedious.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire cautery is universally helpful to all kinds of matter, regardless of whether it is cold or hot.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In cold and dry matter together, some have discussed and said that fire cautery is great help; and the others said the opposite: that fire cautery does not do anything to illnesses that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated for hot illnesses with heat or dryness, but rather those who say the opposite claim that fire cautery does great help to hot and dry illnesses that come into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you buy the body of man and its moisture is in accordance with the nature of fire, you find that the body freezes.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all the paths do not take fire unless one who has tried it knows how to apply the cautery, and is familiar with long usage of cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and remedies and space in time; for other complexions we have no fear, themselves also in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors agreed and concurred on using cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, sons, that cautery combines fire with the secrets of cures, and greater good than applying hot medication.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from fire except to a limb that is burned, and it does not affect any other limb if it is not named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicines carried from one member to another by moving, make the afflicted member sick with disease and pain; and by chance, the fire does not harm the patient because of its height and due to the goodness of its substance, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And what I have found through experience and the long service and study that I have put into this art, is on display in nature; and therefore I excuse myself from being lengthy in speech, because it does not please me to reveal to you the secret of fire, and the quality of its work, by which it cures diseases of the body, as the philosophers said, demonstrating it.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, when they will agree on what time the cauterizations must be done, and they set up prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is beneficial in all times, because the harmful consequences are removed by the aid of cauterization; and oneself is cured from painful necessities beyond and hard to bear which cannot wait until greater harm befalls the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, dear son, as to how the foolish ones behave; because the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and they say so thus; but it's not like what they think, for cauterization is not just a medicine that moves the complexion, dries out the humors which are the cause of pain, and brings about swift results as a medicine, because of its speed and virtue, and the value of its work and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	In order to treat the disease once and for all according to the patient's complexion and the nature of the disease and its virtue; and since these superfluities are gathered in him from the acquisition of food and similar things, if you do not administer cauteries to him when he has little superfluity and moisture, as is done with cauteries of density for pain, and similar things, this pain does not return; but this happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the behind of medicine, and this is seeing; but they do not believe that cautery has any value after medicine, their opinions are false, and cautery is considered the back of medicine because when we administer various types of cures for no illness at all, they do not work, so we give them cautery, and it is valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And then open, for cutting with fire is the medicine of the rear parts, not according to the foolish opinions.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cutting with gold instruments is more potent than with iron, and they say that fire is used only because of the quality of the gold and its substance; and they say that the lead of a cautery does not cause putrefaction, but it is not seen because I have proven it, and I have found that it is so in some men; and cutting with gold is more effective than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And you should not know when you heat an instrument of gold, that it is cooled down by the color of the gold, and immediately cools; and if it is heated too much, then they put it in the fire; and so there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery so that what has been moved may be fixed at our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter on the treatment of the upper joints just as if they were at the foot.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moist and cold on the head, because one does it for the cause of a disease called "soda", and also for many humors that come out of the head to the eyes, ears, and because of numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and themselves for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with medicinal solution, cleansing the head and removing the third or fourth foulness, according to what the virtues, age, and habit of the patient can bear; and then clean the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on some cloth; after placing the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and when you come to his two middle fingers, if they bleed from the incision, then take up the cautery called "olivare", because this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the knife on the patient's skin, and make a small incision with your hand a little at a time, turning it around; then lift your hand immediately, and reset the wound if you see a small bone exposed; and if you don't see an exposed bone, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I told you before; after take some silk, put on gauze and soft cotton inside, and place on the skin, and let it stay for three days; then cover with a moile cloth in fat; and leave on top until the incision is closed; afterwards cure the wound of the torn flesh which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if the old ones said, when it stays on the wound longer, it gets worse; and for this reason you should apply ointment.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that you must so cauterize the wound that part of the bone is burned, and then replace what has been burned with bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they also said that you must cauterize it so severely above, and push it so hard when it is lowered as far as the bone is just as wide as a thorn that women sew into their girdles; for this reason the humors will come out fresh from outside; after that, one must cure and soak.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good in all things; fires that bring relief to some men when they have no choice but to fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; for the joints are weakened by continuous solutions from nature, just as we testify in other members; and also, when it comes to the joint of the sick person, it is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more salutary and healing for me, and therefore I use this remedy.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When all the head comes with chronic pain that lasts for a long time, and he must use the patient's herbs and pills called "cochie", and expectant of purging of head and oil and emplaster; and if they make him cautery as we have said before, and it does not bring relief.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Beware so that the patient's joints are of strong nature and not too frozen; then make the cauterization under that cautery as we have said before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After making cauterization on each horn of the head until the bone, just as we have said, and make another cautery on the one that is called "vasselz"; and it is this one where you put ventouses; and tie your hand so that you do not see through to the bone: the patient feels much more great pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary that the cauterizations on the horns be more subtle than those which are made for the mortality of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When pain suddenly occurs in one part of the head, and the disease is spread to the scalp, and the hairs are pulled out by medicinal means, and other treatments have been done as I mentioned earlier, but none of them help: then you must perform cautery according to two ways, namely hot medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of hot medicine is that you take an ounce of aloes, remove the scab and reapply it over the two hairs, and then perform a cauterization at the temple in such a way that you can replace the ounce of aloes under the skin; when it is replaced, so that the lie is tied and restrained well and left for 12 hours; then unbind and treat with hot fire the ounce of oil, and leave the wound for 2 days or 3 days; then put on a cotton plug soaked in butter until the injury heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of wounds until it is healthy; and if you see if do what I have written about burning medicines, which I have prescribed or ordered to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of what is this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a clover or has little wormwood, and at its center a small appearance; and places it on the painful place, holds your hand, and twists the iron lightly until the middle part of the spice that burns is burned; and lifts your hand that the artery does not burn, which is before, and drains abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After metting cotton in awe of the vein and putting sor on the leaf for three days; then put cotton moist with butter, and cure the leaf with ointment until it is sanez; and if you want to cauterize this emigraine with cautery called "cultellare" at its full point, and keep from covering the artery in this emigraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the migraine.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	As you cure the migraine as we have said in divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cauterys before mentioned by medicine and iron do not help at all, then it is necessary to heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and so put a line of two halves of oil on the leaf, and hold your hand once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and that it does not come near the bone; and be careful of the mandible that mutes when we eat, and let the nerves have no regard except for the mute and spasms do not appear to the patient, and be careful of the decrement of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting has great fear and myself also for he who does not know how to do it, and who is not studied; and leave the operation in my way; but I will tell you how one can sustain life when the artery is cut, and I will show you to him at what place it appears in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If the fire cautery does not relieve the illness, and the patient suffers, cauterize the wound in the same way as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said on the chapter of artery extraction, with the cauterization having two handles; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of pain from the ears due to frostbite.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes from the ear due to frost, and you have tried solutive medicines and other cures that we have said on division, and the pains do not cease, then apply this cauterization which is called "pins", because it has this form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After piercing all around the diseased ear, or between the two ears if it causes pain in both, and then pushing a little towards the root of the ear after staining the area with the cautery, wait for X points around each ear; after the treatment let them be so that they are sane.
de la torture de la bouche	From the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cauterization only of those that move from a swollen tongue, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make cauterization on the appearances that come from dryness and pus.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this appearance of torture that is muffled by a swollen tongue, dryness, and purging of the head and gargareism, and since it's true, then you must cauterize the patient with III cauters: one in the root of the ear, and another slightly behind the temple, and the third near the joining of the two lips; put the cautery on the part that is open and healthy, and cauterize directly the head of the ear above a little below the corn of the head, and another in the temple as long as an inch; and let the cautery stay there until the moisture of the cure is dried.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is like the shape of a scimitar which we have shown before, but it is a bit more subtle and it should be that the cutting instrument is a bit larger; after treatment let him recover as I said, until he is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is an old disease and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the sick person does not have fever, then do four cauteries: two on each of the two horns of the head, one at the forehead, and one in the place called "vessel" which we have mentioned before, and a cautery on the lower part of the stomach near the mouth; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	of lachrymation (lacrimation).
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease it is fitting to give the patient great and large pills, as well as a powder of mind-altering ingredients. After that, take the head of the sick person, and place the emplastre of sinapis on the occipital bone, which is written in treating emplastres; and this is the manner of cautery: if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healthy in this way, it is good; and if not, do III cauteres on the gums of the head when going down to the neck, and have space between each cautery I duo of large ones; and treat him as others, and if you see a joint sticking out, and the patient suffers, do I cauteries in the middle; and if he is strong, II cauteries above the two horns, and the cure until he is healthy; and let be the cauteries which are called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with years and what we have said before; after taking the head of the patient, then do cauteries on the gums of the head and above each horn, and I at the back and III above the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the disease is severe, then do IIII cauteries above the spine of the back; and let it stay until the fever subsides, and lift your hand; after that, treat him as long as he is healthy, and let be the cauteries which are called "olivare" what we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should use fire cautery only on those who are flaky, and it is best to first cleanse the brain of years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and suffers from many pain medicines.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer, he will make gargling and mastication cleanse the brain often with bones meat; after he makes the head rich in milk, and then he does fire cautery according to what we have said before, and on the shoulder, and on each horn; and if the patient suffers greatly, he should do fire cautery as I told to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine at the back and neck, and so he should do fire cautery with olive oil according to the way I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, then if they make the fire cautery subtle according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by the cause of melancholy there are superfluities or moist ones corrupted and swollen greatly, then the cautery for cuttings as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities are declining to melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moist, then the doctor should give him something for which the intellects must be purified, according to what it is in front in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the head of the sick person; after making the linen bandage well-made, like a circle, if you tie it on the head; and the patient must cross his fingers, and they should be held in all parts; after presenting the linen, and applying ointments of pure goat's fat ancient; and the heat is tempered so that the doctor can pour it into him when he can suffer it; after emptying the circle by tying it inside the head, and letting it cool down; and doing this to each patient once a week with another good governance, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see cautery being done while making multiple pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery is most beneficial for the brain, and then cover it with moist cotton in butter and linen grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye pain comes first from the signs that I said in the division, then begin and do thus: give to the patient a purifying drink of wine, and clean off all moisture from the head, and make him sweat or take a bath several times at dawn.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After instructing him to look at his head, and making cauterization on the swollen part of the head, and making two more cauterizations on the temples if there are symptoms in both eyes together, or one if there is a symptom in one; cut all over the cautery the veins and arteries that are under the wound, and make them cauterize long according to the length of the temple; and watch for concussion of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, stain him with as little force as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and by incision how to do it carefully; and never make a cautery or a hatereil behind the two bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the eyes' blood
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	How the blood of the eyes is old and accustomed when it lies on the veins, or where there are arteries that appear to be outside the head; and one sees that it's a surplus of cold, flaccid humors, therefore do as I said in the beginning when I was saying let the cautery descend downwards to the eyes: cut off the eyebrows, and two cauteries on each temple, and two cauteries behind the two bones; and if there is need more, cauterize with a fine needle above the eyebrow.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	A man's body in sorrow through within his eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in division, and he does not benefit from it, then give him three bitter medicines; after his head, and cut fire or on a mile of olive oil cautery; and do two cauteries of cautery called "clavilis" above the two sores, one below the eyebrows; and beware of the artery that you will cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see it, do the cautery on the two sores as well, just as long as the sores are; and do not leave your hand alone except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	One hair that sticks out when it's wet.
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is never any occasion that the hairs of the sores are converted to scar tissue, and they prick at it, and then you do cautery according to two manners: that is to say, by fire or with hot medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in your own room; after so he should write on a piece of paper how it was like as the wick of myrrh, and how it began from the sign of the hairs; then put cotton soaked in oil of beeswax and musk on the wound.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked little by little several times, until the wounds are closed to the point; and the signs of health of the work is that you see the paper withdrawn, and the hairs lifted towards the point of the oil; then let your hand go, and leave thus for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter until the scabbing is removed; after the treatment of ointment until he is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow after this, and the paper becomes soft again, then resume cautery on the same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are fallen, cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural position, even and not pulling on the hair with oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of the medicine that burns is to instruct the patient to let the hairs grow as long as they are great and even; then make a parchment the shape of mint leaf; take French soap and live charcoal each one .2, and crush them together well; and do it hastily, if it does not cool down, then place on the form that you have made like the leaf of mint, and put on the paper of the eyes; and if the patient holds in oil alone, then you must also do it twice; and put cotton wool soaked in oil under it. And apply the head of the patient to your healthy side and show off the medicine, and press .2 pouders (powders) every time the patient feels pain from the medicine, because he feels pain as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your body.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the swelling has passed, then lift the limb high, and reward yourself if you see that it is lifted just as it was lifted by heat or incision; and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not so, then put the medicine back on the limb or let the medicine cease working until your wounds are even and your eyes be fixed; then put soft cloth in butter on it until the wounds are closed, after applying ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must guard yourself well at your wound with great care so that it does not touch the medicine,
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes dry after, and the hair pricks in the oil, so resume the medicine on that one who has become moist with his own natural paper, just as you have done before; until the cure is healed. And this is the form of a fire cauterization made by myrrh.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	Know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to this so be your exertions; and do not reply to the straight way for one who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by fire cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures are not profitable, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in a clean place; and take the bandages on his head and tie them between your hands in that manner that he does not move or lose his head; after put wet cotton in a vessel of oil or juice of persillion on it; after heat the cautery which is in that shape as it resembles a quill of vulture, so they are set together; if you see, it will be marked from one end of the head to the other, and if you see, it will be like an awning; but whatever, this one value for your benefit.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the abscess it bursts open and takes out the pus and dries it; and if it is closed, then apply, and take fire to the bowels; after put the hot cautery in the shape of which, and keep your hand on the cautery near the painful part towards the oil, so that your hands do not go mad; and put the cautery into the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you are coming to the beginning of the cautery just at the bone, then it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not work, then restart the cautery again once and if needed, repeat it another time. Then put on a cotton cloth soaked in fat for 3 days; then apply the ointment desiccating until it is safe to heal, and after 40 days pass if it is still not healed, then put on medicine that causes the acid to eat through the bone so that the bone is exposed; and follow what he comes to in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is also a method of cautery for a fistula that none of the ancient ones said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Let it heal first and then make the incision; after putting in the incision, put in there finely camphor so that this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and make it to the quantity of one .3 [of blood], and hold your hand over the wound firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, until the poultice is dissolved and runs down its oil; and it is necessary to put on the patient a moist cloth in wool or in vinegar: the poultice art used by the physician of fistula, and it heals for marvelous cleanliness.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	But if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If it is not so, then if necessary administer poultices on the wound, and bring the fistula back to the body according to what seems good in his own proper care.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are fissures in the lips called "poil", and similarly in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fissures according to what we have said in our divisions, and the treatment does not help, then take a small cauterization with a culinary knife in that shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it immediately in those fissures until blood comes forth; after treatment, let the wound be treated with clay so that it heals.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the uvula or on the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after it is infected and putrid and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in our divisions, but it does not help: therefore, it seems that you should apply cauterization according to the size of the fistula; after cutting and dressing the fistula, keep your hand until the iron comes out from under it, and at the root of it; and do this once or twice, after treating as we have said in our treatments, so long as it heals; and if it is healed thus, that is good; but if not, then it seems to need to discover the bone and remove the corrupted one, according to what you find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	Double movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat with medicines, and that does not work, then put the head of the patient on a clean cloth; after apply the cautery in such a way that you place a chain around the tooth; and put inside the cautery hot metal sharply, and hold your hand so the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after release your hand and continue the cautery according to your will; after fill the patient's mouth with vinegar and let it stay for an hour and rich fire.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a way the teeth which were moving are fixed, and the gums softened restrained, and the moistures corrupted dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from coldness, or there is coldness in the ear, and medicines do not help, then it is necessary to cut according to two methods: fire cautery and butter cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is done thus: you take butter from a healthy person and apply it to the point with a spoon of iron or flint; after taking cotton and wrapping around the tip of a tent, put melted butter on the aching tooth immediately and hold until it cools down; and do so repeatedly until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see milk-like substance and cotton and butter melt, apply it to the aching tooth, and put iron hot so that the fire reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cautery is assembled like this: so that you tie a chain of iron or rope around it and make it thick enough so the heat does not come to the patient's mouth. After heating the cautery, for sure the form will come out after, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will be stopped that very day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is fitting that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of applying this cautery, and then rushes to pull it out; and this is what the form of the cautery looks like:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make fire cautery where you wish, and according to what power you have; and this is the form of the chain:
des scrophules	de scrofulae  (the scrofula disease)
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is of a runny and moist nature, and will not yield to digestion by medicines, then apply the cautery to the hair so that this follows afterwards. And give it two openings for the discharge to issue from the cautery on the other side; and place the cautery hot above the abscess once, or when it is suited, until it comes to a head of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply cautery accordingly to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and put on moist cotton wool in butter until the swelling is resolved; after treatment, set the limb straight again with ointments and poultices until he is cured.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the snake.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistors conquer on the channels of the body, and itself when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be voided first by medicines soluble; after applying cautery to the root of the throat, and you must not come more to the throat, but burn with one stroke only.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the second cautery is applied to the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and apply cautery to the "clavicle", because we have the shape before; treat the patient as we have previously said until he is healthy.
de la toust	of the tooth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all diseases of the body are caused by cold moistors, and the patient does not have fever nor is dry, and the disease is old, apply two cauteries to the groin in each view; and a second cautery on the space between the two nipples; and apply cautery to the "clavicle" as previously said according to the shape mentioned.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	If you see them, perform fire cautery by pricking at the entire area called "points" because of which the form is present in ear disease; and let the points be 30, or more if they enter.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment according to what is said before, and let there be three pricks according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because it is easier to do so, because you make three cuts at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After the patient is laid on his back and on his chest; after lift the wound that is inside the swelling with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within it, so heat the cautery which has two nails in its shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the wound so that it perforates just like on the costal side, and the figure of the cautery comes with four cauteries; and for this, the cautery is made with the one having three nails, because these are the forms of cautery; and they come in accordance with the subtlety of a net and this is the shape of the cautery which has three nails:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And at times it is pressed against this nerve because there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying heat with a cauterizing tool, put the cautery on the broken bone with thread; then make the patient rest and do not keep the limbs still for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if the head of the shoulder is dislocated, since this happens little often, then apply cauterizing on thick bone or many cauterizing points.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and it is covered with moisture and it heals the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When frost is in the stomach and much moisture remains, then it must be extracted to its condition, and many purges occur to it, and the usual remedies do not benefit it, therefore it is necessary that the patient lies on his back, and extends his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	In the end after the third fire cautery I do one cautery under the nail of the finger by the amount of two, all over the cautery nail, and two cauteries in front of the two bones so that the figure of the cautery is at three angles, and has an equal space between each one so they are not assembled together when they get infected; and let the cautery be such that it pricks both parts of the heart, and the figure of the cautery should be like this near to the joint:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that one cautery is cut with a great cautery in the stomach according to this shape; and if anyone fears this cautery, then cut it pointwise and sign above the stomach at one spot according to the size which you see of 'enche'; then cut all the cautery which is called 'poins'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As for the liver, pain from churning and moisture and great swelling arises, so that it is forced out of its natural condition due to superfluous things. The sick are cured with what we have said in divisions, and they do not benefit, unless the patient lies on his stomach; and this is a sign that three cauteries should be performed according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, excluding the hypochondriacs, to the left or right of the spleen, when there comes space between each cautery; and it should be done with long cauteries of the body, and not press hard at all; and only burn the middle part of the liver, and the patient lies directly on his feet; if he cannot, then is seated, and extends his legs, and lifts his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If your will is, then cauterize these cauteries of the cutlery, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and take care not to burn all your blood, for you would be drying out all the body; and lest it come to boiling, for the blood is very subtle at that point, and knowledge to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When an abscess forms in the liver, and you see whether it is within the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not very strongly; if it is in the membrane, he feels severe and unbearable pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure needs to drain the abscesses, it is fitting that the patient be placed under his head; and then they sign him onto where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to the razor, because of its shape.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Instruct the cautery to cauterize so that the wounds are burned, and it comes into contact with pus, until the wound is completely healed; after treatment according to the nature of the disease so that the patient is healed; and it should not be used from this cautery any fire other than by one who has studied long in the art of medicine, and whose hands have cured these diseases at some time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And so one can boldly perform it, and often I think that wounds should be left alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of cauterizing the pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said to cauterize pleurisy with the roots of aristoge, and in this way: take a long root of aristoge, as big as you can find, dry it, and make it just as big and just as long as your thumb; and cover it with oil, and press it onto the fire, and cauterize with cautery between the lung and the neck, and five small cauteries near the chin; and one cauterization below the fifth cost; and another above the stomach; and two between the shoulders, and two on either side of the cauterization between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather make it so as in aromatics.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said that an ancient man used cautery of fire similar to the razor, and heated it and placed it between the ribs, until it comes to the point where it is incised; and he sears the pain, as we have said in the apostle of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is great fear for the sick, or they are dead now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of mice.
