Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the mouse disease, of which we have said in the divisions of the treatments, and it does not benefit, then they assert that there are three ways of cautery that all are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one way is that you make three or four cauterizations, linking them according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery on the liver that we have said before; and do not press your hand too hard at all the cautery, so that the sick person lies on his back; and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery that has two edges, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound where the mouse is located, or when the cost comes from the left side, and lift the wound according to the size of the body, according to the length of the flesh, and the cauteries are according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to pour two fingers of wine into the wound so that they can be felt on the other side, and then apply heat to the cautery, and so four times. And if you see that there is only three left, cauterize all the cautery to three fingers.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has been soiled with rot for a long time, and this is what we said before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Fire is not good for dropsy, except when applied to the way called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the ways we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations inside the wound, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one above the navel, and two behind, on the spine, and one in the back.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the cautery burn for a long time, open it by cutting out the putrid flesh; and do not leave the cure of the patient after the cautery; lest the healing be hastened, and both wounds will be worse together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the same as that which we have shown before; and it is olive oil for the back, according to what has been placed here.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical and full of bile citron, it is necessary to cautery on the back of the foot between the auricle and the little toe; and lift your hand with the cautery so that you turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, otherwise it will melt like fire, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing the two legs again, do each leg with two cauteries at the point of the cutlery; and let one cautery be longer from the knee before and another after it in the leg; and let the cauteries remain long enough to cure what's in them; after curing the other treatments that we have said.
de la menoison	of the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When there is a solution of the belly coming from cold and moisture, to the point where the virtues that are retained and digestive which is in the stomach and intestine are effloresced and cannot be cured by any other means; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with a very violent vertigo, do I grant cautery on the stomach according to what was spoken of before or the stomach cautery, in a circular movement; and four cauteries inside the belly subtle ones around all the cautery with sharp blades subtle, and two cauteries above the hanches.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, perform fire cautery on the fingernail, and fire cautery on each joint, and two times fire cautery on the stomach beneath the great one, because the cure is beneficial when it has good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at their base, or one or more of them, and are old and large with cold and moist humors corrupted, treat as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit if you do cauteries: three times on the spine behind the back, the one that is entirely in front of the almeçade, little by little in triangular fashion, and one cautery below; and if you think the stomach is cold and the meat does not roast, and the face swells up, then put a grant cautery on the stomach, as has been said before, and another above the liver, and another above the muscles with all cauteries; and let the cautery stay for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment let the limb be healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "theelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the flesh, if it is inflamed as if by a razor, and then burns it completely on the flesh cut off; and let go of your hand so that the cautery comes to the surface of the vein, because it will not penetrate; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh to be cut, cauterize each part as we have said; after the treatment of ointments, let them heal until they are sane; and if you cauterize a great cautery on a swollen spot, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of badly treated wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patients cannot endure a lance or an opening, what we will tell him in his own tongue, if it comes to this illness that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is a fistula and it has become inflamed, decayed, and putrid due to moisture and corruption, if you examine it thoroughly, and notice how deep it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After applying the cautery that seems like a razor, and pouring it into the fistula according to how much the wound is open, repeatedly applying the cautery until the infected and corrupted flesh are burned away, one or two times, depending on how deeply the infection has set in; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is exposed, and watch for great pains.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	Inflamed fistulas in the body of the testicle and intestine, if you warn yourself about these signs, do not apply fire to the groin only when it is cold, and think that they are not personal; after a cure, keep him so long as he becomes sane, and if the signs of infection appear and the materials are ossified long time, then know that he has become completely sane; and if the materials are not ossified, know that he has died, and corrupted the bones to the bone; and thus, like one of those we will speak in his place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from the fruit comes to the kidneys, and great swelling, and cannot urinate as much as usual, then it is convenient that you make a cautery on the kidneys of one part and another, using the cautery claw like we have previously mentioned; and if the cautery wounds are in the middle, three cauterizations in line will be needed, and more aid will result.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and swollen from heat and moisture, if it retains urine, then do fire cautery in the part facing upwards over the bladder, where the hairs of the nose begin, both to the right and left, and cut each one as long as you can with a finger; and hold the cauterization on the back where you have need; and cut them according to the form that has been said before.
de la marris	of the gallbladder
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the gallbladder is cold and moist, and it doesn't let itself be felt because it's swollen, and its flowers are corrupted and their ends are late; and when they come, if it causes great pain: then it is fitting that you do III cauterizations inside the belly, as we have said for cautery of the bladder, and II cauterizations behind the back; and cut them according to what we have said.
de la hainche	From the hunch
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist viscous fluids descend to the joint of the hunch, and because of this they move out of their place, and the signs are that the knee is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the joints are swollen in some departures, so it is advisable to cauterize the patient on the joint of the hunch with a fire cautery similar to a circle, and sign before the joint as the joint turns, so that the joint is within the circle; and if it is cauterized like those who have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make three cauteries of the large olive oil, and do them as far in as all the joints. Let the cure until he becomes healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin, and it is of cold and moisture, and patients are treated with what we have said in division, but the cure does not work, and the disease is ancient: therefore it is fitting that you purge the patient of gross humors, or fetid pills, or other hard-like pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After purging him with fire; and the manner of the fire cautery is two in number: namely, assembling hot medicines, and cautery of fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is also many in number: among which one is that you cauterize on the groin area; three fire cauteries are done according to this shape, and make great depth and size, and space between each cautery the thickness of two does, and use olive oil cauteries; sometimes it is done at the midpoint on the chief of the groin, because there are four in this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, so the cauterization on the cautery of the circle that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the haunch; but do it in such a manner that the circles contain all the haunch, and all the small points burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way to do it in sciatik, when the pain stays in the haunch and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the knee.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and the knee, then for every pain that the patient says he feels, two cauteries are made on the outside of the ankle; one on the left side a little, whatever the cut may be: either the cutlery cautery or burning the thick skin. And if the patient feels the pain extending as far as two feet or almost to the knee, then make cauteries where he feels the pain three points or four at the cautery called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	Instruct the patient if necessary, to do it more; and if he sees that the pain is below the kneecap towards the thigh, perform fire cautery with a cauterizing cutellaire or circular knife, and take good care in all your cauteries so that you do not let the cautery burn the nerves and great arteries, and do not cause the patient more great nuisance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen others who had fire applied to the ankle on the foot, and they let it burn so that the leg was entirely bare, and also the foot, and it became perceived and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a treatment of the abdomen that led to death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	If the pains are in both upper and lower parts together, do fire cauterization in one and the other.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	Instruct the wise men to make in cautery of the hainche (which means 'hen') thus is the manner: make such a hammer as this [points to an imaginary hammer] and let it be of the head as big as ours, or one less, and let it pass through each other in alternates so that there is space between them like the width of an ear of corn; and let the spaces be two-thirds, and also be like our teeth; and have a well-made iron handle; and this is their form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated so that it is red and smoldering, and then put it on top of the diseased hen, and turn it over to its healthy side; and once it has cauterized with one cautery, let it stay for three days; and then apply a poultice of butter, and let the wound open for a long time; after that, administer treatment as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its effect, and if you see few who use it; and since it seems to be one of the good cauteries, which can endure, and at which place where it occurs.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make an instrument between two bars, in which it follows the edge of a door, and is made of iron or linen to a length visible, and has II [two] us, and has between each one the quantity of the thickness of a doves [dove's] neck; and over and under, and join together as this form.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the flax of the hawthorn on the patient lying on his cost side, and press your hand very much on the flax of the hawthorn; after pour some hot water between the two circles of the awl that have been heated a little by the fire, and let it remain for one hour, and suffer the patient the heat and the burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It finds mordication in the same way as fire; and when the mordications pass, lift your hand with the instrument and move the hump of the jaw downwards sweetly, and leave for three days, and put on butter so that what is black from the splintering becomes absorbed; and let it stay three more days until it rots in the wound; and this would be the rear aid after the treatment of limbs till it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to just up to the thigh or just down to the leg, then use that instrument which you heat according to what you have done with the jaw before; and this is the way of the hot sweat, and I have written it in the treatment of medicine for rectification.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take calomel and quicksilver, equal amounts of both, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	In case of small defects that cannot be seen except for the point of a splinter entering; and put over that hole another pot with better weight, and put above it alkaline and chalk and apply sweet on top, until there are two more puffs of powder to grasp in your hand; and leave it thus until they come out wet and sticky like wax or pot plaster, then take all that away, and place upon chalk and upon alkaline so as it was before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And if it becomes very wet and is administered in the movement of overworked medicine and cautery of other members; because all these works are like fire, and there are other medicines that must be cauterized well like this, with vinegar and honey acacia and chalk with soap, all these things melted together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galiens tells us of a cure from which one man was cured of the pain in his groin and sciatic nerve, and great praise, and says that no other cure is needed, and he became well only once when this cure was performed, and he would bathe as he instructs here afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this manner that you take a green and fresh vertigris, and crush it much with a little bit of fat, and apply it to the groin and the thigh where the pain is located, and bind it; and let it be for three hours, and as much as the patient feels the pain, will cease.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put it in a bath so that the body becomes a little red, and put him in the litter, and the pain will depart all and he will be well.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And instructs that no one should use cauterization of such medicine after evacuation.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyascorides says that when a sciatic vein is cauterized with horsehair, it must be done in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and anoint it with old oil, and place it on the fossa between the big toe and the little toe called the scrotum.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dry horsehair, and anointing it with fire until it becomes charcoal, place it on the linen cloth, and let it sit until it is stained; then repeat this process again, and do not stop doing so until you think that it has reached the spot just above the hunchback, where the pain is gone; and this type of cauterization is called "cautery of horsehair".
de la dolor dou dos	of the painful back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either by falling or by percussion or by too great evacuation, or by the appearance of something spread out cold matter, none of these similarities is worth cautery, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the sick person be void of fetid pills or other similarities, so that upon their back you make three lines signed with an incision, and in each line perform cautery or more according to virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and thus do the cautery as called "poins"; and if you see this, do III cauteries or IV at the clavicle middle incision according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease comes often to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow spine when it is straightened, and fear; and you will find in the lower back on the spine at the base and in its appearance that comes up on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to treat it, if you cauterize with the cautery of the cell according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the cautery is purple on each part of the spine, increasing.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, if you cauterize inside the spine at the puncture point one or two lines deep and so that the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the treatment, keep the patient so that they are healthy as we have said, and guard so that you do not introduce cautery into a swollen gland which is in the grip of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	From the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by swellings in each limb of the body, and when pain comes on foot, which they call "podagre" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured with medicines, if it is cured with cautery in this way: make a poultice of cautery around the joint of the foot, and use olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a spot that you prick on the face of the foot, make a cautery all around the point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come to the groin and other joints, and this happens many times, make cautery on each groin 3 cauteries or 4 of each part, all around the olive oil cautery; and if you have need of more, do more, but do not hold your hand over the heat longer than until the specks of pus are dried.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the genitals and the back, administer the fire cautery that we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, do pain into two fingers; and if there is no more pain in them, then apply pain to each joint and to the skin of the hand; and if the pains come down just on the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and some medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give good governance and purge the phlegm, he will be made healthy by God's aid.
de la routure dou syfac	of the incision into a abscess.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an abscess comes with ulcers and the bowels descend to the joints and it is new, it is advisable when you cure his wounds that he does not make use of them the next day; and he should use things that lighten his belly, so that the fevers come down from his belly. After that, have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to pull his leg until the ulcers are healed, and tie it to your two hands, and sign that there is a sign like the half of a circle above the bone of the finger; then take out the cautery by this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until it is white and has stopped bleeding.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the bowels to their proper place; and let the physicians tie off the veins so they do not return; and work well on the patient, and put some linen and a servant above the knees, and another under the thigh that holds up the hands; then apply the cautery to the marked spot on all fingers, and the right hand and the left hand until you touch the bone, and if you don't hit it the first time, do so again another time until you reach the bone; and be cautious that the bowels will not escape when you perform the cautery; so as not to burn them; and thus let the patients not die from this, or any other sickness.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	Instruct the cautery to be subtle according to your size and that of the great ones as well; after three days' cure let the patient heal from the fire cautery with butter until the scab is shed; after the cure of other ointments until he is healed, and apply heat to the patient for 40 days on his back so that the wound is properly closed; and it is suitable that his nourishment be taken long enough, so that the boil does not burst when he is going to move about in rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to rise, apply a well-made bandage and wear it for 40 other days; and have good rest, so that he works little and avoids excessive drinking and eating, and speaking too loudly; and if you follow this teaching, then he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after your cutting treatment of the cautery.
de la routure dou ventre	of the cut on the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When cuts come in other places and are identified, and you see that they no longer grow, then do the cautery as its quantity demands, and burn off one-third of the wound; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the level of the incision and make a line for the width above the cut, and another below it; and with your finger press around the entire edge of the cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and less severe.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, or from a fall or from injuring it, and the pain lasts for a long time, and medicine cures are useless, then it is necessary to cauterize with the cautery that is called "poins," and do the cauterizations according to the length of the limb, its thickness, and its weakness, and its virtue, and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it heals after the first cauterization, that is well; but if not, do another cauterization on that part, because often this type is such that it must move to the limb next to it, so that you make cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of incompetence
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The problem is treated with no success by cautery for great help, and the same malady that comes from the putrefaction of pus and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You cannot view this cauterizer, take precautions if the malady is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in division, and do not stay or remain, and doubt that corruption seeps into the entire patient, so make V cauteres on the head: i put the head anew, and the other towards the front at the end of the hair; and II over the II horns, and I behind under the hairy part; and hold your hand so long as the cauterizer comes to bone just until the scabs come out so that the vapors of large humors can come out; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Et se li meselerie est partout espare;
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And knows that when you do more cauterization, you will cause more harm, and the patient will suffer; and knows that the patient does not feel pain from cauterization as much as they would if it were not infected.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It is fitting that cauterization should be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in various ways with the iron tools.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment let him be left of flour powder mixed with honey and other remedies until he is made whole.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an inflammation arises in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but does not heal, then you should do cauterization on the member according to its size and shape; and if the cauterization is inserted a little into the flesh of the wound, then treat it with bandages until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes they perform cautery with their hands and feet and back, at the end of the nerve that makes the member mute, and thus if it is removed the swelling; and no one enters into this without knowing the members and the openings of the moving bones of the body.
de albaras	of scars.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "scars" is aged, and medical knowledge does not help anything, then cauterize with cautery a little bit at first, according to the amount of the blood that flows out, until the flesh is removed, and it changes its color; then cure with flour of onions and lentils with olive oil and plantain leaves, and salt of gall and salt of almonds, each one in turn; and mix all together, and tie with a cloth, and let him eat as much as he can until he is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The doctor who pricks with fire
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the chancre comes at the beginning and you stop looking, prick it with fire that seems like a circle all around the turn of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all the wise men say that you should prick fire at the middle of the chancre; and all think it not good, because I fear it will be ulcerous and corrupted, and I have never wanted to try it before, and there is no other remedy than to cut around with the fire called "circule", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have a disease called "adubelati", and it lingers in dying or because of its abundance, or because the old man has aged (it means too much age) and he is weak with little blood, or because of his long illness; and you see him hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauterizations, after that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	She will soon die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you view her pierce with the fire cauterization, so that the cauterized form is like this:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of this disease which is called "adubelati" so that the cauterization has pierced the liver, and it should be such that the patient feels pain on both sides in this manner so that the course of the putrefaction is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure, so that he may be completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the burn cauterization by iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease that is called "corrodens", and it is no other than an injury to a limb, because it causes the limbs to rot as well as dry bones.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this sickness in one who can endure fire cautery together with the fire, then heat the cauterizes small and large according to what is fitting for the patient or the disease; after having cauterized all parts until you erradicate all corruption, and nothing remains of it, that which is corrupted should be cut out.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him lie for three days, and put on his cauterized wounds to suffer from a firebreak with oil until the escharatures of the fire are cut out, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of bone-grown ulcers.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that a healthy child is born, it is good; and if not, then repeat the fire cautery on those who are left with corrupted wounds.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this condition is sometimes cured with medicine water instead of fire cautery; but all see that fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already said the cure of medicine water in its division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of worms that come to the bone
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that on the bone by chance there is born a disease which we call "clos" according to our intention, and it is a great thing to blame that causes the pain.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And there are two kinds of fire cauteries for this disease.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the iron, just like a hair tie, and it is made of good iron to the size that can penetrate the nail from all parts, and it has subtle margins; after that put hot iron on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes out at the root of the nail; then let it be for three days so it starts to get rotten; then make an ointment of fresh marjoram ground with fat, and put the ointment on the whole nail, and the nail will come loose and will be despoiled of its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let his hair grow long and even.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted to frost of the body, and this happens in his hands and feet, so it is fitting that you apply fire cautery with hot water; and thus: take a rod made from iron or oak, or a needle of walnut, and place on the warts; and put the rod on until it pricks all around, then put a little warm water there, and hold your hand tight, and press the skin in turning so that the margin of the rod goes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep down till the root; and let the patient suffer a little from the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as is, and he will drain all out from his roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	In this manner do it after another, until you have searched through all those which are in the body, then treat the limbs that bind with strong bands.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment for the quiver
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people are shivering with cold or fever, or with another ailment, it is fitting to make four cauteries or five above the spine on the back, one cautery between each spine; and one over the belly, and one in the region of the liver; let this stop the trembling, and hasten their recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of dry sores or ulcers
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No time do they appear without the body's internal baths, or dry sores/ulcers, that come from great corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary to make cauterization upon each of these sores, a subtle cautery made from the wood of myrtle, with which the point is grasped by fire, or from the root of aristolochia long, or with a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time are the cauterizations made at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow again forward, but the superfluous things that come from them are broken, and they are healed; but it is necessary to do so after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often happens great bleeding of the artery that is cut at the wound, which comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or by cauterizing a limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stink.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct the patient to wait until this happens when it has occurred to anyone, and then hasten to put your thumb index on the wound of the vein, and strain them very much so that they are not appeased underneath your thumb, and that no more gout is produced; then apply olive oil cautery in small and large sizes until they are all red; then apply heat I, whether great or little according to the wound and where the artery is routed, and put the cautery on that vein which you hold with your thumb, and keep it there until they no longer strain.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the fire has disappeared when you lift your thumb off the vein, and the cautery has cooled down, then take it hastily another cautery which is on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until they no longer strain; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve which is near, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when the blood does not flow from the artery, it cannot be well stopped by oneself when the artery is large, unless it is done by one of the four ways in which we have said: either through cautery, or extraction when it has not been treated, or with a strong tying of thread, or with medicines put on who have power to stop bleeding; and let it happen that they are bound and strained afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will put a stop to the swelling of the tightly bound limb or putting things on it, or other similar things, if they do not profit from this.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to him and he does not have any medicine or remedy, then let him put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well until the swelling subsides from the wound and from the vein; and do not stir him, but let him be moistened with cold water often until he becomes very cold, so that his wounds become congealed and swollen, and then perform these operations in advance of what is needed to cauterize and use medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments of cuts.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we have said in the first chapter, about any disease where it is necessary to cauter with fire or with medicine, and the causes and forms of cauterization; and I have placed that chapter at the foot of this same page, and I will go into this chapter by the same route so that those who find it will be easier to understand.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear boy, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than with the first cautery, and therefore it must be done with greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to enter into folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of men come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	But some come who have been cured so quickly with their disease that they die easily due to the force of their own disease, and the great size of its evil; and for this one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from these cases which you hear my sense, and say "wait, I am cured"; and the sick person is pitiful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not right that you only consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetise; and do not be too weak but rather wisely of what you are certain of and of what you have taken for yourselves; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your sick people so that salvation is converted; and that will help you to acquire a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three dear sons, Our Lord gives you good understanding and truth, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I instruct you on this chapter in devising by chapters, according to what is before or in front of the cautery chapter, which I have devised for you from the head joint to the joints, because you will find it easier to deal with that which you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Fill the full head with water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the child holds it too tightly to the head of the infant; and sometimes it comes from a return that no one knows.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness occur only in children, and at every time that I have seen it, the death has occurred; and therefore I think it is worth making the work more thorough.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	Et I saw the child because the joint was swollen with water, and the head became engorged every day until it could no longer sustain itself; and he believed so much that he was dead, and this swelling is assembled under the bone above his spleen, between the kidney and the bone; and wounds are of such a nature when the swelling is between the kidney and the bone, and abscesses are small, that you cut into the head with a large incision; and be so long as II of us, as much as we have seen, until the swelling runs out.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is deeper, and the abscesses are larger, cut two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the swelling is under the bone, and you see the signs that it affects both sides of the face, and the water spurts out when you press your hand inside, and this does not stop: then it is necessary to cut three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After straining the wounds of drapes and powders, and putting vinegar and oil in, and letting it go for so five days; then clean it, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head drain out, and give the patient dried meat a small amount of moisture until the limb is comforted and cured.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is to look at or open the size of the abscess and its assembly, because sometimes it's in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure then, when the abscess opens or is made open, and the inflammation of the water, and make the cut accordingly as you have the skill; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and give a generous amount of blood, so that the patient may die from the accumulation of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of flesh
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens that there is no disease which is called 'catarrh' in the eyes or on the skin, and the disease is old and medicine does not help, then the following remedy should be used: cut with cauterization as when you cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary that you cover the eyes so that the patient stares at his forehead; then rub him with a rough cloth until the arteries are visible, then stretch out the patient's neck with all the cloth; then look where the vein is rising, and check whether the tendons are in place next to the ears, and if they have come back; then tie the tendons with leather thongs; then cut one and both of them with a good spatumile two parts long until the vein just touches bone, and so that this be done through the wide space of the forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	If you see this, pour out the spatula under the artery and strike on top, in cutting as is necessary to traverse.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it should be closed with a continuous downward flow of fire.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at sight, it is wise to measure out three times the space of two fingers, then mark and cut through the bone; for this is six, six fingers, and by chance a little more or less, according as the patient can bear it and the swelling of the artery; then look at the wound: if the point of the bone remains above the surface, do not cut again in that place, for it will be useless to make another incision, then strain the wound and bind it, and cure with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	The body leaves
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient body comes in and catarrh is present, due to moisture of tears and colds in the temples and old sores that resemble similar things, and he is treated with various medicines and remedies and none of these help him, we must extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize the ulcers, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes his hair grow behind his temples, and listens to the artery which opens up in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is little replied with heat as in very few men who are too cold; and if it is warmed, then he strips off his collar on the patient with some cloths, then rubs him with a rough cloth, and heats him with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then takes the spongy spatula of this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then take it up at the top with pinches, and pull well from both sides that are under each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it to the point of the needle, then cut from that side according to the quantity of the two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not cut, do not separate it without pain throughout everything.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And take out the vein of six fingers, just three; and if the artery is large, it is fitting that you tie it in two levers of a double strong thread of silk, so there will be no hemorrhage before the wound heals, and it will come to pass again from the vein; then cut the superfluous part which is between the two levers at this same hour, and if you see, then cauterize with cautery knife just until the bones are cut; for that is the better work, if the patient has no fever and he is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is aid to finish the moistures: for this it is of greater help as moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries, fill him with fresh wool and put on fine nets; and when you remove them, if he needs medicine dry that makes charcoal, and threads, until he is healed; and if without cutting the artery as often as you work, you will hurry by cautery, or take a wool of vitriol and the strain in your hand that it may not be stained; and if you do not have this present, put on the wool his dressing so that the veins are congealed, and raise the dressing with cold water until they cease, and bind as much as is necessary; for what must be drawn out and is more light in the extraction of the artery is cauterizing the vein of this cautery with two parts trenching, but the trenches should be well-spaced to ward off its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instruments are too dark, he holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And he must have two knives in his hands, one of which is thick and large, and then when you take scissors made from iron the second time, put a hot iron on it until it comes close to the bone, cut the vein in two places; and let them be separated between the two incisions because there's no doubt in this cautery about all of it; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the eyelashes are falling into the veins that are above the forehead of the forceps, and he does not take any benefit from medicine that we make, and you see the patient's face turning red, and feel pain at the eyes as if from a burn; and the oil is cool and moist so that the hair of the eyelashes come out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, if it requires this cure.
