Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	Instruct the old healer to call this person 'cure contused', and you shall make a reenactment on the patient who has this illness by making their hair grow long at the front; then make three equal slits in the forehead, so one of them is like two fingers pressing down on the forehead from below, while the other two are like two fingers pressing above on the paper-like skin, and keep away from cutting the arteries that are located on the paper-like skin; and move your hand away from continuing to press on the two mandibles, and apply three stitches each on every wound through it; then apply a piece of sponge and a lot of drapery for cleaning, and use a good spatumile with two parts equal to this shape.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the first incision in the temple, make the second incision; and scrape all the wound between the two slits as far as the bone above, then apply another piece from the middle incision to the other side of the second incision, and then remove that spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If it is cut in the first wound with the instrument called "cultellary", and is very sharp from one side and the other, soft not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And cuts the costal bone towards the raw flesh at the wound, and the costal bone is soft towards the bone, and it presses hard until it comes to the middle wound.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And immediately cut the vessels that flow from the head towards the ears until the incision is continuous just as far as the opening of the wound; then another part make in the middle wound just as far as the other fault; and then extract the blood equally, press out the vein that has been taken; then put a soft cloth in each wound, and cover it with moist cloths in wine and oil and herbs, and keep away from swelling; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer great quantities of water and vinegar, then the treatment of basilicon ointment with olive oil, and other cures for wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	They must hold their eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When they have a good cough accustomed to it, and you see the eyes darkened and reddened, and weakened vision, and the papillae burned; and the hairs fall out, and pain is felt in the head, and the patient sneezes; then from these accidents you see that those materials and this cough come only from many veins, and how the mother heals it, if there is a vein.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to raise his forehead, then make a great cut along the eyebrows.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision just to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move towards the side; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, then close between the two lips of the wound and put cotton wool and linen thread; then tie over drapery soaked in wine and oil, and beware of an abscess; when it is healed, it is necessary to rub the bone until it starts to come out, then treat with purgatives that make the bowels move.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of cochineal dye, and make it into a paste; and administer it to these wounds for the healing of all skin.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the evacuation of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that comes out of the ears is one of the four things: grains, or meat, or stone from the mine, or similar thing like metal; or seed, such as grasses, beans, fennel, or other things that flow out, like water and dregs, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it comes out of the ear stone or in some other manner of thing that does not adhere to the ear, nor grows in the ear, if you put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, put on a small amount of violet oil or sesame oil, then perform the extraction. And let the stone be thrown back in the ear canal, and apply the cloth to the nostrils when it comes out, and place pieces of cloth or wool into the ear so that it goes above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often times the procedure comes about through this cure; and if it does not happen, then they perform the extraction with fine pins, so that it is in this form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it springs out with the pins, that is good; if not, then perform the extraction with an onion skin and a small double fold; and if it does not spring out by this, then make a pin of thorns and pour the head down into the pin or ear hole very tightly, so that it cannot enter through the pin; then pull out carefully, because often times it springs out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such manner, seize the sprout with a bit of it when you take hold of the ears, and put some cotton around; then press the sprout on the stone or whatever thing, and pull out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not avoid all these things that we have said, so hasten to pierce the ear thus before piercing the bone and causing spasms; and the manner of the incision is such that you first make the patient healthy from the head, and extract the blood according to the measure of his virtue, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat or where it hangs down; and the incision should be like a crescent moon until you come to the bone, then extract the bone with your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and the cure will last as long as he is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that has grown and has swelled up, so administer the extraction; and if it cannot come out, so administer a small spatula in between them according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And instruct the patient to make a cut at that point.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make the cut when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many cuts there; then take out small stitches and at the wound site, as we have said, so that the extraction may be gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water then it is best to vomit into the ear; and that the patient may use early condiments, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And also if it is swollen on the same ear or in the water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it falls through for that reason, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If that's not the case, if you pierce many pieces according to the length of your head, and keep them light and warm, and put one or two pins in your ear, and stand on those feet on another foot, and freeze on another joint on the joint in the ear; and do not cease to do this of joint by joint until the water has all been drained out, and so will it fall out entirely; and if you see, pierce the joint, and put one of the pins back into the ear, and the other joint takes fire as long as that one is ardent; then again make another piece of joints as long as the water drains out, as we have said in the piercing.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the earlobe, if it is of small size, like a wart and similar things, treat it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size, which can be felt, extract the prickly flesh; and this is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When you are cutting out the worms from the ears, in order to cure it as we have said in division and when treating dilations, if the cure does not profit, so that you look at the ear towards the sun: if there is no worm visible, then take sharp needles; and if none are seen, then pierce with a pin of this sort, because this is its form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it may be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And pour the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then strike to form at the whole ear; do this often until all the veins appear.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	But if they do not come out when you apply heat in the ear canal as I have said in the cutting of stones; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations as the ancients have used in the removal of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear canal with this instrument, because here is the shape that you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is of silver or of lead cut off near the small passages, and on top over it to distill; and for pressing in the distillation into the instrument well-made for that, and if you see a razor and blow into the point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicine in the canal; and the ear should be in the ear; then pour into the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or just about to come out of the ear; and it will feel good to the patient inside; and let them not be too cold, because the medicines would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the bursting of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a small hole in the ear; and this same thing happens to adults by bursting of wounds or by burning something inside the ear, and this bursting often occurs within the ear so thoroughly that one cannot see it; and sometimes it has a large hole, and the ear is very swollen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	This one which occurs within the ear so thoroughly that one cannot see it is because of bad humors in many dispositions, and when you look inside, it is necessary to put the patient's ear to the sun; and observe: if you see pus or discharge apparent, then the wound has a certain shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And if it is bloody and trenchant in front and behind the ear, but does not burst the ear; or if the pus or blood is from an ear injury, if you have fine needle points, and carefully prick gently until that blood is entirely dried.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the swelling is in the ear, then take a fine needle lighter and place it on the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the swelling which the sick feel a great pain in the ear, prick lightly, and guard that you do not press the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to its size and shape, and apply ointment Egyptian.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do nothing on any day until the wound is closed, or you take a tent and apply ointment in rosewater, and powder with vitriol broken; and if you see that the ear is swollen, cover it so that you treat the tent and remove another moist tent made of olive oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat as long as he is cured.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the blood comes to flow again, then plunge an sponge and wring it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that can relieve bleeding from the flow which are for treating oozings.
de la char des papieres	from the flesh of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	To the ulcers that come from paper skin when they are moist and dry, if it is fitting to extend them with tongs and tweezers, and cut with a spatula of its roots; then put on it vinegar.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not peel off, if you cauterize the lenticular skin with fine cautery, and cauterize after incising is useless; and many times repair, since nothing stays from its roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are scorched and do not return again.
de la gresle	From the shoe.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	There are times when some things that look like hair in the eyes come to paper, which is called "grandine" disease, because of their shape and hardness; and this is a mixture of moisture great on top and below the paper; the remedies are such: take care if the grandine moves from one side and the other, and it's a light thing to know; do then make a wide cut, then scorch each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and pound.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you can't cover it by piercing the paper at least a little, it will cause no harm to the patient; and if the cut is large, if the assembly has a seam, and treat the cure until it becomes sound; and if it's small, don't do anything with force, because the ointments restore it immediately and annoy the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the hair is falling into the ear, towards the upper part, let the paper turn and look at the dirt; if it reaches to one pinched finger, cut it off and press hard from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, nothing will be disturbed; and when the dirt is cut off, wash away the dirty oil of salted water, and cure the patient until he recovers from this disease.
de la graisse des eulz	From the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	This is a grease that clings to the threads of paper above, and it happens more often in children who have no one to care for them, and causes great suffering to their eyes, and they come with catarrhes in the mornings, and cannot see the light of the sun because their tears obstruct their eyes; and because of this they lie on their faces until death, and sleep on, and their skin is moist below their eyebrows that are infected by the exinach which seeps into the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your hands and feel the swelling inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your healthy one; and then take a linen cloth, and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of swelling in each part, and put it there; and press with your hands from both sides so that the swelling is assembled inside the circle; then make a cut at the midpoint of the swelling, cutting a wide slit, not greater than the wound you made on the vein; and let the skin hang down until you see the swelling; and in other situations, comes the swelling out of the cut, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take out the bandage then to one piece of cloth charpie between your two shoulders at all times and turn your hand to right and left so that it is spread; and be careful not to add anything in the wound, lest you come near the whole spectrum until now, lest you burn it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the extraction is not made in the beginning of the wound, close a little of the wound lightly until it appears; then cut as we have said, then dress with cloth in easy and wet manner, and put on the patient, and tie up with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such men who break the silken thread and place it in order to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to a swollen joint, so that the patient is being treated with emplaster until he is well.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of paper are born on a place other than their nature, and become wrinkled, if they prick at the eyes, and cause various kinds of illnesses such as tearing and swellings of the paper and albugen, until it is the cause of destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in four ways: either by cautery with fire, or according to what is before or in the chapter of cautery medicine, and is done either by incision and suturing or by tying, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your own hand; then turn the paper with oil at your left hand; if it turns over, it is good; if not, prick one needle into all the hairs above. Either cut along the edge of the paper where the hairs grow out from those hairs, and pull the thread upwards to the entire width, from the great tear to the small; then remove the thread, and put a small cloth of linen and a drapery under the paper; then draw on the paper an image of an ash, just like the horn of myrtle, as you see it rise up in size; and it is necessary that the figures be according to the quantity you see the paper increase by.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Et if there is someone who has a special need, on cuts a great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is soft; then you do it all over the spatumile above the two lines that you have signed, and start with a large needle from just below small; and make one of the incisions near the natural hairs in the growth of a root, then pour some oil on one of the two angles of beauty, then scrape everything; then assemble the two lips to a stitch of an awl with all the fine yarns of flax, and wipe out the blood, and do it dry the excess flesh of the filaments above the two sorrows in all sorts of sticky things, if you see this done; or if not, you don't have to care, then leave the stitch and the filaments just for three days or four.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off that which overhangs because of small, even, equal parts according to its shape.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tongs firmly, and that is not even, then prick an arrow or take a thread and tie it to the figure; and then tie another thread around the larger part and the smaller one, and assemble them evenly between your two fingers; then bind your hand evenly, and bind all the skin on which you have marked, just as we said before, then assemble both cheeks of the wound by stitching, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then clean it with cypress and similar ointments soothing; and sometimes happens that the hair of the patient's body are converted: so it is advisable to use what we have said about the incision; but the stitches in one and both are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the chains is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the flesh inside as I have said, and then make two hinges by art, and two subtle strings so long as the paper and the large space of the spatulum are; and cut at two fingers of two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what overhangs from the paper of oil, and strain the two hinges of the two parts together; and let it be in this way for some days, and the skin that was strained will harden and dry and become thick, so that it feels by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late and the cut has some strength, then treat him until he is sane; and when the wound is sewn up and the paper is lifted, and the hair will no longer be pulled; and this is the form of the two hinges that you make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to prick at their hair, which has grown long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold your eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Et if the arrow is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, so treat the arrow below to the length you have ordered, until the arrow comes forth from the part that has been perforated, and you see it through your vision of oil; then so treat the arrow and the thread, and close the eye and let him rest two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the arrow appears above; and if the hairs are small, so accompany one long hair from the neck with natural nature, and raise them with that which you leave, until they are stretched out and then lifted.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's spoilage
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease is called "alearcati" or the spoilage comes to the oil, there are two kinds of it: one natural and one unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden injury or cutting or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of treating the injury is that you cut open the scar, and serve the lips, and put in tenters of linen, and tie so long as it is healing; and it is not advisable to use only in the treatment of things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but to work with softening things, like fenugreek; and boiled rosewater or fat, and seeds of flax are cooked, and ointments made from yolk fondue in any oil, and put a tent over it, and then cure.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you guard yourself not to take it according to the form in which it was before; and all the injuries we have mentioned are only for the purpose of describing this disease, that it may return according to the same form as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is outside, and truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the path of the work in the body is such that if you prick an artery with an awl, because it has one thread double, and the stitch in the fat, and you pierce from the left shoulder side to the right, so the thread veines into two joints of the fat; then pull the char above all at the spot where the awl is, and strike with a span long.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of paper returns according to what is desired, it is good; but if not, then take a razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side within the paper; and so that the joints of the two cuts meet at the angles of the incision you made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as if of a letter with the non "I griesche"; then cut out that char, according to the quantity its sides are below, from what is left of the paper, then join the two parts sewn, and the cost of a thread of linen; then the cure of what we have said of mollifying medicines and poultices, until he is well.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	Et if the sickness comes from cutting or piercing or cautery, so it is fitting that you cut a plain incision below the hairs of the paper; and according to what I have said; then sew between the two fingers of a belt, as I said; and one must do the work according to the shape of the illness, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare an engine of all kinds of poor skill so that it may return the figure to its natural shape; and the sick themselves, according to what they require of work and treatment for many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	and suddenly from the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	As soon as this suture occurs in the hands in a certain manner, where the paper is stuck with oil white and cannot move or do its natural works, so it is fitting then that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and sew from the top, until you copy what is good to the spatumile fine, which should not be too rough nor too thin, so that the patient can suffer neither too much irritation nor burn the oil; and make your incision, with which you scrape that assembly lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural shape; and it is all healed that assembly, and no time ever in the sickly oil salted, and washed with warm water, and vinegar; then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and put the woolen oil on top of it soft, soaked in milk, and for three days use only colic and similar things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the uncleanliness of oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	That the itch of oil is in two manners: it is like a nervousness and seems to be on thick skin, and another that is not nervous but resembles frozen milky white substance; when touched with iron and cooked pan after pricking, it will not come out; and both seem to start towards the great vein, and grow little by little until they cover the whole eye and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of cutting is that the sick man puts his head on a clean cloth, then opens his eyes; and lifts paper with his hand, then cuts the itch as pinpricks of small stitches, and stretches it upwards; then takes an awl, and puts some horsehair, or vetch, or oxhair, in it, and makes a strong thread; and doubles the point of the awl a little, and inserts it into the itch, and pokes through all the awl, and ties the itch to a string and stretches it upwards, and scrapes off at all the hair on the cost of the itch that causes itching and pus on the hair just above the head; then cuts the remaining part in the root of the vein up to the small, subtle spanile, with fine forces, and leaves the natural nature of the vein, if the blood does not come out according to custom; and sometimes it only stretches to a single nodule, and to the thread, as we have said; then scrapes off at all the spanile soft because of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the suture does not touch the raw flesh and breaks it, and that the lancet is not felt; and after the incision, take a little bit of sawdust in oil and put it at the wound, and let it sit on the neck until the next day; then the doctor will take care of what needs to be done so that he may heal.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	But if the finger is not sensitive, and you cannot prick it with the needle, and the nails will not enter, this resemblance of an ingrown nail often happens due to medicine; and when I have explained it in the division, if you see that it covers, then apply oil to the patient, and take the suture lightly, a little bit of good matter according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And take the ingrown nail beneath gently, and if you see that it shrinks at all and the reason comes to press, then distill from your mouth into the oil, a collier made of litargire and red wine-seed, and let the oil sit on the neck until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same operation, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the oil, as with a wound, then take the ointment and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed; then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the skin is marred by great suffering in the oil at night, and if it suppurates in an abscess, and you cut into one part but not entirely, so that no blood comes forth; then distill into the oil a red vinegar, which is made from quicksilver.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh born on the eyelid.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And sometimes flesh does not appear at all on certain people, and they cover the eyelid and restrain it with paper and linen as if to conceal, and it seems like a rose of balsam; and wounds are made so that the patient puts their head under the healthy one, then they cut the eyes, and make whole all that flesh is suitable for such, and support with strength; then cut the first flesh, and go completely cutting at the razor until to the end, and guard that you do not bleed the oil on the work; and as in the incision of the scab we have said, as small forces as one ought to oint, as if it forms after this chapter shows; and when the incision is completed and all flesh cut out, then employ the oil of silk or distill vinegar red and similar medicines corrosives, and put on the oil cotton with linen wool, so that you are sure of an abscess; and if it does not come, and they say without cloth covering them, and you doubt of an abscess, so leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing medicines for abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and do thus put flesh covered in oil by this semblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But everyone should know that you must alleviate the cure for each weak person, and by the natural way and also the accidental one, in the presence of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these operations until you see that this limb is suffering from that operation.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These veins are red and covered on the skin, and they hold back their own work and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The master is therefore to first examine whether the vein is swollen, if so, and there is no other disease of fire than the swelling; then do it in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on a clean cloth, then suspend those veins until one hour according to his wisdom, and cut them at that precise moment into thin strips
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two on one side by degree in the four according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then tie off those veins with subtle forces, and suck out the blood after another, until you see remove the veins' force from the oil; and guard that you do not prick the oil at the tips of the lancets, and do this work in the hour of noon before the sun, being very fervent in your work so that you do not bleed too much; and when you have done this, if you distill oil of rue and red into it to corrupt what remains at the wound.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to tie off all that in that hour, then apply plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are assuaged, and secure yourself against an abscess hot, then resume according to this manner as long as he is healed.
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The artery so-called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and medicine according to what I said before, and it is not cured, there is an infection in it that you cut through above the abscess, where it must die, and take out all the moisture that's in it, until the bones are exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, if it has the shape of that which is; and is called "aspere chief", and must be made from iron at the head where it is found, and pointed like a nail as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put the bone of the corrupted bone on top of it, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand just enough to know that this corruption has dried up; and do this only once, then restore the bone with medicinal extracts.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the head of the shoulder is swollen and painful, and the bowels are swollen, and it remains so for 40 days, and does not heal and is not treated with an incision, then no accidents happen to the patient, he is safe. If this is not the case, if there is no other remedy but to return the fistula to the perforated nose according to this form: and you discover a second time by iron, and by medicines acute, when it heals discover so that you find in iron three angles, and the fistula be attenuated up to the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place the head of the lance on the bone of the shoulder blade, and remove your hand from the wound a little, then turn around to the forest as far as you can penetrate the bone and feel that the patient is coming in with his hand over his nose; and then restore the lance with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the swellings come out and harden, take the material to the nose; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and not at all disturbed, nor alleviated by the head, if it is necessary to bind the patient; then apply salve, then put hot poultices or hawthorn to cause vomiting, then make a poultice of oil mixed with ice and Aloe and frankincense and sarcocolch, and then strain the oil, and apply the ointment on gauze and drapery; and the way of the drapery is that you take soft gauze, double each one in four, and then put one over the other according to the quantity that the eyes have need; then strain by a strong thread from above, and reapply the poultices to cause vomiting again; then remove the poultices and leave the oil strained every day and night, and if it binds the patient, do so; but if you see the oil healing, it is good; but if not, then reapply the ointment and the gauze and the poultice until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Drop of fallen hair
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a thread of hair breaks in the web, then comes out, and comes forth from the paper as if it were a grain of resin, and it is frightening to see; therefore, if you cover your eyes, the wound is like such that you poke an needle into the root of the part below just beneath this above, then poke another needle where there is double thread from the side of the larynx; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle as it is according to the arrangement; then take out the leaden thread and tie a part of the web together, and tie it well, then pull out the needle and put on oil linseed moistened with a great quantity of water; and let it be so long that the threads bind with the web, and cure the oil for things comforting until the wound is healed; and at no time will the wound be held by the web each one part of a circular piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, then he should prick in the spot below at the root of the hair, and clean away the moisture, and descend the eyes, and enter so soon; then extract as soon as it is safe.
de la bowe de l’oil	of oil from the bowel.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness called 'alcunnati' is nothing but the oil-filled bowel assembled like a liquid descending, and not actual water; and in its appearance as follows, you should sit your patient on that prepared seat straight, then take the head between your hands of two parts, and let it move until you see the bowel coming to the top at your eyes; then push inside, do not descend, but hold together the lightness, and see how the patient is going as usual; and if it does not descend downwards, know that it's not water, and if the bowels are assembled in such a manner as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take the small spatumile and make above the eyebrow by continuing the conjunctive with the eye skin and the crown; until it bleeds and when it is out, distill in hot oil mixed with warm honey or fenugreek, or boil them and then be cured of another cure till she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the likenesses of water in cutting, and that which is needed to pierce; if in operation according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands crossed, over the fire by the sun, and tie tight the good oil; then put on your left hand the paper of oil to your left eye if they are to the left, or to your right hand if they are to the right; then take in your right hand if they are to the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if they are to the right. Then put the point of the instrument near the crown by the size of a finger in that blistering part of the oil at the lower corner near the bone; then push the instrument which is called "almagda" nicely, and turn your hand until it pierces into the blistered part of the oil, and feel when almagda comes to the empty place; and it is necessary that the measure of almagda be exactly the full length of the measure of the space from the pit of the nose to the end of the nostril; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the eye skin, then put the instrument just next to it or where the oil is, then express it on one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If they are now bleeding, so he sees the patient before him and the instrument on his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the bleeding starts again on the second vein, put the force with the instrument, and when it is stuck in there and does not rise, gently remove all that's left of flesh by turning his hand slightly around; then put back a little blood into the wound, and clean out its oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put the oil-stained cloth or a moist linen in olive oil and plenty of wine, and bind with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	So, and for those of our time, let us put on a common broth with plenty of wine.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the arm cannot enter into the oil because of its hardness, for it has many people who have very hard eyes, so it is necessary that you take hold of the instrument which is called "alberit", for this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then cut the conjunctive alone, and do not go too deeply into it, but make the new one subtle, then pour in oil, as we have said; and on the completion of the work, bring to the patient the doctor who is coming along with him, since he lies on his back in the dark room; and you should be careful of all movements, and give him light food, and do not move his head or right arm or left arm, and you should bind him according to his disposition, every third day; then release him in that same dark house, and examine his eye, and let him see some things, and then he is released for the seventh day; and it is not fitting to make this in the room of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary to lighten it, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	In case of an abscessed limb comes, that you remove the pus on the seventh day, and take heed of the remedy for the abscess; and when it is soothed, then remove the eye and put on its face a poultice to cover each day, and be returned to that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then come the people from that place, and it will transpire in its cases; and know that no disciples should interfere with this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Irah, who said that in some other land they performed the operation of making an almagda incision, because it would cause the water to flow, but I never saw anyone from our land or knew about it in ancient books; and by chance, perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of alchemy, because those who do not know them will see them; and they are made from pure tin:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of this same subtlety, and the behind in three angles of inflammation.
de la char sor le neis	of the blackness on the skin.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are no times when chills occur in different ways, because there are some that resemble scorpions to the point of being pressed; and if they have such or their chill is covered with a foreign color, and their cold is like the color of bone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore in those chills that are cold and not covered, it is necessary to seat the patient between your hands against the sun; open their nostrils, and let their chest rest on these chills, and try to calm them; for until you can sustain yourself with the subtle powder of a certain part, as long as you know that this chill is entirely gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is any remaining thing that cannot be covered, if you will put all sorts of subtle and light substances inside it, so that it does not stay; and if it does not swell without being incised, or has an abscess on the feet, if you cut it as it seems to you; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize them until they are stained and become all bones, then purify either with vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If there is no poultice and moistors come just to the face, know that he is cured; and if moistors pierce as it seems fitting, know that there is a bone exposed in the marrow of the above, because the substances do not come for cutting: therefore it is necessary to put a thread of linen one small size, and made from our hands, and with some space in between; and place the patient's fingers on the thread in his nails so weak, and rub in odorant until it comes out by the thread into the mouth; and this is often done to children in schools, and it is a light thing for one who wants to do it. Then hold the head that comes from the thread with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other as we are with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Instruct the patient to do this as long as you know that no one has corrupted the flesh of the child then take the son, suck the wound, and anoint the head in Egyptian oil, and put it directly on the bone so as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put a poultice of some kind for several days until it is healed, and if he has need of dried medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, because one distills oils and medicines into the poultice:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or lead, resembling a lampshade, as like a poultice, and conduct it thus; and if you see it, do a poultice closed, and let the instruments be plain for purging the head; and have a piece of cloth on the head to hold it while one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the sword near the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Sometimes the head of the neck develops a disease called "telul" and it grows and becomes great abscesses, visible to the sight; and because of this one must take care to apply a poultice at the beginning, with hot medicine or cautery; and if it is delayed for too long and it becomes large, one should be careful and treat it with wax color, powdered powder: but do not touch it with iron because that is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut it once it brings great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is soft touch, not of wax color, and you see what can be covered, then open the patient's mouth and apply the poultice with fear, and treat the abscess as dry things and restraint.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are struck and crushed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	So that when some continuation of solution comes to one of these overgrown cartilages, it is not enjoyed at all, whether in any person.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
