It is therefore necessary to look at this thing in order to see if the wound is fresh with all its sanguis; and then add two lips together with a seam, then treat him until he recovers; and if the lips are devoured on one side and another, it is necessary that you burn all the parts of his flesh so that they heal, then assemble the two lips together with a seam, tie it up, and powder on powdered dragon blood, and incense broken; and put on the powders a piece of melted emplastrum of strong or other emplastrum bonding, and leave him to take effect until he takes his strength back, then treat him with ointment until he is recovered.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing on the belly; or with thread, as I told you.
des apostemes des levres	of swellings of the lips.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With the help of the hands, there is often a swelling in the lips, like grains of sand, small and larger ones. So it must be that you turn back the lips, and split each one apart, and take out with pincers, and cut into each part; then apply the new to the incision with vitriol broken, until the wound is stained; and then clean the area, and cure the area of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
des sordens	From the sound
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Never are the molars assembled in their place at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, with rough and painful surfaces; and never do black and yellow teeth and roots occur until corruption comes to the gum, and they become smelly. So it is fitting that you have the patient sit between your hands, and his molars be in your sight, so that you can remove them when the cracks appear, unless anything remains. And then apply a mixture of balsam and verdigris, and yellowing and other colors, until they are smooth; and if it is determined to be at the first cause, it is good; but if not, make another attempt on the second day and the third day, until you have removed all of them. Note that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, because the razors which remove teeth have other forms than those which remove between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as you can before taking it out, because this should not be done to me; for it is a very high substance and therefore we have no excuse to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is forced to take it out, if you want to be certain of the tooth's vitality.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the patient makes them think it's a rotten tooth, and takes out the good tooth; and one should not take away the pain at all, in case it is the bad tooth, for we have already tried that with other doctors; and when you are certain about the vitality of the tooth, it is necessary to scratch around the tooth with a sharp instrument, very strongly to protect the gums from all sides; then extract the tooth with your two hands or pincers finely at first, until they are well cleaned, and afterwards firmly fasten them; and put the patient's teeth between your own shoulders, so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth from the cheek directly, and if it doesn't fly out, take any of these instruments and put them inside each side lightly, and move them as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is impacted and must be pulled, it is advisable to fill the socket with cloth in that place where the wound is; and if you tie it subtlety with forceps, so that it does not break while being pulled; and it is wise to apply great care over the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient when the root becomes infected, causing greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not make the same mistakes as the ignorant physicians, who by their haste and boldness break the cartilage every time, and do not bring us any of those things we have said; but sometimes they come through the cause of great illness due to the roots that remain, or by breaking the cartilage, just as we have often wanted; and when the tooth is loose, wash it with vinegar or ale and wine; and if blood comes, then employ the liver of vitriol, because it has happened that way, and if this does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the ulcers are such that, when one swallows saliva first, they are long and pointed with large roots, which do not double back when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are long roots if they do not bend when pulled, and are thick limbs well made, and have teeth to hold them in place.
de la racine des dens	of the tooth root
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root is held in place by pulling, it is to be put on with a wet cotton cloth soaked in butter every day or twice.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	so long as the limb is moist, then put in the tongs called "algefri", because the joint seems like a tooth; and they are made just like a file, which is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out from all these ties, so it is fitting that you uncover the whole chariot around the root, and put the instrument which is called "althal", namely palm, in order to make this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it breaks and is large whether or not it does not break, and the root jumps because of this, that is good; but if so, then help with all the instruments, for surely the forms will come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it is helped by this instrument which has two veins, then surely the form will be:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the region of the teeth, and from this instrument which seems like great pincers, whose form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Instruct the surgeon to use this instrument with extreme care so it does not break; and know that many instruments of bone are; and also other instruments which should be known but are not told; for the wise masters subtle will find their own instrument according to what works on those patients, because there is a diversity among such cases, and if they do not work when they hit bone or another part, in order not to break, so that you know the instruments needed, which I have told you, and help with gestures, for this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Let them be large and well-held to hold the bone tightly without breaking, but so that it can be held and extracted; and then restore the patient with medicines suitable for him, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, if the physician has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear and do not fit according to their natural body form, and their shape is ugly, and especially in young girls, it is necessary that you know whether the teeth are new after the tooth, and are not in the right place, and one cannot put them in or fix them: then the extraction; and if they are attached with the tooth, so take this instrument of the kind shown here, which resembles a small beak, and made of good iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut the gum with a small instrument daily because of the hardness of the tooth, and in order not to move the other teeth, if it appears that you can put it in, take some kind of glue as shown here.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also as the glue for which one makes needles; and cut the gum with a small instrument daily lightly, so that it does not move until it chisels; then smooth out the surface at the end of all rasping, if the teeth are too sharp and they bleed on the tongue, you must file them until they are even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are loose, or by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press down on this that he chews less than before, and you cure them with medicines restraining, these do not work; if they must be restrained with a thread of gold, for silver threads become green and rot, but gold does not move at all; and whether the threads are too thin or too thick, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are loose, take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the pins between my teeth, as many as there are or more, until you find the healthy tooth on the other side with certainty; then continue covering just where you started, and gently pull your hand so that it does not move at all; and be careful to bind loosely next to the root of the tooth if he cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to cut the nails with a pair of tongs, and assemble them, and put them between sound teeth, so that they do not bite the tongue; and then let them be tight until they can endure no longer, and if they break, or the filaments come out, secure it with another filament; and leave him thus bound for as long as he can endure, and this is the form of the nails and the figure of the adjustment of two sound teeth and two crooked ones, so that you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, fresh as new, just like we said; and do not put anyone who is not skilled and knowledgeable into this work; and never have a fake tooth made from an animal's bone, and put one in the socket where the defect is, and bind it tight as we have said, and leave him bound for such a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is there a ligament that comes from beneath the tongue or is of nature, unless it is so; or by accident of a wound that heals; and the injuries are such that you must open the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your own, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve tendon on the large side, until the tongue is loosened from its place, and if there's any hardness or scar tissue, and it's a sudden wound, then inject an onion juice and cut the large tendon; and make sure the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is beneath; and when you have done this, lift the head on hot rose water and air, or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue. Every night, each patient will be able to heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If the wound from the fire comes, apply vinegar on the skin; and if it does not come to life, cauterize with cautery, which is good for this; then treat with another remedy until it is sane.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see pus of color, whether red or black or hardened, since the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, because it is a chancre; and if it inclines to blisters and there is moisture, then scrape the ulcer, and make an opening from one side and the other; and if it does not come to life on its own, apply vinegar until it is stained, then return to its original state until you treat with all force; then lift the limb gently and carefully, and treat with other remedies until it is sane.
des apostemes de la gorge	Evacuation of abscesses from the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There is no occasion of the throat having boils which are called "godath", and when we call them by name properly, and as we have said in division, they do not become healthy if you watch out: if it's abscesses that last for a little sense and a little flesh color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, just as for the evacuation of blood; but let it stay until it dies, and then you will separate it, or it will break apart on its own; and if it is white in color again, and the root is subtle, have prepared a tool to cover it, but first examine whether the abscesses are closed and quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his joints be healthy, and he open his mouth and let the servant press the sergent between his hands, and push the tongue downward towards the instrument, for this is the form; and it shall be made of silver or of fine gold just like our scales.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue to all of this instrument, and you see the abscess, if take the needle and prick in the walnut, and pull it up above what you can; and take no other thing from the linen with, then cut to the instrument, for this is the form that seems like force; and look at the chief, which are curved, one side on top of the other, and they are very good, and it is made of iron or silver.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument before it, then take a pair of tongs, because this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And so cut in one part, and the other part too; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot and cold water, and hot and mild water as well, and if blood is coming out, then gargarize the patient with warm or scalded pomace of green apples, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; and when cured, wait for a while; but sometimes new abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them accordingly as they are bound together.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, which is to say the small joint; and I had well closed up the entire throat so that she could not breathe through the obstructed passage, and nor could she eat or drink, and she died if she stayed like that for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses are raised so high that they have been forced to break two times by two wounds on the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	So I stuck to it and made a cut on one side, then the fire was applied, and a large portion of bow (probably a thread or cord) was used. Then another cut was made in the other neck wound, and the swelling was pressed against the tongue; afterwards a stitch was put into these abscesses, and part of it was cut out, and only a little blood came out. And so I closed the conduit to the throat for the woman, and now she began to drink cool water and wine, and did not stop cutting at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept recurring, and filled the vein again as much as it had been emptied, until it became very big; then I removed it and cauterized inside the throat: thus it remained stationary for some time; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the vein descends to the eye and it is swollen and prolonged, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is too large and rounded, then it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut in the same way as we have said in division, and the cure does not benefit from it, and you see that the arrow marks are smoothed out, and it is subtle, then it is advisable to copy; and the one that is rounded and not prolonged; and if it is sanguine or of a foul color or black, then you should bleed from the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner in which I have said, of its size and shape, you should sit the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument with which we made note previously; then prick into the eye, and pull it away, and cut twice at the two almond marks.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to cover no more than the natural surplus, for if you cover more, it grieves your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the cutting of the two almonds, and heal until she is cured.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, it is advisable to use a fire engine at the cauterying of the painful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is wet water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts his head on the healthy one, and then presses the tongue with the instrument we have said in the cautery chapter, and mixes with hot water shoe leather, if it is not too thick or too clear; and with this edge of the instrument, there is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to put a hair from his head or an object of metal in the mouth, so that the ointment of the cautery falls onto it and stays there; for if they are not attached to their chest, the saliva and mucus run into his mouth from the medicine, which does not descend to the throat, nor does it pass through the bile; then take hold of all the medicine and press upon the wound, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it dry and the stinging of the medicine is calmed; and if you see that, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into the can with the cotton on top, until the cotton sticks to the wound; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry, and cast it after four days or five; if you have need to reapply the cautery of the medicine, so reapply it, and after applying the cautery clean it around the wound with cotton soaked in butter, and purify what is around the medicine.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery. If it is cured with smoke according to this method, take calamondin and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put them all together in an I pot, and then mix them, and make a boil; and let the pots be well glazed with hot earth, and add to each pot a small instrument according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it can be of silver or lead, and one of the pins stuck into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises up to the eye through the nose, until the eye is numbed; after that, repeat it frequently, until the eye dries out, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the eruption of an abscess, because many things happen; and do not do this except when the abscess is running down.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If the instrument is not present, take a candle and insert a needle of fire into the head, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the needle of fire will not weigh down the vapor much, and it is a good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Sometimes it happens at the throat with or without a splinter of fishbone, or any other thing; therefore you should treat what you see, and press the tongue against the sun for the entire length of the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and when whatever is in there does not show up and returns to the throat, it is good to make the patient vomit so that the meat may be cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing burns from vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread, or a root of lettuce, or a slice of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then cut it; and when it comes out, it will burn, and then cut it again; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take an instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Instruct the straitjacketed so as to let it enter more easily into the throat if possible, and lift the head higher up in order that it may be easier to go down; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest its life comes or else you burst the bone within; and make sure that the patient does not push against the instrument, because he sees it is rusty; if it bursts, then push all of the way with the same instrument until it is finished.
de la sansue de la gorge	about the cutting of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for cutting the throat, as I have said in division, by the treatment of medicines; and when it does not profit at all, then look into the patient's neck in the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the wound, so the arrow has come out at its small end, or you have fine tongs that are worth it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If this is not worth it, take a caustic horsehair, and put the bottle in the throat of the sick person, then pour or touch the caustic horsehair to the warm metal, and do it often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the sick person suffers from water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full goblet of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in such that it is swallowed from ear to ear, and move it with one's hand often; and as soon as the wound feels the water, let it be vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she does not vomit as we have said, then perfume the sick person with asafoetida, at the instrument which I spoke of in the fumigation of the ear; do this many times, for she will vomit like a pig.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, and the method of fumigation is that you take a container or it has charcoal holes, and the cover is covered with a sieve pierced in the middle, and in that hole are the keys of the instrument; then you put your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth so that the smoke does not enter, but comes just there; and now the cough will start, and if it does not come, you repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient suffers from thirst, and eats foul and bad things, and does not drink any water; and therefore they are cured by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument by which you treat the abscess is that when it can be seen, resembles a pair of curved tongs to enter into the throat; and has a resemblance to the mouth of an eagle, and has roughness like lime, so that what it takes in cannot release it; and thus is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The physicians who treat abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, just as is remembered in this book from both before and after, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two kinds, one being similar to the other, and it is due to moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is for when they are inside or in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscesses in the head are different from those on the lower jaw, and the abscesses of the shoulder bone are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if you do not cut at abscesses until the bowel is dead according to its completion; and if of such as it is necessary to cut them while they are believed to be dying, and do not die according to their completion, just like those that occur near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from the joints, and one leaves it there until it is full of pus, by chance if it infects the ligament and nerve of the joint, because that is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is at the main limb and if you wait until it dies before making a perforation, it will harm the principal member; or if it's at the foundation, if you pierce there also, then it will kill. It is not advisable to pierce an abscess when one believes that digestion has been completed, for fires that are near the foundation will burst forth and cause pus to accumulate inside, and create a fistula, and it cannot be healed in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the site of the perforation of the abscess which will lead to death according to completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the separation from fever, and the reduction in pain and redness, and the gentle movement and the sharpening of the chief of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation at a location more dependent on the abscess, where it opens, and not too high on the body, because if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or joints, nerves, or arteries, or all those locations that are equal to them and have no pressure.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those joints that are swollen, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And if there is an abscess in the jawbone, so that it will be left open until it has been fully digested and confirmed, just as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	Because if you pierce into it, the body will swell with the blood from it, and it is full of much filth; and by chance, the lips and the fundament become hard.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that must be pierced according to the size of the body, according to how much it needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	It is necessary that you bring forth small abscesses, small punctures; and large abscesses, large punctures; and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is wise to sew the wound, when it has become as thin as a cloth, so that it may be softened, then it is done in the same way as one makes for the nose: and if there are such as are split into three angles, and those whose punctures are made like the horn of myrtle, like abscesses from arrows; and if there are others with which you make a circular cut, and other shapes and sizes, and seeming cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, as an abscess is soft and superficial, it is necessary to pierce them plainly; and if the abscess is large, and has collected much pus, and you pierce, so that you don't take out all of it in this hour, but only part of it; then stop the abscess just next to where it was the day before, then do not touch anything around it; do this repeatedly from one place to another, until the pus is all gone; meanwhile if the patient has weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an old man decrepit with age.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But you must hope for the worst-case scenario at all times with the outcome of the pus, so that by chance the patient may die, and you will not be disappointed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct then this chapter with great care, and when you have pierced your abscess, if it has opened the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a smooth incision, try tending it with linen or wool; and if there are great abscesses, and much pus, it is fitting that you put one tendril in each so they come into contact with each other; and if you have pierced an abscess of the skin part with leather, and sewed it inside, it is fitting that you fill it with old wool or gauze soaked in moisture, and tie it to the flesh on the third day; then the bone, and the bandage of ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you find blood has come out to your work, then tend it with cool and easy water and salt, and cover it with the same cloth again many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to persevere with bleeding if it persists, observe his government and treatment, and apply the powders I have described in this book into your hands. If it is now winter time, and the poultices are applied to the wounds or abscesses and are very hot, then cover them with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it's summer time, and the poultices are hot, soak wet cloths in water and oil, or wine and oil heated, once a day, as we have said; and after removing the poultice and cleaning it, treat him, as is fitting, until he is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is the case where one must carefully examine the treatment of abscesses: for we have said how to apply before treating an abscess, and that is in the chapter.
des soros	he heals with fire command to the sick person that he lets the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the pus of head wounds come out small abscesses, and there are those things similar to cloth, as is the wick of a cat's skin, and there are many such appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fats and swellings such as pus, and similar as wet like skin; and there are swells that are hard and stony to cut, and none have doubt when the arteries do not give any bad consequences.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the arrow wounds of the shoulder are such that if you examine all the instruments called "entromissoire", because the form comes after this, what kind it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they will cut from above the long bone.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried out, they will scrape away skin without leaving any area, because it returns to swelling if left untouched; then they submerge cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise in water and wool, and applying the wound, and letting it rest until the next day; those who are left for the night will be cured.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the cotton is reapplied, as before, on the second day, and the dressing, until you know well that it does not stay at night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for it, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses are swollen without any fat, they will cut according to this form on the long bone; and I wipe away all your ointments, and scrape from every part, and put all my care for traction to treat the wound where it is; and if the arteries make a counteraction, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do thus with an abscess if it is hollow, and when cutting and when curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And he cuts on the abscess if it is hollow and moist, for if it is lighter, because there is less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are some of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and such as I copied or head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a stone hard, rough and white, which cannot be broken; and if any one has tried to pierce it with iron, we have also done just as well a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come or heads, whatever those which arrive on the head of children and roots of the ears, he opens so much as it is to be done for a long time until it comes out from the bowels; and cures as is needed.
des scrophules	Described by scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	This happens often to abscesses on the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they occur elsewhere or in the body, and are very foul, and often join one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located in its own chest cavity, just as the abscess and swelling of the head, as we have said; and the symptoms of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one, therefore, where you see a good disposition in the armpit, and it is like the color of the body, and mute from every part, and not sour as the milk of the neck or at the artery or in the conduit, and not deep; then it is fitting to copy it over, and to scrape off each part, and they will be the two lips of redness, if you have need, just as we said about abscesses on the head; and take care little by little, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and do not use too much force or cutting with sharp tools, lest your hand gets wasted, and you see too far ahead, so that you do not copy more than what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you prick the vein or artery, and this does not stop bleeding, apply vitriol to the wound or any powder that remains in the blood, and bind the wound; and leave it until the swelling is reduced, and the pain subsides, and begin to clean.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is not infected, it will return to its original state, until you complete it; then seek your doctor's advice if there are no small swellings forming, and cut them off and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If there is a large vein at the root of the swelling, it is not recommended to cut off that swelling in its root, but tie with a strong double thread and let it fall down without causing harm; then apply the wound dressing made from Egyptian linen cloth, and then treat the patient.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you hit the entire scrofula, it is fitting that you assemble both lips of the wound and sew now, because there will be no remaining fluid from the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is fitting that you listen to cover the root of it, and treat with force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have fluid, let us pierce in or where it opens; and pierce as we said before, depending on the situation, then apply ointment and similar things, if they infect what remains of the infection; and when the wound is well cleansed, so that the treatment of ointments will be effective until the patient is healed.
de squinance	of squanderment
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient people spoke and said about cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land do it, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have fallen into a coma, it is necessary to prevent the opening of the throat that is called "epiglote"; and do not give aid to this because all the veins and the membranes of the patient are at those who have a cut in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the membranes, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary when we want to cut the epiglottis that we cut it below three circles or four, with a small cutting across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cutting through the syphac, not on the cartilage; and thus, if done carefully, it is convenient to section the epiglottis without breaking, and the vessels are long in remaining.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Instruct the masters that if they are afraid, then it is fitting to stretch the skin of the throat all around the neck; and make a cut at the jugular vein until it comes out; and remove the swellings of blood, if you see anything; and then strike the sinus, as we have said; and demonstrate by cutting the section of the jugular vein that has come out from the broken limb, and by the failure of the voice; and let the wound be left open one piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed by which one doubts strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound at the jugular vein, and remove all the skin to the cartilage; then administer medicines that make a fetus grow until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this (cutting) until the throat is completely stuffed, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect in the liver.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Instruct the patient to tie on the throat so that the patient cannot inhale, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and because the ancients command you to leave the wound uncovered until the malady has passed, and it passes away after three days or four days, then they commanded you to sew the wound and cure, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young woman who took out a knife, and she stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of her neck; and I was called to cure her, and I found her also dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had been drawn from it, and I saw well that she had not injured herself nor cut her vein only to the throat, but that the vein came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I have failed to translate the text.
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This is called a hernia of the throat, and it is a large lump in the color of ebony, and it occurs mostly in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; for a natural one has no appendix.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is twofold: because one resembles fatty flesh, and the other resembles a lump coming from an artery; there is fear of it, and it should not be treated with hot fire unless for those who are small, and he probes and searches inside the passage: if you find it similar to fatty flesh, and have no suspicion, then strike as we do when cutting meat, and take out all its covering, if any, and thoroughly search, and cure as is necessary, until it becomes perfectly sane.
des nous	from ourselves
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many of us to describe, all their similarities; and it is necessary that I say all the differences between a new birth and an old wound.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is when and fever remains, until the ebullitions are passed, and it has been completed as to putrefaction; then rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a new wound, there is no heat, nor fever, nor pain, and it contains the pus, which are its own sacs, according to the color of the body, and begin just like a jelly, and become large; and are so similar, or in size, or moist, and much of color, as I have said in division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of this thing, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form or chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about the abscesses is that you take or more moist than what you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you see that the instrument has pierced the core, then as long as it follows the size of the abscess; then pull out the entromissoire, and be careful not to cut.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moist corran cuts through whatever color it has, if you cut as I have said of other abscesses; and if after that the instrument does not come with moist, then see if it is fatty, if so then make a cross and take it out with pincers, and lightly scrape off each part, and keep warm where you find it in order to treat the wound with the nose; and if you cannot treat it well, cut it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays there, it will return again and again; and if it stays a little while without troubling you, apply the wound to some corrosive powders, hold the wound tight, put on soothing things like abscesses cold, and treat other treatments until he is cured; and if the wound is great, cut off both ears of the wound, and treat the one who hurts.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is inflamed against this or another thing if you hasten and apply the new vinegar cut, let it remain for two days or three, until the wound has passed, and rests the boiling of the blood; then returns to cover that which is remaining nowhere.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Now here are the forms of the interstitial struma, and they come in three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb"; and there are three kinds too: great, medium, and small, to encircle the fistula abscesses; and they are also like the needles with which we sew the sutures, and made of citrine, iron, or silver, and are yellow in color, and are more effective for puncturing black abscesses; and there are three kinds too: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of ulcers are of many kinds, just as you see here: large, medium, and small; and some have two heads in three different ways; and some have three heads and are so divided into three ways; and some have two heads, and only one head, and are so divided into three ways; all this is necessary for their treatment.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these cuts is made sharp, and of such kinds that some are cut only from one side, where the flesh is scorched, so that the vein and nerve are not cut; and these incised ones have the amputated limbs returned to the hand, in such a way that the patient does not lose them at the opening of the abscesses; they come in three kinds: large, small, and medium, just as you see; and do not use them more frequently than in the chariot joints, namely, legs, arms, nipples, and elbows, and similar limbs; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling a strip of scar tissue, according to this shape, with which they stain blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it on no occasion at the place which is healthy to have veins cut, and arteries, and never return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never do the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them must treat according to this form along this line from a to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scorch the fat, and apply the wound with medicine mixed with charcoal, then assemble the two lips of the wound to the seam, and treat until it is healed; and if the nipple turns towards downwards and becomes inflamed for its size, as in women, if you make two stitches over it, so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, because the greater line contains the smaller according to this form along these lines from a to g; then scorch the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powder, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision has not been fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the corruption of blood, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton cloth in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it produces the remaining and the fat, then cure until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	The evacuation of blood from an abscess
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofulas or it has scars, and if there is moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the whole bow of the abscess is empty, apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment suitable for that until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofulas, treat them as we have said in incising scrofulas, and if the wound is about a vein, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the artery removal
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin is sutured above it, if there are many abscesses, and the vein flies out with an abscess; and when you notice this in your fingers, you feel a strangulation; and when it's for the vein, it appears red and swollen; and it's folly to cover up this abscess, and itself when it is below the joints and sinews and at the neck and filled with many other things, and it's very great.
