Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to open the iron wound, and he who has a head wound should do so as well, and in one who has an inflamed artery make a cut above the skin for as long as it is possible; then sew around the waist with stitches, and carefully draw out the artery from under the skin; next insert an awl into the vein, and pierce to the other side, and tie the artery with two threads of linen, just like I have taught you in extracting two arteries at the temples; next keep the patient tied by a strap until he stops bleeding; then treat him with bowels that come up, as long as his stitches are dry; and if the abscess is large enough for the vein, it is necessary to tie one part of two fingers around the thread; and if you doubt whether the threads will not slip out, insert another awl under all the skin around the wound, and tie the threads in four linen strings; then cut off the superfluous part until there is nothing more to cut, then cut the superfluent part with a needle and leave what remains tied; next put on a moist cloth soaked in vinegar and oil, and keep him treated with poultices and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	In the wounds of those who have suffered from this cautery there are often evacuations of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	So too do abscesses come in the artery and vein, and abscesses appear at the wounds when they are fresh, or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows or at joints where there are bones, because it's an abscess, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and is accompanied by many deaths; and when it is strained, he feels pain, and isn't easy to cover with armor, but worse under the skin, and falls ill from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor above or below, and one who has joints cannot be covered with iron: perhaps they will come from contraction; and those who are on the head or forehead, make a blister at the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have tongs, and cut it at its root; and if it is large, if you wait for the swelling, and scorch it, then take out the bone, and assemble the wound to the back, and let the cure continue until he is well.
des grosses boces pendans	of great mouths hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	never happens in the belly and not anywhere else, it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to onions, and has subtle roots and large knots; and there are small and great ones; I saw one man who had 2 bellies that were similar to fungi in shape, but there was no difference, they were white, and had thin roots, and had been split open, and it rots with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I let them cut and found them weighing 18 ounces in one of them, and in the other six ounces, and the wounds from the incision are such that you look to see if the patients are moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist with a subtle root; so they cut with a large spatula, and they do cautery on fire in front of us.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	But when cutting comes often too large bleedings of blood, and they do not warn you, so hurry then to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision with iron, take a good strong thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and let it remain for two days; and then reset it, and do not cease to tighten the thread until the artery is cut, and feel by its sensation; and if the roots are thick, there will be fear to cauterize itself on the belly, but you can well cover half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cauterize the tendon which is of a red color and full of pain and red marks.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an enchantment or spell, and I came to this cure for the chancre after.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or a cut on the scab, and is located in the abdomen and there are other boils, as it happens in other cases, such as when veins burst open or arteries rupture according to what is before them, or because of venosity; and if this is due to the cut of the scab and its discharge, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and is a light thing with pain, and opens up through various openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it comes from the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press on both sides, it returns, and then goes away, and by chance it becomes scarred, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and for strong work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	Et se c'est por moistor, c'est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is fitting to leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	But because of doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter about abscesses, for arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is of an intestine or spleen, then instruct the patient to tie his girdle tight, and lie down straight, then tie himself tightly around a bundle; then command him to rest between your hands, then go towards the place you have marked off with chalk; then open half of the abscess on top of a large needle; then bind it around with a strong thread or a cord made of thick silk firmly, and make sure the ligature is secure; then uncover half of the abscess above the ligature, and pour your medicinal liquid into it; if you find the intestine caught in the ligature, release it, and pour the intestine away from the belly; and if you find the spleen, cut off the superfluous part; and if the artery or vein is against him, then go calmly, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert them into what you have made pierced; then strain the abscess in four lews above the needles; and if you see, loosen the needles, and leave the patient until he perishes, and cut off the dead flesh by himself; or cut it when it has passed through subtlety and died, then treat the abscess as we have said; and extract the wound or moisture that you find, then cure the patient as it is required, and heal the wound.
dou chancre	A skin sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in division the similarities of a sore, and how to treat it with medicines, and how not to use iron treatment; and we say that a sore spreads to the marrow, and great care must be taken in its cure, and the ancients said that when sores are on the skin or can be scraped off like a sore on the nipple, and in the groin, and similar places, and one must remove all of it at the beginning; but when they become large and old, you should not approach them, for I have never seen anyone cured of this, nor has any person ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the wounded person, when it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make him healthy if he has shown manifest overfeeding; then fit the patient well to make the wound; then apply your poultices or sores, and the head from all parts, and leave nothing behind in all parts; and let the blood flow out completely, and expect the patient to be sound at your hands or with anything; but if they bleed again at the incision of the artery or vein, you must cauterize until the wound is stained.
de ydropisie	Fever of dropsies.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have discussed in the division of the similarities of dropsy, and in what way the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made with medicines, and the one cured by iron: if it is exposed alone; and one should not touch iron in these two similarities: this means tympanites and hydrops, because they are a mortal thing; therefore, when you treat this similarity of dropsy called "exposed" by medicines, and the cure does not work, look at whether the patient is weak, or if he has another illness than dropsy, such as constipation and similar symptoms; do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient with great health, and he has only dropsy alone, and is neither too old nor too young, then thus operate: lift the patient upright over your hands, and the minister presses the belly outwards with the spatumile of thorny wood in the most lowest part of the stomach.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let them cut from both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Cut with a point and do not pierce so deeply that it may reach the intestine when you insert it; nor should you be able to feel relief. Then check if the dropsy is confined towards the intestines: if it's fitting, cut below the third vein on the right side of the neck; and if it's due to liver disease, cut on the left side of the third vein; and if it's due to inflammation, cut on the right side, but do not make the patient feel better by cutting in a way that the superfluous blood flows to the weak person. Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pour out, and leave your hand at the space between the skin and the vein as if you were scraping away to the quantity of an nail or less; then pierce the vein until the bleeding stops, which is like the swelling of the water; and that's the mark of the liquid.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it seems like a knife of silver, and is made from iron or horsehair lightweight, and has a small crack in that part; and on the cost it has three cracks; and two on one side, and one on the other; and they cut the nails so as if they were a feather, and this is the form of the incision which the scribes carve like a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	On the top of it there is a nail, so when the instruments come to water, now take them out from the instrument; empty it then for the third part, because if you empty more than it should in that hour, by chance he may die from the resolution of his spirit with the arm, or he will drop his fists, or he will approach death; but empty according to the amount of his virtue, and according to what the arrangements of his virtue indicate for the patient's hands; then take the instrument and hold the water, because it is now held by the nail that was above on the syphac, of which I have spoken, so you must pierce in this manner; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw a small amount of water from it. Do not do this every day, and be careful not to become foolish until he is freed but with a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt about the patient, and let them drink much water, then apply a poultice of earth or hot ashes, and have them stay for a long time in the sun, and if they get thirsty, give them a drink; and cure with medicines desiccatives until they are healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, just as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without any deformity in the penis, or if there are deformities they are small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If they wish to pierce at once, so that it cannot be pierced on the entire length of the penis very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Instruct the patient to insert the punctured clove into the boil for three days or four nights, and when it wishes to urinate, stop the flow and sew the wound, then do so again after urination, and possibly there will be no discharge, because the urine that comes out is not able to close the wound.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those of whom there is a puncture are small, if it is treated with the clove of garlic, as we have said, because they will swell.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have a puncture in their own vein are troubled, because no one is born with a puncture on the head of the penis, for they cannot urinate until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot defecate due to this matter not being able to come down just to the anus, and this is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to lie on his back, let the head of the rod rest in the middle, and strike it as hard as the length of a finger, so that the punctured piece is in the middle, just like he needs; and take care not to cause more bloodshed which often happens, and if there is, then pinch the one who causes the bleeding, and cure the wound until it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	of swellings of the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often swellings come in the rod, and it's an ugly appearance; and some are bad and some are not so bad; if you want to prick them at one time with a subtle needle, strike and puncture all of them, then put on cotton wool soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure with powdered opium until they are healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the inflammation is malignant, of a foul color and smelling, then it is fitting that you apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you cut it, and if the inflammation is within the vein, and has part of it inside the skin and part outside, then it is fitting that you remove the inflammation which is first inside; and when it is sewn up, take out the remaining part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat the whole thing together, if you are not certain that the vein is completely healed, and darkening and corruption come upon it and on what is next; then it is fitting to remove all that which is black and corrupted, and put an ointment of honey and flour made from pomace of grapes and figs, and tie up with bandages until it is cured.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if the hemorrhaging comes, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two situations: when there is bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and swollen, it is advisable to insert a stick into the penis and let the patient urinate through it. And when the hair grows back onto the head of the penis which has not been circumcised for any wound or abscess, then it is advisable that you burn it with an instrument like a file, until the laceration is dissolved, and the head of the penis is freed from all parts; and if this is a painful procedure to treat, then it is advisable to burn it with a single spatumile (a small stick) near the top of the penis and beard; afterwards serve well between two, and insert a subtle linen strip soaked in cold water, so that it does not cause further injury.
de la circoncision	About circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the cause of further complications like other wounds; it is permissible when we do this work by our own will, and especially in children, for it is necessary that we perform it the best way and with the least harm to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say that they cut the circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the greatest part of the masters and doctors who performed circumcisions in the past, with force, and with all sorts of novelties; it was often that the kings feared because they had two tongues, and by chance if those above were killed, the one below remained.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	For the recovery, and there is double pain, and when cleansing the point of the member is not secure; and by the cleansing of the swelling sometimes escapes the iron, and the wound heals, and thus many times as if they needed further cleansing I have desired.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Through the cleansing which is done on all parts of the limb I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut exactly equally above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, the fingers grow equally in all directions except for the skin; but if the thread is tied tightly around the leather; and if the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child think it's being done only to tie the thread around the shaft so much as possible, then make it straight between your hands or below your fingers so that the child does not see anything, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the shaft and blow gently into the wound, and take it up as high as the head of the shaft is; then clean well with water assembled around it; then tie a double thread around him, one above the other, and tie them apart by half an inch; and hold tight for two fingers by the second band to the pouch and to the dock; and cut between the two bonds; and take the head of the shaft up hastily; and let the blood flow little by little, because it's the worst part; and put powder on top and above the powder glue made from a mixture of rose water, oil of roses good and fresh, and confited with olive oil, and leave it on for just one day, and cure him again with another cure until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the force at purification is this: the two heads are tied and are cut off, and they are as large as the middle finger equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	the error of purification is when the hairs within burst at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the wound becomes an abscess; and strike equally, and if you cannot hold it to your finger, then take tourniquets, and then strike.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	and if they burst for three days, and the thing below the vein is swollen, you should leave it until the abscesses of the nails are healed, and skin lightly; then strike as you can move, and keep away from the part of the vein, so that it will not harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the shoulder from sudden wounds caused by powder, as we have said to treat powders, and if one strikes at the joint out of measure, and it goes up, so as not to harm; cure then, just as we have said, until he is safe.
dou retenement de l’urine	When retention of urine occurs.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	When retention of urine occurs due to stone, frost, bowel obstruction, char disease, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not flowing, and you see it is caused by a stone lodged near the neck of the bladder, so that the patient's knees are curved under them; then they should be placed on their buttocks, and extend his stomach from above towards his back, and restrain the patient as much as possible; and thus the necks of the bladder are constricted to force out the stone upward, because the urine is flowing out; and if it does not come, just as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, so it would be fitting that you administer extraction for all instruments called "siringue", whose form is this: and it should be an object of fine silver lightweight chain, similar to a bird's feather; and it should have a length of half a palm and half a palm, and be delicate at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, and tie to the chief one poude of laine or of couton, and but the chief dou fil dedens la siringue; and cope la superfluiteit de la lainne and the bute juscau chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre and d’aubin d’uef, and fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, and li arose la vessie and la verge d’oile moiste and d’oile d’olive and d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant juscau la vessie, and the sente li malaides venir juscau la chose vuide, and ceu n’est mie fait according to ceste ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc and poc, and li urine en suit la laine, puis the estrai fuer, and fai corre l’urine; and rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, and soit aligiez li malaides.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or pus comes to the bladder, when putrefaction is assembled, and you see water and medicine dripping, do this with all the instrument called "clepsedre", and it's the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three perforations: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the medicinal liquids are applied so that they can be absorbed well into the urethra, if possible, and poured when necessary; and when you see your medicines dripping into the bladder, put the head of the cup over the moisture, and draw it off at the source; if you draw the moisture off at the source, and then pour the medicine back in strongly; if the moisture enters again, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle catheter used to catheterize the bladder:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	Instruct the patient to let his hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division of stones, and the extraction of assembled medicines; and I said the difference between stone embedded with iron nails, or with a splinter, and all signs; and in which stone we must cut with an axe; and in the bladder, and the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones embedded in the bladder often occur in children, and this is a sign that water is bursting out of the bladder like urine from its subtlety; and they burst open, and grieve the patient's penis, and he cuts it many times, and then becomes inflamed; and at most of these accidents, death occurs; and children take less time to recover until they are four years old, and are much more grieved in old men, and are between those who have gone from youthfulness to old age; and the cure is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, so it is fitting first to purify the patient by cupping, in order to draw out all the blood that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	But it is often not worth seeking to cut stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the hands and push down on his feet, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not rise up again once or twice; then have him sit between your fingers, and let his hands be below his knees, so that the bladder is completely emptied downwards; then look at it and touch inside; if you feel a stone in the space, now hasten to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not empty all down into the toucher, (if) apply a small amount of oil from your right index finger to the wound, since the patient is sick or fevered, or if they are young and not accomplished; and pour it into its fundament, and look at the stone; and when you feel it with your right hand, if it adheres to the base of the bladder; then press upon it with your right hand, and pour away where you see cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he must stretch out his right hand to touch the fingers at the top, and with his left hand take hold of the skin under the fingers in the part where the belly button is made; then let him pour the spatalium on it, so that this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And let him make an incision between the fingers and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left nipple; and it should be straight above the stone, and its two edges should meet at or near the foundation, and if necessary, cut through the belly button so that it is wide enough by default, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, neither too large; for chance, the press may hit something on the foundation that causes it to bounce off work; and note whether there is part of the stone or an angle, and margins: if it's cut out easily; and if there is part that is smooth, like a glint, and rounded, from which the issue comes lightly.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those with angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it won't break, it is best to strain the nails that are like a file on top of the head, in order to strain the bone so that it doesn't escape; or you pour liquid substance into the instrument bent at the top; and if you cannot put it in thus, make an opening in the rotten part, and if they don't come out, then strain them with vitriol; and if there are more bones, first pour the largest one down the neck of the bladder, then cut up, then take out, and the smaller ones after if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then make a larger wound and cut.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For these two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes back into him again because of a wound that cannot heal; but force yourself to treat, whether by dressing the wounds or cutting the nails, until you have treated it by pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the ointment of pitch, dragon's blood, and sanctum balm, and bind it, then put above it a wet cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water to soothe the abscess; afterwards revive the patient on his back, and do not untie the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, apply a lot of oil and water to the patient well, then give him an application of diffinicon and basilicon ointment until he is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes in the wound and causes corrosion and congealment of blood in the bladder, and is retained by this, which prevents urination in that manner without passing with urine: therefore put dough in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains there, the bladder will corrode and rot; then lift the wound with water and asphodel and silphium, and treat him in all the ways you know, until he is healthy; and it is to be considered that all the remedies you use, should tie together his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on him.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it is located near the rod and fixed there, and urine cannot come out; then the doctor of what I said again, that you measure its length many times, will be excused from measuring for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron according to this shape and stick three nails into one tile:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie around the rod near the stone, so that it cannot come out through the bladder; then put the iron lightly into the rod until it comes to the stone; and turn the iron in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; when it comes, then press your hand over the part of the stone that is left inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bone is broken and swells with urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread under the bone and the other above, then straighten the rod between the two tendons, then draw out the force, and free the ligament, and cleanse the wound of frozen flesh which is in the injury; and let the cure continue until he is cured.
de la piere des femmes	About women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is little chance that a stone will be found in women, and if it happens once, the cure is painful, and is prevented by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that you cannot find any woman who knows how to show herself naked before mirrors, especially when she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If it happens that she finds (it), so it is fitting to move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder up to the knee, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then strike above the stone in the root of the thigh against the midpoint of the bone, where it is moist and matted, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move your fingers over the stone or below it, and let the first little piece remain; then pour in the hot liquid into the bone, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as far as the bone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small ones and big ones and rough ones and smooth ones, long ones and round ones, and those with cracks.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, and the he takes it to the land of vinegar, and he holds him for an hour until he is stained; then returns to his work, until the pain subsides, and has bandages that I have told you about in the extraction of stones for your help in your work; and if he does not vibrate, and this is from the artery that was cut, he puts powder on the land and the stain of tenters and bendles, and should not start again, and leaves the stone and does not treat it more, lest by chance the patient dies; then cures the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is appeased, and the swelling subsides, then returns to his work, until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	of a hairy navel
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rice water is nothing but the assembly of moisture or white scab, which is underneath the curd, that contains the blood; and it's called "scab", and there is no other cause for it; and it's the skin of the curd between the white scab that we have said about; and this happens unless it was a different wound.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rice water is from weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: or it's color fading to yellowish, or it's without red, or black, or white, and it happens more; and these are the signs to know that there is this assembly, because if it is like the scab we have said, then it is the abscesses returning, for a long time since like the figure of an ear, and it does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	If there is moisture in the own wool, then it is understood that the abscesses return with part of the flesh; and because of this one thinks it is another wound; and if the moisture is between the skin of the groin and the white flesh, it feels numb; therefore when you see to know the color of the moisture, take a survey of all the surrounding area, for that's where the form was previously.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Then judge what is inside according to what comes after the surrounding area.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cut with iron, it is fitting that the patient be judged according to one's strength and the replenishment of their body; then make the sign above on their back, on a high place, and put down much wool upon them; then sit on their left side, and command the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two costal bones near the groin; then take the spongy stick (spatula) and cut the skin of the groin from long to short, until you reach the flesh close to the white bone; and scrape it gently according to the strength of the pain; then pierce the white bone straight through with a sharp point, and extract all the blood, and then put on wool, and stretch the white bone upward; and do not touch the skin of the groin, but only the white bone; cut it thoroughly in pieces at once, so that if you do not cut it well, he will return to bleeding; and if the flesh is torn apart in your hand, fix it in its place when you have completed the operation on the white bone; then assemble the two breast bones near the groin into one costure, and treat as other wounds until they are sane.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the corrupted vein infected with another disease, it is appropriate to tie off the vessels that are superimposed on it, in doubt about the progress of the blood; then strike the vein at all the superimposed vessel, and draw out the vein, and cure as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If an injury is assembled into two parts in a similar way, that is to say, you have seen it is made of two branches; then strike the other part as you have done with the first equally, and suck out the blood, and put on the wound a soft linen moistened in rose oil; and put over another soft linen moistened in wine and oil, and put on both veins, and cover it with double draperies, and tie it up above all according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the draperies, and sew them with woolen batting according to this resemblance and assemble them by stitching in the neck of the braies, and one of the knots is placed on the foundation just above the back, and the others on the part of the nail; and the other two are placed above the two arteries, and so all assembled the restraint is tied around the noose of the braie; and it has been medicated with cautery in place of iron binding, as when you take a subtle cauterizing instrument, and strike the skin of the veins, so that the white substance contained in the blood is uncovered; if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the syphac with nails, and burn it with this subtle cautery hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	Instruct the patient to do everything as you wish them; until you are certain all is well; and be careful that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more safe; and keep watch for the stopping of blood, and beware of the injuries from cutting; and if nothing opposes you or an abscess or a stoppage of blood or any other thing, then cure what opposes you, according to what has been said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is fearful and will not wait for this operation because of its horror, perforate them as I have told you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs we have said that urine comes out, then put the patient on a high bed; pierce the abscess at the place below until the whole purulent mass is released; and make a large opening so that all the pus can flow out; then apply cotton to the wound, tie it up, and let the rest of the pus drain off; then cure them until the wound is healed; and if the scabbing does not allow the pus to come out from the mouth of the wound, then you should put a pen or the instrument used for treating urinary issues, in the shape as before; and expand the wound further, and know that the pus returns and comes together after six months or so, and when it comes together just like before, and thus will pass the patient's days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Out of the abscesses of the throat
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	It is clear that in the cutting of this branch there are many deaths and fatalities, so it seems to me that one should not cut; and I will tell you about the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the body and especially from wounds, and this is for many reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is that is due to superfluous acidity and water, which spreads into the abscesses or by percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, but an abscess with a wound; and sometimes it is a heavy and painful abscess, and a swollen one, and of a foul color, and not often comes from another source than an artery, or swelling in the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is through some artery, so it is recognized by the disposition of the abscess in the hot place, when you press on both sides with your fingers; and it is not advisable that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from the inflamed vein is recognized by its disposition at the point of touch with the fingers, and can easily be cut on this shape, and on other marks; and it is that you strike the pulse in the neck, then keep the ear above, and pull downwards to white skin, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the ear.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the ear is already swollen with these marks, then it is advisable to treat the ear and strike it; and if there are arrows in the cartilage, or inside the vessels, it is advisable to deliver all that space, and strike it round.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the child is at your back side, it is fitting that you copy it all over and extract the phlegm, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your wounds are finished, apply the wound of soft linen moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat with other treatments until he is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the teeth.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess that has broken out wrapped in a membrane similar to the bone marrow, with the softening of the teeth, and the patient experiences great pain when it heals; and the treatment for this disease is as bad as we have previously said, and as we will tell you, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Instruct the patient to sit upright on the elevated bed, then take the suspender cord over his shoulders down to his elbows, and stretch out all the surrounding vessels, and the nerves, and expand them; then cut at the spot where the vessel traverses the bone, until it is visible, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples; then put a needle or double thread on the first level where the vein has come out, and tie it to the other cheek, and cut straight ahead, according to the length of the body, and take away the corrupting moistures; then cure the wound as we do for broken bones, so that none of the vessels come out, if one of them is found; because this does not bring harm, and when all the vessels are tied, they do not lose their nourishment, and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the surgical cut of the face
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The symptoms of this branch are caused by sectioning or cutting the face, or by stretching on the belly in the area of the entrails, because the intestines descend from that incision to one of the joints; and these two kinds of causes come from: percussion, impact, burns, or lifting of a pain, and similar things; and the signs when there is an extension of the cut on the face are such that they occur little by little, over a long time, and do not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equalized up to the bone, because the incision presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section on the face, which brings sudden pain at the beginning; and the abscesses appear in various appearances, under the skin, near the intestine and outside the bone of the face.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes they cut with the bowels, and it is retained in the groin, causing great pain to suffer from the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments with fear, because it is avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way of treating wounds is that you instruct the patient to tie a fold of intestine into his hand inside the wound, if it can be returned; then sovize above his neck between your hands, and lift the knees; then make the incision on top, and cut through all the skin around the joint long enough; then pour in the intestines according to what you need to open the wound, and so that they can come out; then scrape off the yellow stuff that is below the skin of the joints, until only white scar tissue remains visible from every part; then pour your two fingers into the space between the skin which is over the joint, between the white scar tissue which is under the skin of the shoulder, and between the second scar tissue, and in front of the joint, and in the space behind the joint, and between the second scar tissue; and move it back to the right hand inside the incision on the joints, and lift up the joint above your left hand, and extend the joint above, and release what is tied behind the band; and if you find that there is no intestine attached or white scar tissue, then pour it into the abdomen below; then take an awl with a 1-inch cord made of X threads, and pour it in at the back of the scab, which is after the skin of the joints; after the abdomen, then cut off the hairs that appear from the threads, until there are 4 threads left; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the scab with a strong cord of 2 parts; then evacuate the hairs from the threads, and bind them firmly for 2 parts, so that no servants who suckle you can enter into you, that there is no opening or passage; and put the cord in place according to the first cord long 2 times of that one, and after those 2 cords leave off the scab which is under the joint the length of a double cord; and then do all the rest according to the curvature of the joint; then cut through the skin below the joint as we have said before; then anoint laine with oil, and apply to the wounds, and put on the binding that we have told.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes cauterize the white flesh so that we have said, after incising, by doubt of decomposition of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.
