For this happens many times, and let the bandage stay on it until it falls off by itself; and if it delays at night, either rises from hot water, and puts on what we have said, until it falls off; then treat the wound with another cure, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of caruncle or varicose hernia.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this section I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done in this way: like the raspberries that are assembled on the skin, in such a manner that you tie the straps, after cutting above, lightly below; then cut into the flesh, and cure the abscess that occurs, until the strap chafes; and cure so as we have said, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you strike the hair, if it muffles and cures the wound, so that it is sound.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is tied, and has no appearance in the wound, and the cautery is more moist in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	It happens often that the skin of the joints is softened in some people, because the flesh inside is softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary, when you want to cure him, to make the patient lie on his back, and strike the soft skin above the natural skin; then tie the two lips together with a bandage, and if you see, cut through the first three layers of softened skin or four firmly; then strike between the layers, and the cure is like other wounds, until he is healed, and the stitches come out.
dou chastrement	Let the cautery of fire command to the sick person that they let their hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold your eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cauterys are forbidden in our law, and for this reason I do not want to speak of them in this book; and it is necessary only two ways: one, so that those who know about cautery may respond when they are asked, and tell the cure; and the other, because we have often had need of cautery from certain animals to help us, as from oxen and sheep and goats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauterys are done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that way which we do by attraction, we make the person sit best in hot water, until their flesh are softened and relaxed; then prick with your hand, until they feel no more.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: it is fitting that you tie the bestiary, and press the skin of the joints to your left hand, then suspend the suspension rope, and strike each joint once, when you have well scraped them; and let any little scratch on the skin and the subtle scratch which is on the harnesses; and this method of chastrement is more gentle than that which is done by attraction, because attraction may perhaps leave some thing from the joints, due to which the bestiary desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of those who are hermaphroditic.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	An hermaphrodite is according to two kinds of homes: one is that between the two sexes opens like the figure of a woman's nature, or he has hair, and sometimes no urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And other women are also thus, and they have a point on the nipple, just like a stick.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cures for indigestion and hunger are thus: you must tie up the stomach all the time, just like other wounds; in this second manner, men who have urine bursting from their penis due to infection, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the testicles
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tentigene is tied up on the natural part, until it becomes too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as their hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to dye the superfluality of the testicles on your hand or near the nails, and tie it lightly; and do not go too far, lest blood comes from it, then you must apply another cure until it is healed; and there is another char where a boil appears at the mouth of the vagina, and the vulva, and by chance bursts forth, and is like an egg, and for this they call it "the cow's disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to copy it, just as we have said, and the treatment until it is healthy.
de erratique	Of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	In error, for when the nature of woman is not perceived, or the defect is felt; and it is natural by birth, or an accident due to illness that came upon her, or it's caused by a chariot accident, or by a sharp stab or piercing, and it occurs in the womb, or on the breast, or elsewhere, or whatever way; for it fails conception, childbirth, and by chance the flowers may not have appeared; and knowledge of this is perceived through the swelling of the face.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If there are signs of a rupture near, then choose whether to do it with your two hands or the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is swollen with pus and it is close to the two pounds, hasten and do thus: put your two fingers together, and the woman lies on her back, spreading her legs; then set the two pounds apart, as long as the swelling subsides, and the pus is stopped; then take lard in oil, and put it on the joint, and have the woman apply to every part each day, so that it will not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and dense, it is best to make a wound like leaves of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stopped blood is of charcoal, if you apply to the spot and wound, and have the medicinal juices, like aloe, dragon's blood, incense, and many others, then put a large linen bandage around it, so that the wound cannot heal; and do this for a long time, and apply a linen tent dry; and be cured with other cures until you are healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the groin comes a wound or sore, so they must cover it according to this manner; unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is in the groin does not need to be touched with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which are not usually cut, and when old hemorrhoids occur they become swellings; and we have said in the section on ulcers the similarities to abscesses, and I will tell you here those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and swellings when they are swollen in the groin and do not appear to the sense of touch, unless it is treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who have at the corner of the mouth, you can feel, are those that you can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then sit her at the altar with tongs, and cut in her roots, then powder over medicines restraining blood, as it was accustomed and bleeding of dragon and incense, and similar things; then pour her feet into boiling water for an hour, then put her in cold water; and when the bleeding comes, if you do so, make her sit on a decoction of sumac and grape juice and gall and similar things, and then mix with wheat flour and honey and easily, and enfold it on her back to apply;
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it clots, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this is not so, if they make the patient inhale hot air on the back and on the shoulders with pain; then take a linen cloth, and apply it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of angelica with wine old, and let him breathe.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess heals, then treat the patient with poultice until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so they should cover it as I have said; and then continue to treat him until he is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come from the marrow, such as canker and bone abscess, herpes, itching, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and other diseases that I have mentioned in this division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I tell in this treatise the abscess that comes to the marrow of the bone, which is not an abscess that only cools bowels; and if you see well how the fire cautery works, look carefully whether the abscesses are present at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	And therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let the patient rest until the pain is alleviated; and then put him on a seat, with two petis sieges or he can recline, and support his back and assemble his feet towards the leg; and make his knees spread out, and place his arms under his girdle, and tie them well with a good ligature; then take the bale (of cauterization) to the right side of the face, and apply it afterwards to the form that comes after this; and it is necessary that when you see apply this instrument, that you pierce first in place by depth so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not harm the patient; and if the instruments are large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with drapery, so that the instruments do not grieve him; and it is necessary to put the cone of the instrument on top, and to tie the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	If the wound is covered with linen, then it is wise to avoid applying hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The skill is first in the birth that she knows the natural figure of birth, and the signs are when you see the woman press herself to expel, and desire to bring forth the afterbirth: then hastens the child to come forth quickly; for it seems that those children born naturally are according to their own figure, and are out from under their head, and with them is the second part; and when you see these signs, it is wise to press lightly on her belly, so that the child comes out soon; for when he pushes upwards from his head, then is the second part with him, and cleanses the linen of its superfluities by good cleansing; and this that comes about other ways does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it happens sometimes in his feet, and the flesh or the joints, and the hands, where he comes upon his belly, or sovin, and is transformed by chance to the neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the healer to be cautious and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fever comes upon his head due to natural cause, and a pregnant woman cries out, and the virtues of her flesh are weak, then you must put her on a stool, or have women hold her; and if the matter is cooked in oil or fenugreek, and then pour the balm between her two nipples with the small spatula which is this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cut the sinew, and strike at one of her joints until the moistures that are in the fire come out; and take away the belly of the woman as long as the fever descends; and if it does not descend, you should cover the woman with musk and fenugreek with olive oil; then let her drink and vomit with condities, and keep her mouth and nostrils closed for an hour: if this is done now, she will be cured.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, so it is fitting to gently pull them apart little by little; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on the bed, lift her feet up high; then draw the bed onto the earth, and let the woman, so she does not strike with the falling down; and if the hands cannot enter and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is placed before it, and extract the child, and pull them apart gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child's feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, so it is fitting to push it upwards; and then turn it a little by a little, until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them out a little by a little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can he jump just as quickly, if he pricks himself with a needle, and the blood flows out from his body; if he falls, may God be with him.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he is unable to do so as we have said, if the pain increases little by little, until it is according to his natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then he will be lightened.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come about as we have said, then take musk and aloes, and olive oil, and gum arabic, and grind everything in mortar; and put on the natural woman's substance inside and apply this ointment, then let him sit in cold water until below the ribs; and when he is softened down, let him tie a linen band around, and put it on, and let him lie still for an hour; then let him sit on the seat, then let him vomit and tie his mouth and nose, and let him take to his belly lightly, because he now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, so it puts on its balance when its hands are little by little; then it leans on its shoulder and hangs its feet below, and sits gently on I lit; and bends its knees a little by little, and then it grips with its hands upon the air, and opens the cussins beneath, until she is dressed down below; and if the child does not leap, so take its feet and bend them together, then lift up the belly, then pour in your hands; and let the child come a little by little; and instruct the woman to dress herself while the child is still inside.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child which comes with a limb extended
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is fitting to endeavor to return the limb: if it cannot be returned, if you raise the woman and go; if she cannot go, then make her sit on I lit, and bend the knees; then bring in the musciline as I have described; and if she does not conceive, then make her sit on the stool, then study to return the limb; and let the child come according to its natural figure, and make her prepared, and instruct her to dress herself until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of a child after its birth on the neck, and has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its back its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is certain that the child twists its hand, then turns it a little and little, and makes it lighter; and when it has become even, if you put some muslin cloth on it and oil, as we have said, then he commands her to make it move a little by little; and when you have done this, sit her down in the seat, and she must bind herself.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner to all the rest
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When he comes to this manner to all the rest, strike the vein at your elbow, until the moisture is clear; and if his face and neck swell, strike from the nose, so that it does not congeal, and die the child; then pour him into a vessel, as far as you have put him in, as much as is fitting, and command the woman to bind herself at all times: then he becomes lighter.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the issue of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	They are said to be born many times, and sometimes they are born with three or four fingers; and this is not a strange thing, and it rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things and do not live if they are named; I know that they are multiplied and are cut off by the same factor that devises them, which is linked to the bowel; and sometimes they come out naturally like all of us have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out severely, then the cure is as we have said, and it's done with subtle bile, and it heals quickly and lightly what she does; and it is just like what is found in good medicine for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marrow of the femur I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than fifteen times, and all forms take on the shape of a child according to the measurement of its glorious size, for it is possible that some similar thing has occurred; therefore, do as this seems fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I said in division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained by work of hands; if this seems fitting that you know whether the woman is of good virtue, and has no accident, or has fear of death; if this seems fitting that the woman be sure on her back, and her joints inclined inward, and her legs raised; and the minister gives two parts of oil to the marrow with muskillaige of altee and fenugrec and seed of flax, then rub the jaw of the marrow with these oils and muscillaiges, then inject into the marrow lightly, then take one at a time or whatever seems fitting to you, and be careful if the infant is appeared that it comes forth from its chief; then inject one in his eye or on his chin or in his mouth or on his cheek or near the breasts or under the armpits or beneath the navel or near the ribs so that the thing comes forth by the piez, inject a second and pinch the skin and along the cost; and it seems fitting to give an onion to her hand with her right hand between her two hands of the left hand, and inject into all these places lightly until it is dry; this is the shape of the onion:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Instruct the patient to find another bone where it can be fixed, or if you have to operate on it, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch it evenly in moving from one side to the other, for it to come out, and keep the bones aligned as it does, just like this:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if it remains in part, pourge with some of its two parts of fat, and put them into that part, and treat the other part; and if it does not remain in place, move this bone or higher to you, and do thus until it comes out all fiery.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be reduced by straining, so that you wrap up its drapery, until it comes out all; then cut in the joint of the foot or at the cost, and do thus with the other hand, and on the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is upon its feet, so that there is a slight attraction to it, and the address to the opening of the marrow at the mouth of the femur is also light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is strained in the belly or in the groin, so that you bring forth what has been hidden above the navel on the arm; and make the belly or the groin, until the moisture that resides there; and if another member is dislocated, and the head (of the femur) remains stuck, then fill the gap with water and oil, and let it flow; and if the marrow of the marrow is closed by a sharp clot which has come in, it is not necessary to further trouble it, but rather to offer soft and moist things; and these are suitable for eating after the passage of time, and slice them in milk that soothes and calms.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its chest and you can put it even, follow what we have said in the living infant; and if you do not have power, place the wound by pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, follow what we have said about the apothecary's measures that come out from the marrow; and if bleeding comes again, then tie it up in water and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman with child, and the child had died, then she consulted another besides it, and the other died as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came an abscess in the tooth, and it swelled so much that it burst, and great pain began.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the doctor, and I thought it would take so long, and could not wait for the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and from it an bone came out, and after some other days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised much, because that belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I sought the wound, and with my hands I found bones, until the woman was in better shape; and she had lain there for long time like that, and finally it began to show a bit of bone on her left. And I have never written this chapter except because when the master physician encounters an unusual thing, he knows how to give aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	Letting the marrows return to their place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of pressure, where one presses the books; and then again to the two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	In any case, the horn is more subtle in its restraint, and is made of ebony or boxwood; and it has a mouth that is two fingers' breadth wide, and the margin of the tree should be one finger's breadth, and an arm's length long; and for both joints of this same horn, they are two adjacencies of this same fist, which are firm in one and in the other, half a palm or a little more; and these two adjacencies are sealed in the mouth of the marrow to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar in subtlety and lightness, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of the nails; and it has two joints, with two adjacencies, just as you see, one palm's length, and two fingers' breadth; when you open the marrow with all the instrument, place the woman on a stool over her belly, and bend your knees, and overlie your feet; then seal both adjacencies together in the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument between its joints; then operate your hand over the entire instrument, just as you have done with the nails equally, according to the amount that opens the mouth of the marrow, until they cause it what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all above, and it is multiplied in its likeness; and when the wounds are prepared with mirrors, then it is more hastening to do the work, and higher to the heights for its quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not prepare the instrument that you use it, because their necessity is no excuse.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second tooth is retained in childhood, it is fitting that you command the patient to keep their lower lip and gums tight, and then make them spit out with condensing powder, and tie your hands tightly around the mouth and nose; and if she swallows this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If that does not happen, then the procedure is performed, and make a perforation or a cavity, and put herbs which can open the mouth of the mare, such as camphor, anise, chamomile, saffron, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or boiled in water on fire; then put a candle or a perforated pot in the mouth of the mare, and tie the other cheek inside the mouth, and let it remain until the vapors come out from within the mare's mouth; then make her spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If he takes the secondine ( likely a reference to an instrument used for cautery) immediately.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and is not better, instruct the nurse to moisten her left hand with olive oil or with musk or alum, then soak it in water, and later bring back the secondine; and when she finds it, grasp it gently and straighten it little by little, so that the stitches do not cut during the extraction; but they should move lightly from right to left, and then treat her again; if she comes and loses her hand.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the stitches on her mouth are still tight, we have prescribed to unclog and to fumigate with herbs; and if she is not better from what we said, be cautious so that you do not err in treatment; but it is likely that what is tied around the mouth of the stitching will be bound to a woman's cistern, then wrapped with ointment tetraformula; put on the poultice and restore her; but however, when she puts it on herself, if there comes a foul odor to the stomach and head, and troubles the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is therefore necessary to perform fumigations convenient for this: none of the ancients has proved that fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which to fumigate the woman at the retention of flowers and second skin if this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And is to look like a knife, and put the head subtle in the nature, and the hairs wide on the fire; and so be the fumigation on the coals, and the lice until they are consumed, and begin again another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	But infants are born who have no pierced foundation at all, unless a subtle syphilitic has infected one: therefore it is necessary to pierce the lump in the baile where he has infected him, and not pierce too deeply with a sharp instrument, and loosen the lacing so that she does not touch it; then put on a linen cloth moistened in wine and oil, and apply ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, put a bandage on the wound and let it sit for days, and be careful when it comes in to visit.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes there is sudden bleeding from a wound or an abscess; if you want to cover that moment: if it heals, as we have said about the bandage on the wound.
de la fistule dou fondement	of a fistula in the fundament.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from beneath the fundament are nodules, and those that come from the fundament without going through either of its parts, or when there is more than one fistula; and when that nodule is old, it festers, and covered with moist pus or subtle bowels, and sometimes these fistulas burst; and they occur because of egestion or flatulence when the patient makes egestion, and by chance some pieces break off.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that open just above the bladder and just above the penis; and they reach just above the joint of the thigh, and not beyond the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus you find the fistula running to the fundament, and not going any further: and it is that you put your thumb on the foundation, and pour an arrow or thin iron into the fistula when there is tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, so you put a subtle plug or the hair of a horse in it, until you feel the plug or the hair on your way out; and if you don't feel anything, and they do not come out through peristaltic movement or windiness, as we have said: see that she does not pierce. If you hasten to the cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced just above the bladder or just above the urethra, so that it bursts and cannot be closed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived just above the joint of the thigh, so that blood comes from there; if there are no knots or signs of pain near it, then it hurts and does not heal by medicine or application of ointment; and in these piercing fistulas, there is no cure except labor and folly of foolish physicians who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those who are not piercing and are not old, there is hope for health by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient should lie between your hands on his back; lift up his legs to the knees, and bend his knees towards his belly; then pour a poultice of earth or plasters if it has knots, until you know where the poultice comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the bone, then it is advisable to put your two fingers on that spot, if you feel that the pain tries to pierce inside; and whether it is discovered or you feel a seafic or char between your thumb and finger, then know that she is pure; but do not try any more, lest you cannot cure her.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is commonly known that some can be cured with treatments, but this happens rarely, and the help we make for them, if it is done as instructed earlier; and if the cautery is heated subtly according to the size of the fistula, so that it comes out from the bottom; and do this twice or three times, until you know which characters must be burned, which are similar to a bird's feather; and then put on moist poultices with butter, until those characters burn, and then apply ointment to bind and stitch.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is so damaged, this is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is so damaged, nothing else can be done to heal it; and if he tries between them and doesn't pierce exactly where the foundation is, and there's a thick covering of charcoal or pitch between his two toes and the tent, and you see the fistula at that spot with a covering of redness; then cut away from the beginning of the fistula, and let blood flow afterwards until it reaches the top of the tent; and he will be freed from the pain and the inflammation; then take out those charcoal-like things that resemble an owl's feather, and don't leave anything.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he doesn't bleed from it, and cuts between you and the wound, if the fire cautery or astringent medicine is applied.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery there are two things to consider: that is to say, the burning of these charred joints and the stretching of the vein and the drying out of moisture; then the treatment of wet wounds in butter or in broken places, until the joint bleeds, and the veins are heated up; then cure the wound of the quick limbs, which are touched by hot iron, and are burned with it, such as those who are charred on the bowels, and are the medicines that dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	But when it is restored again, it is safe and does not come back.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes to a complete stop at the bottom of its foundation, and is distant from the body, pour two or three of wine into its foundation, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tendons, and there are two of them that are torn or charred, or it is close to piercing, if only fire was visible by chance and expectation, through the management of one of three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you pierce it from the bottom, or if you can, you apply poultices and cure as first; do not go too far into the depth, lest you cover the seat that holds the foundation, and bring out the extractions by chance; then cure, as we have said; by luck, it may become healed, or the covering will be removed from the wound when it is pierced at the bottom, or with a poultice, or with some other instrument pointed; then examine this faulty char that is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and to keep the fistula away from the opposite part of the foundation: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way; and when you put a tent in the fistula, if it is open at the foundation of the skin above, take a tent that reaches up to the head according to this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I tie a knot in the first part and tie the tent all along the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perforated in the margin of the foundation within, then pull out the thread from that part, so that you tie your knot or on the foundation; and pull up the head from the thread, and assemble the two joints together, and fasten one to the other, and leave them for one day or two; and restrain it no more, until the threads are cut these characters that are between two, and close; then cure the wound until it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula or abscess is not punctured, then pierce it in all manners that you can, unless it is too close to the bone.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not advisable to tie it shut if it is too close to the bone, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spine which we cut when making a fistula is very angular and sharp, one part being long and narrow, and the other short and broad; and on this account it must not be cut too deeply, unless as you see.
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the fundament like a grain of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and in wounds they may have one or several, and it is to avoid the fundament and the head of the fundament; but those that are not are scarce moist, and stuck together by a little water citrine or a little blood clot, and have the color of flesh.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is fitting that you fasten the seam in this manner: take a thread, and put it through one hole, and then take up the thread above and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two joints of the thread below the needle, and if it be thin; and tighten the thread, then loosen the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus to all the others, and let one remain for sealing the superfluity of the wound; then place upon the foundation a moist cloth in rose oil or in ceruse, and place upon the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave him until he heals, and when he is healed, if his pain and other remedies are not sufficient, take out the thread.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	until the flesh or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times happens suddenly of blood in the intestines, and by the constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is appropriate to reset at the point of a spatula or on one’s nail the scab over, which does not allow it to dry; then treat as long as he is sound so as it may be; and if he cannot get well, restart the scraping stronger than before, until he heals completely and the skin is cleared, then treat him so that he becomes healed.
dou fremit	do not shake
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A small worm is a false appearance before the body, and goes in further; and sometimes it freezes the true path, and you feel it just like death of shaking, and comes throughout the body, and more so in the hands than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Instruct the cure to take a reed of an eel's feather, or a strong raven's feather, and place that reed on the swelling, until the purple circles appear all around; then turn your hand over the entire reed so you cut through it entirely, and put the reed into its root, and sharpen the swelling at its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a reed of thorn or iron according to that form, and be subtle under and above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, lest you make a mark that will be seen twice, and press; And if you see, cauterize the swelling, just as it is before or after the cautery of the fire.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a syringe or castor oil bottle.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	None of these things are done with silver or an iron rod, or melted tin or cloth; and sometimes one does these small and large instruments, according to what they have brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These are then used in the treatment of children who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small or large syringe is used when they are closed and bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if there is a rupture or the belly is bound, as you see, and the syringe is inside perceived; and if it has one opening on one side, and on the other one; and if the belly or the womb receives the medicines from a cow's bladder or parchment, and they are perceived all around with small openings, and there are one inch of space between each opening, then you must put in an inch of space, then pour into these openings strong thread, cut in the shape of X or inside, and assemble the belly like a donkey; and when the medicine is inside, if it sticks to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then syringe. And this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And so let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or bearberry wax, or a similar thing, then give it to drink lightly; then press the ministers' hands together on his two limbs, until he is all well, then remove the blister, and lift up the patient's legs, so that if the medicine comes out, so too will the boil, and if he sleeps through the night completely, then there will be more aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you blisterize him in an illness of descending wind, and the medicine comes out quickly, then he will start bleeding again until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there are hemorrhoids on the fundament or abscess, so that the blister is as subtle as when an infant, then it's the form of the fine blister where the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	For we have already said in the treatment of wounds; or you will tell us about the treatments for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they were made of, and according to the place or where wounds are made, and because of which they were made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things because wounds are made of are caused by a stone being struck, and the cutting from a sword or knife, or lance or club, or sieve, or similar things; or what is made according to the parts of the body, if a wound was shot onto the neck, or head, or ear, or belly, or liver, or like a limb; and I will tell you about each wound, and begin with simple wounds on the head, because the memory will come back in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I am warning you when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, so be cautious if it's a stone or similar thing, and the skin is completely torn apart and the wound is very large, and you doubt slightly whether there is an abscess: then do it immediately to heal the cephalic itself if it's come from bleeding of the wound, and let them be healed in the opposite direction of the naval part; and avoid the malady being replete with wine and heavy food.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal, if so that its meat is weakened, and does not drink wine, nor eats no flesh; and puts on the wound, if an abscess comes up, put cotton soaked in oil rose only, or in vinegar tostic; and if there is no heat, put on the wound if it is fresh with all its bleeding, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say one more time later, and if the fever has moved it, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a cut from a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be closed by stitches, then they are sewn together, just like I will say of wounds on the belly, from suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and flesh, and it cannot stay in place except by a small piece, if it's stuck; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore a hard surface in its place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat great quantities of food, such as meat, eggs, and bread, just like birds, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or rotting leather in the wound and it's not adhering to the bone, then remove all of it, and drain the pus, then cure the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound without any stop, that cannot be stopped by medicine, so cut the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then it is a light cure: and you must apply this powder which soles the wound just as much as the arrow has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take cense a part of it; dragon's blood two parts; calcined vivarium three parts, and finely mixed powder, and apply the wound, and bind it firmly, until it has been dried well and united with all its sanguis; and then tie it well, and let it loose if it does not swell; for one does not withhold medicine until it is healing.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes only calmed vivarium is used, when one does not have either the cense or the blood of the dragon, but the arrow has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the limbs have moved the wound, especially when it was open, do not put on this powder but put on some ointments digested or made of wheat flour with water and honey, until they dissolve; then the healer must treat other healings until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a fracture of bone comes with the wound and it is small, so that I will tell you later on after I explain head fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is at the neck and it is simple, and there is no difference between it and a head fracture, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is only leave to let the cure and not put anything that restrains, for they can be harmed at night and make them retreat; and do not put any thing on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of this is with the brain, which are the highest members; but if you take medicine, such as chalk washed in sweet water and melted with olive oil, and apply it also washed in sweet water, and other stones of lead according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, so tie on gauze bands, then cure until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.
