Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I try to translate the given text line by line into English.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the top of the arrow I put under the liver, stomach, and digestive tract, because the lungs swell up; and appeared the swellings on the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on his hands days before, and solved the wound directly underneath it, and he remained thus for a long time, until he felt the swelling in his chest one day; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put medicine on the wound, which was acid and corrosive, day after day, until it became open, and tried it, and felt that the head of the arrow had dried out in the chest; then I adjusted by opening up the wound with that medicine, so that the swelling of the arrow appeared visibly; and after passing well through the ends for four months, and then bursting the wound because I hammered on the nails too hard, from one side and the other, and could not get out; therefore I did not cease to subtilize and devise ways with instruments, until I took it that day with nicely made nails, according to what its form would come to in the end of this chapter, till I had tried it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wounds were closed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your cure on what I did not say, because the books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters have known little about a great thing, and those things present and faltering, find new work, and nine instruments, when they withdraw foreign things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not enter the members or they are fixed only in two ways: either through the bone or into another part; and if it enters by the side or another way, that is an arrow entering the marrow cavity, and it goes there for the first time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not heal now, let it be left to the point where its pores are opened and it is cleaned up; and so if it is fixed into bone, and it cannot come out, let it be left that way for some days, and move it every day; and thus it heals, and if it does not heal, then perforate into all of that forest, until the pore is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if an arrow is fixed into the bone of the head, and is stuck just next to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents I mentioned to the patient: do not treat it yourself, but let it be left until it is even after some days, because if the arrow comes just next to that spot, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone alone, and does not come out immediately, and the patient remains in this state for some days without any further accidents, then try to extract it by pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck very tightly and will not come out for any reason, then apply tartar to the wound, as I have told you; then treat the animal until they are safe.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is reinserted into the body of the animal when you cannot see it, and the arrowhead has all its points; and if you feel it, and the bowstring is not suitable for drawing; and if you cannot pull out the arrow because of the tightness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there are no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then feel the pain as long as the wound is great; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears with what they hold onto, if you take off the nail that is stuck into II parts of the muscle which you can reach, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be subtle so that you do not break the arrow, but instead pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it once, if the blood is spilled until the vein enters its opening, then take care, because extracting it is an ordeal.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If those who have the same disease do not get cured when you follow what we said in this chapter; and you guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and apply as much care as you can to treat the arrow wound without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to how he was before the arrow got stuck, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then put him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow comes from another part where it pierces something or the skin is inflamed directly if you see or feel it, then put on that size again, until the shears can take hold, and then pull it out: if now it has come loose.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand around it completely, until it enters the bone, and then widen the bone, then pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it will not come out, if you leave it alone again, and then continue the extraction until it comes out; and if an arrow is lodged in the wound, pour out its contents; and if it's full of pus, administer poultice, so that you apply a head instrument with a pointed tip; and then pour, and if the arrow is covered by hair, pour again into the hair of the instrument, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is touched, if it is deemed necessary to copy all the flesh around where the vein is located, so that you can, then treat the wound as it seems fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	In case of an arrow shot to the belly or intestines, or to the bladder or groin, and it is close to the surface, cover over it, if it is covered; and protect the vein and nerve, and then draw it out, and then sew the wound, when necessary; and the cure until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the clamps used to treat arrow wounds are similar to an eagle's beak, and look like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: great, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the bow that presses the hair is like the feathers of a bird, to press against the tip of the arrow, as it looks like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pliers for pressing and stitching if there is:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Veins that bring health are XXXI in number, because there is XVI, namely: Two branches after the ears, which are called the "dull herbes"; and two arteries in the two temples appearing; and two veins where two cartilages of the two eyes, which are called "aspirers"; and one vein near the forehead; and one vein on top of the nose; and two jugulars around the neck; and two veins above the lips, which are called "augeherich", and those below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that bring health are five in each arm: One is the cephalic, and it's located on the left side of the shoulder, and they call it "vein of the head" among the common people; and the middle one is called "fast", and it's composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is located on the right side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the belly", and it's above the diaphragm, and that one brings health, which opens clearly in the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The arm vein is the one between the auricular and anular, and it has two blood vessels; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: the first one is below the wing-shaped pouch on the left side of the chest, and the second one is located near the ankle bone on the right side of the body; and the third vein which is called “nasse” is located in the other ankle.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins behind the ears help with old cathartics and migraines; and the quality of this vein is as I told you, so that you lift the head of the patient, and rub the cloth on the veins which are rough; then tighten the patient's neck with a rope until the two veins appear behind the ears in two opposite directions: if they do not move, and you feel your pulse under your nail, it is a sign to go further; then take a lancet, and push it through below the vein against the bone; then lift your hand up all along the vein, and strike and cut both the skin and the vein well two times so that you see blood; then strain and tie, until they are healed; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Instruct the patient that if they have two arteries in the temples, and inflammation of the ancient sode, and obtalmie accustomed, and a lump on the eyes; and the qualities of the sickness are like what I say: and it is that the patients strain their necks, until both veins open completely; and feel pain under their skin, and then pull out; then lift the vein up to the neck index point, and cut with the lancet downward, and lift the vein upward, and strike, as you have done in two other veins, and perform the puncture according to your need; then free the patient, and place the neck on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then close it, and let it heal until she is healed; and what we have said about their piercing and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sickness of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the sickness of the head with old face diseases, and with emigraine, and with redness; and the qualities are such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and lean it up from your hand, or from another thing, and let the blood come out according to how much you see; then set the patient free, and tie the vein until it is healthy and there is no more bleeding.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	But it is not good if the stitches are too thick; and the healing twisted, because the bone is close by, and perhaps breaks the stitches when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The sick of the two veins that are in the two joints if they are aided with the eyes, and the tendons, and the redness, and the swelling, and the boils, and their qualities of their sickness so is that the patient twists his neck from any link, just as before; then he heals, and it is the healing through a hole, a little long, a little wide, because there is no point of char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the swellings are subtle, by chance they break; then do quick cuts on the wound, as much as you have need, and then bind up tight, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The sickness of the vein at the neck so is equal to an ague, and a severe fever, and face diseases, which cause inflammation and redness that comes on the face, especially when it is old; and their qualities are such that the patient twists his neck, then twists his neck with your left hand, and takes the thin flame long, and strike it into the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well in this place, and the pain will begin now to come; and do not go too fast, make cuts on the wound as needed, then bind it one night, because it is very soon restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The patient with the second gouty complaint will be aided by the narrowing of the vein, and at the beginning of massage, and with a great many ailments, and empetigine, and corrosion, and herpes, and istiomenes; and the qualities of the complaint are that the patient takes away his neck apart from both sides, as we have said; and when the master is standing over the head of the sick person, and the patient sits on one side, then they heal the vein by a long cut slightly, then pull out the wound temperately, or until it seems best; then do another thing in the other vein, then untie the bandage, and restrain both veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke; and leave him just as he is in the morning, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the cleansing of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of the veins of the liver above so helps to break down in the mouth, and to corrupt the gums, and splits in the lips, and does not heal well.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the cleansing of the veins if is to have the patient sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I said; then turn the liver, and look at both veins, one being on the right side of the liver and the other on the left, which can be recognized by their color and the small black vessels within them: strike then both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, strike the larger of each one, and do the same for both veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the inflammation of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	If the inflammation of the veins is on the tongue, it is helped after the inflammation of the head, and it's through the tightening of the throat, and with diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and if you cut the quality to heal so that the patient feels between your hands in front of the sun, and lift the tongue, and look under each side a vein black: then heal both one and the other, and do not go too deep, because under are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that are cut according to common healing methods are done in two ways: either by piercing all the inflamed area with a thorny myrtle large, or olivaire subtle like the thickness of nails, and they are called "anesil"; and they are thick and thin according to the size and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame is like a mirror so it is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the vein on the flat cheek of a large amount of bloody pus and that contains a great deal of blood and trouble, and this is the form of the flame olive tree.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle in point, and is to heal the small veins subtlety, or where there are subtle bloody spots.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The balsam of the basilic, which is one of these veins, greatly helps with diseases in the throat, and on the neck, and on the breast, and in the abdomen; and it is fitting for a master that he heals quickly, and that he warms from the artery under.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If it touches the artery and bleeding comes out, if he must stitch again, as I have said; and should not be pinching the flame, but cut like a slaughterman.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic is not opened manifestly, if he must be extracted, and change another one; or you do not want any rain on it, or you heal in place of it the vein that has come into the arm: it opens manifestly. And cut at the flame like a slaughterman, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the vein of the wound, then so too must you extract the arm, touching the place until you know the pulse; then sign the mark with encaustic, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein at the flame like a slaughterman. And be careful not to cut the artery when you see the vein swollen, for that is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it protruding in the same way as the urine of an infant, and if they are pale and subtle, know that there is no artery: hurry then, put on your doily long, then take off your doily if they are not stained, for this has happened many times; tie up your arm, and leave it so, and do not move the sick one; and be cautious, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If they are not stained, and if they faint, and the medicine is not present to them, cut the artery if it opens, for the head of the retreating part; stain them.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a strip of thistle and puncture it, and take one half and tie it well to the other half tomorrow; if they are not stained, this is good; if not, if you do as we have said, apply the powders that stain blood; for the staining is not harmful for those who are dying from small bleeding due to the little size of the wound, and the power of the tied arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The patient of the vein must be treated in such a way that he is cured from the pain on top and bottom, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic blood, as we have said; and it is necessary to the master that he warms for the nerve below, and if he presses too much into the bone, and cuts the nerve, and it swells and the sickness worsens, and by chance, it cannot be healed; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in anyone at all because of its subtlety, it is necessary to clean the sainement with the instrument again; and take care of the skin as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has veins between the two nerves, so that they are cut to the long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The pain of the cephalic vein is treated so that it is cured from the top and eyes are aided; and it is necessary to heal in the pointed at the flame of olive or at the flame of myrtle, because this is the most saved of all veins, for there is no below the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Every time, it is advisable to seek the lighter method first, and do not worry if you must try it for the first time, and then start again; and by chance, it may swell in some people before trying it, but it will not hurt.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the cut depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that healing should not be done for the sake of healing alone, but to preserve health and prevent diseases from coming; and let it be done in one of the three veins: cephalic, radial, or basilic; and should be done at the beginning of prayers on a Friday, and after eating in autumn and winter, when the sign of fullness appears; and should be done on the first day or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick person who is being treated does not have a fixed hour or time determined for his illness, but rather when the need arises to visit him every day and at all hours and in every season; and it should not be necessary to heal children before the age of 14, nor women carrying after only four months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not attempt to heal those who are over 60 years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be healed in some manner, if they wish to purge their intestines with a light purgative, if they have much flatulence retained, so that the veins do not carry out the superfluous pus and cause harm to the principal members; nor does he heal properly who is too fat from eating meat, or who is ill with fever, as long as it is so, or dropsy. And if one wishes to be healed after a bout of colic, vomiting, and intestinal degeneration, and many times lying with a woman, traveling, watching, and working, then subtilize the humors, first without fatness, by foods and drinks and medicines; since they have lost their power; then take a bath, if no other thing is forbidden, to subtilize the sickness, and be healed of the vein in three days after the third day, as we said; and beware that day of work, point, luxury, and similar things; and be gentle and kind, and let the doctor heal higher than anyone else, and rub his arms twice or three times, then tie the ligament at the midpoint, because when it is too tight or loose, he cannot correct it without; and then rub him with oil as hands, until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the suture with the flame of a little old oil, then put on his own thumb nail on that vein below the elbow when he wishes to heal, so that the vein does not burst or fail to do its duty.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow just like strings to the healer, and such as are filled with windiness, so that when you put on the flame, it retracts again and cannot open the vein, and thus is done for those; and if you cut the vein, then the wound is too narrow, because of this they must be advised by healers in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, then again take a little from under or above that place, since the veins are inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed, and the patient fears, then let him rest for one or two days, and do not tie the arm: by chance some abscess may form; neither go into the bath, then re-start the treatment as it pleases; and if the swelling is small, carefully make a cut under it with subtle movement, in case it does not burst so much as you see, for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swollen limb, do not start again with the dressing, and apply a little bit of oil upon it, for it alleviates the body from pain, and is moistened by the oil; and thus to administer the oil in each wound that you treat, to quench the flow of blood; and this same method is applied and bowels are also treated when one puts it on the limb; so subtlety must be used and spareness, when it becomes too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes in, which often happens when it cannot be treated only at those times when the vein is cut open, quickly take action and apply a moist sponge soaked in water and wool a little hot, and hold for an hour; and it is fitting that you do this after the blood flow from the vein has stopped, and if it remains on the limb after some days without any harm or benefit, then it will not be beneficial; and if you see, apply some aloes or mirror dissolved in vinegar, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times happens an abscess and appearance at the opening of the basilica vein: then put your hand on it, and if you find the bone hard under pressure of the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then that you do not put anything on what we have said, for by chance cutting without the artery; but make it dry and cool first to harden the bone, then cure with another cure until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And apply to each person according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is not black, then let it breathe out until it becomes red; and if you see a big one, let it breathe out until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for him who is robust and strong, and has need of blood extraction, to make a larger wound and wider flaps; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and he will recover more quickly and often, and must be healed by cutting across, not piercing; and this manner of healing is safe from the deterioration of blood and the bruising of nerve, and it is better than having the wounded long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him who needs the blood to be cut, it is fitting to give moist pain in juice of green grapes; if he is heated, cut twice or four times; and if he has a cold complexion, mix before the wound pain moist in syrup mulled, or in aromatic syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if the palm holds the wound, after a great amount of blood has been lost, it is fitting that he drink broth made from cheese and sweet syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open the vein on one arm and cure himself again, it is fitting that when he is weakened by great blood loss, he heal little by little, according to the continued quantity of his virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to open the vein on one arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong pulse, will recover in 7 hours after the first bleeding, or within an hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to cure himself on the other side, if he should have to cure himself on the second day or on the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, and fait venir fievre;
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein has been cut away, so let it remain and do not bind it tightly, until the abscess is closed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If a second wound needs to be treated with the same treatment as before, in the same vein or in another vein.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is closed in place of the vein at the head, because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of closing the wound, if it is that the patient pours their hand in hot water, until the swelling is red; then bind loosely, so that the vein appears well, and now close the wound from the inside, neither too large nor too narrow; and apply large poultices, and treat them well near the joint of the hand, and if it does not come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the swelling drain into the water until you have enough; and if this is so, do not put the hand back in hot water again, because they put more on in a fever than in an inflammation; and the closure of this vein is more safe than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sickness of the saved hand is worth all the other diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and pour in hot water, until the vein opens, if it can be seen; and if it is opened at an angle, and you copy it to the whole limb, do not harm anything; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are now all dried out from the char, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the wound is not frozen in the flesh, and it will come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have applied to the wound as much as necessary, put oil and sinew on the vein to sew up hastily, and do so for every cut.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness of the vein in the left hand is worth the disease of the mouse, and do it just as I told you over to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the liver is worth all kinds of diseases of the body, just as illnesses from the marrow, and retention of flowers, and illness of the kidneys, and joints, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its liver are such that when patients put in stones into hot water and rub on the vein until it dies, and place above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and through above the foot they take out a lot of blood; then healing takes place, but only if you go bigger or wider than the ankle, or to the foot.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal on the foot, then beware of the swellings that are under it, and the healing by piercing through as when cutting. So let the fumes be made.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If he cannot come out from it, so put his foot in the water, and let well drain the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	If the veins require the first time, if he restarts it on the top a little because they are salty; do not doubt of the nerves, as we have said, and do so for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the groin are in the heel of force, and its cutting is worth pain of the hamstring when it's for blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the quality of its cutting is such that the patient takes or bathes in it, and you strain over the heel 4 times in twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open; and when it opens, cut in all ways that you can, and in crossing; and be sure to copy it, because the veins are swollen, and they return like the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find it, then your body will be weakened by any rain or pain from the head or lower back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and do as much care for the wound so that you see, and then release the bandage, and put cotton on and tighten; now she is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of venous issues
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	They are made of horns, or thorns, or needles; and venous constriction is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing out the wound, or by piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this venous constriction done by piercing is in two ways: either it is all fire, or on fire; and the venous constriction that is made by piercing and extracting the wound is done in 13 places of the body, for one is at the top of the head, one near the neck, and two more on each side of the neck; and the venous constriction below the chin; and below the shoulders; and above the elbows; and above the knees; and between the two arms; and between the two legs; and between the two ankles; and it does not treat the wound, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the body, which weakens no one, as we do with venous bleeding; and it should not be made in any case of overloading, but only when all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of sickness it is convenient to ventouse, or out of custom, we bring each one every hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and at each time; because there are those who, when they need to ventouse, have a heavy head; and such as experience redness and inflammation on their face, and head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have pulled out the tongue, and swollen with it; and there are those who see, or feel pain, and death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and myself when it is time for the month, we command to be ventoused after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sick person of the mouse should be treated in the warmth of the chest … so that comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this is done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the sainie of the cephalique, and it is not fitting for those who have hot complexion or who are suffering from catarrh, because this causes great harm; and therefore do not use the vigilance, nor who have a cold head with illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become blind, and therefore it is fitting to apply the venous suction a little lower by the examination of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The venous evacuation in the neck is in place of the sainie of the head and the basilic, and therefore it is fitting to apply the tightening of the belly, and cutting of the channel of the pommon, and touching, and repletion; and it should not be pressed too much, because if it holds too tightly, it causes blindness or stomach or bowel obstruction.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The patient has two costelz (shoulder blades) close to the col (neck), so it causes pain in the chest, head, eyes and migraines, and strangling, and there is pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in place of the suffering of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the healer to express his hand when applying, so he does not cut the artery, and does not wait for the blood to flow afterwards.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cutting in the lower part of the chin causes mouth diseases and corruption of gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and is in place of the suffering of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cutting on the shoulder blades causes disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cutting on the shoulders is as much to be feared as cutting three veins in the arm, because it brings out blood from these large veins; and instruct the healer that he should not pierce too deeply, for the skin of these areas is thin, and knows its nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling on the flank is valued at the groin and in the belly, and it is necessary that the swelling be great and of sand, for it needs to be treated well; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and it causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings on the legs are treated openly because they attract blood from all over the body, and value themselves at ancient pains of rain, mares, and bladder, and bring forth flowers; and in place of the two knees and two shins, they weaken the body after a long time, and cause fainting in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the swelling is that you first fill it, and tie it temporarily, and move it equally, and do not cease to do this until you see the body swell red and inflamed, and draw out the red from the wound; then again, put back the swells, and take care in the disposition of the body, because there are many who have turned pale, and you should be wary: if it happens only once, it is best to do so; and it is necessary to make large wounds, and deep ones too; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the lump is small, so it must be injured twice: once to make subtle the way of the large vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not very thick, so it must be injured a third time: and when we tend to the vein little by little, we suffer only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we tend to the vein much, repeatedly start again; and if it is not thick, then pierce deeply: and when the ends are reached, so that the keys can be perceived suddenly, cut at him who has a large skin and hard, and those with hairy pores, that you anoint them with the oil of the perforating ventouses, and dissolving; either violet oil, or almond sweet oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it's in yvew, then of cresson, lily, camomile, or another similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is great and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or balsam, or anise oil.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if those with skin that is sensitive and large pores, should not be put on oil, but should be washed after the application of rose water, or cold water, or grapevine juice, or cucumber juice, or other similar waters.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture, lift him up from the cold, or from the water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those with great swellings lift him up from old wine, or cold water, or the decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things. And they should not be sutured after bathing nor in a bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and he should not sleep afterwards, because he must be sutured and when he is sutured.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And instruct him who is recovering to take cold things, such as pears, grapes, and lettuce, as easily as possible, and similar things; and eat small meat, and cheese from the chest, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should take honey syrup and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, eat little, and eat small meat, fish, pigeons, and plums; and on the day he will recover, he must drink more than he eats; and it is fitting to give some men honey twice a day or after recovery, for comfort of the principal members; but be subtle about it, not because they are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The poultices that are applied to be heated are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mouse, and podagra, and on the stomach and the boil and the joints and the hamstrings, because these members do not bear to be struck or struck with force, and only for the purpose of attracting the blood from one part to another, as we place poultices on the breasts when they are healthy; to thin out the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put poultices on the stomach and on the boil to ease the member; and take away the pain, when there is swelling or a stone, taking away by its attractive power by chance the swelling or the stone from its place; and thus they are done when one places them on the liver and on the mouse when it has retained poultice, and these poultices are emptied to suck only; and sometimes are applied together with heat, and sometimes plain water, as in the case of painful pleurisy, and in such a manner that we fill the poultice with hot water or with which there have been suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction to apply with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And they have two fingers of length and half a palm from top to bottom, and one finger inside the middle, like inserting an awl, so that it does not prick the patient when placing on the limb; and at the middle has a crossbar of iron or wood, for securing a bandage, with large and small sizes according to the diseases and age of those who take them; because the suction vents of children are different from those of adults, and thin ones than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus you must put this suction on the limb: wrap the wax string or linen around it, and place it inside the suction through the crossbar in the middle of the suction, so that the light shines at the bottom of the suction and does not burn the patient; then place the suction on the limb, with the two fingers above the opening we previously mentioned, so that when you take it out, the vapor escapes, and remove the suction; wrap linen around as before, and replace it frequently, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the treatment of the chest disease called pleurisy, when you are full of pain, there is no joint or swelling and it does not become painful unless it is placed on a limb alone, and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Unless swellings occur in members, for it is not possible to put pouces on a thin skin such as lips and gums, or similar ones; and when you take out the discharge from a nose, if there are two or one, and others like them; and the quality of use so that when you find swellings that are in clear and clean water without injury, take them; and put a net in clear water until they become accustomed and have nothing in their stomachs; and then be taken away from vein and pouce, then rub the member until it is red, and place on swellings; and when they are full and swollen, if it can be put on pouces again, put them on, for this is very valuable afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If that is not so, then lift the limb out of its binding, and then into water, very well, and then warm it up; and if the limbs are healthy too soon after the removal of the bandages, moisten with a linen cloth in cold water, and put on, until the swelling subsides; and if many swellings multiply, put on vitriol crushed or vinegar, and similar things, until they subside; or you should put on one-eighth of boiled peels, and let them sit on the limb, so that now it will be stanched; and if you have more need, then take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the bandages do not come away, then rub the limb with fresh salt, or prick it with a needle until the blood comes out, and then put on the bandage; and as soon as they feel the wound, they will dry up; and when you see them weeping, then sprinkle some powder of aloes and millet flour or ashes, so that they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of fractures begins
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the art of this chapter is unknown to any of the ancient books, nor have we read them in letters; and because of this, the knowledge of our land has been lost, for I found none that were good; and I know nothing, except by the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated it, and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described here what is contained in this chapter, and have abridged it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the wounds that must be treated, as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in this prologue of this book the explanations and the chapters where the wise men put their understanding, and take care to explain it further, so that those who have learned from experience know and learn this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When a fracture or dislocation or twists or swelling comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the sick person from one side and the other, if no remedy is available, for weakness of body, or sickness, or old age; or if the joints are very tight, or too cold; and attend chills caused by cold, namely frosty stools, and charred meat of bird and deer, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty foods, and do not stuff oneself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about an abscess or swelling in the joint, or the spread of matter to a member; if you return to the previous treatment for the sick person who has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore itself, it is fitting that you nourish the patient with foods that cause great swelling, if they have viscosity, such as bread cooked in water, and cheese, and eggs, and butter, and pancakes, and fish fresh from the river, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	But swelling causes more representation of wounds and the break occurs faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old people and decrepit ones cannot be well mended or soldered according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those who are too soft, like the bones of little children; but there is no cure. Reinforce the broken bone with large splints which secure and join the member together, so that it will heal as it was before; and do not neglect its work, for this is why they must nourish themselves with great foods, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or thigh, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur at the neck, and others from cutting, just like the length of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with a small split or crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type has its own method and proper instrument for treatment, according to what the memory recalls in its place; and it is known that fractures of bone are recognized by this: that the limb is twisted, and the joint is open due to movement, and feels near the touch of the hand; but when there is no twisting or kinking, and the patient does not feel great pain, unless there is a fracture; yet it can still have twisting, splitting, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not good to move the fingers at all, but apply the medicines that come after this, and then pull it now subtly.
