Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And when the fracture in the arm exists and are two parts dislocated, it is now necessary to set them equally, so that the abscess comes; and if an abscess forms there, leave no day, until the abscess is calmed down; then set it at ease with the bone that you can easily set straight, and know that the restoration of this part is lighter than that of which it has pieces; then pull, as seems good after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, when extending two parts, it is so with hands or a piece, or with small members, or with two cords, or one cord and a hand; and set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb are cut short, then pull back all the additions in their places on the bone, as you can, and take care that through your work there does not come to the patient an injury or pain; and adjust well both joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not good: if the dressing is made well and not too tightly constrained, nor pressed as those do who make it come by their own work, a hot contraction and stiffness of the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set straight, instruct the patient well that it does not move, neither while he watches nor when he sleeps, nor when he turns or in any other way; and be sure that the limb is so securely fixed that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	Because when he feels no pain, it is not set straight, and you must put him in such position that he feels no pain; and be sure to keep it properly aligned so that tortuous movements do not occur when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The broken limb is of various size, shape, and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small members like arms and hands, one should wrap a soft cloth around with glue; and for larger ones like thighs and legs: one should wrap it with a wide and hard rope, because the large ropes encircle the entire limb and tighten it equally on all sides, without any slack. Then tie tight over the joints lightly, three or four times according to the size of the member, and press your hand into the middle of the knot so that the rope becomes more snug; then go up towards the break and tighten less, until the break starts to move a little; then soften the rope little by little, as much as you can get out from under the limb's healthy part, then put on another rope, and turn it back over to the limb's break; then go down to the lower part of the break, and tighten moderately, not too hard nor too soft, as we have said in the first rule above; then insert cloth or drapes between the ropes until they are all equal, then tie everything from above with a bandage, and then put your stitches well-made on top, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it has a swelling or abscess, put an absorbing dressing over the abscess, and apply heat to relieve the swelling; then release the swelling after some time. Then strain on your joints, and tie with a gauze bandage of moderate width, using wood from which clivuses are made, or palm fronds, according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is advisable that the bandage you put on the break should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and so long as it suits the limb of smallness or largeness; then tie on your joints just as you did at the first binding; then wrap above with a thread made from flax, not too thick nor too thin, but soft linen; for if the thread is too thick, like I have wanted to make works of the foolish ones who make their bindings with corded linen threads, and it's a great error, because the binding can't be equal if it's too subtle, and it cannot fit that there should be less space between each joint than two fingers' width.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is weak from the pains of the arrows after the straining in their safe place, then put stoppers made of linen or wool on them, so they will not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will tell you the cure as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not good to strain the arrows every member at once, the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the members are large, it is not good to put arrows on every member at once, but rather after five or seven days, or longer according to your safety and a cure previously made; and here is how the ancient plastermakers used to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that is kept in the walls of the mill, mix it with a lot of wine, and make this concoction, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, for this is the common way of using the plaster to restore fractures in many cases, especially women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to treat plastering the fracture and dislocation and twisting: take 2 handfuls of starch and lard and honey and alum and gum arabic and myrrh, an amount equal to the size of X; mirror and aloes, an amount equal to V; alechil VIIII; and make powder, and mix with a mixture of honey and vinegar; if the complexion of the flesh is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores the broken bones quickly, and saves many lives.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to treat plastering that is good for twisting: take myrrh and vismalve, an amount equal to the size of X; mirror and aloes, an amount equal to VIIII; acacia VI; boric Armenian X, grind well, and confit with water or a mixture of honey and vinegar, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to splint is to join and wrap the bones and to fix their limbs, and to soothe the pain that follows, and use the bone to cut and break the fracture: take new linen, apply a poultice in ease and in oil cooked, and put on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore the health, but they are good for soothing an abscess.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to splint that restores the broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth leaves, crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to splint for restoring the break of the bone and for easing the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of sallow (willow), camomile, flowers of violets, flour of vinegar, one part from each; and crush, and mix with wine, and apply to the limbs when heated, and mix with moist coriander water, or just water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to apply plaster more strongly than the first, when an abscess is formed on the restored limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of willow, and seeds of flax, balsam, meadowsweet, and sanctejuice, and flowers of violets and camomile, one part from each; and crush, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, there is no place to put a broken limb for repair so that the salve made of wax and oil is applied, and nothing else, and he says it should be between too soft and too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that you must put a broken limb on, to restore, things dry with a little hot, just like myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat an injury and pain: take mallow and horse chestnut, or pigeon feathers, and vinegar, and cut them equally, and grind them, and make a plaster with the paste and the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then wait a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor does he bruise his bone again; if it does not happen by hands, but if pain comes to the limb, whether it prurites, inflames, or swells, you must act quickly, and remove it, and now apply a plaster; and take light bandages, and a sponge soaked in moist water, and plunge into the water, and lift up the limb until the itching ceases and the pain is soothed; then let rest the limb for an hour, then put on a dry linen cloth, moistened with vinegar or rose oil, and tie it up with a bandage, until you are sure of the bone being set; and rest the inflammation in the limb, and soothe away the pain, then resume subtle dressing, and a little plaster, but do not press too hard as before; and proceed subtly until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess is red and swollen and painful and inflamed, I have a bone that has been broken into all of them, and you must apply plaster and tie it up again, as you did first when it was even.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the member anything of what we have said, if you do not untie it after three days or four or five, but rather leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the break heals and the surrounding bone approaches; then hold back a bit more than before, and let the flesh swell again, as I told you earlier; and if you see that it dries up more than necessary, know that there will be no recovery. Therefore, do not cut off the swelling from the member, but rather apply hot water to it every time you untie it, and let it dry on its own for three days, then cut off the swelling with the wound; this is bad, and it leads to painful recoveries, and I see nothing else than lacerations and wrong healing.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of different kinds of breakage
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of breakages, and various forms, and the causes are determined; for there is a breakage that is caused by the percussion of a sword, and the collarbone (colz oste) breaks all the way through to the bone just beneath it, as if struck by a blow or thrust with force; and this kind of breakage is called «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes the bone from above and pierces it, this kind of breakage is called "absolute"; and there are two kinds of wounds resulting from these breaks: great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has been pierced by a blow that has embedded itself, or is a fracture, or of the collarbone on stone, or of the shoulder on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a persistent fracture, which approaches the tendon that is under the bone, or above the bone, and is this wound big or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is closed in the bone with a subtlety like that of our sewing, and there is a small fracture, and because of this it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound was made by hitting the stone, or falling, or some similar thing, and the piece of bone entered inside, and its ends are as thin as those of the coppersmith when he heats them on the copper pot, then something gets stuck.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have moist bones under their head, like that of an infant; and it occurs in all these kinds of fractures where small pieces are separated as if from stones; and I will speak on behalf of them.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by removing them from under them, and the inquiry has tested them, and by the corrupting fire that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like resemblance is known because when the bone has been discovered and the surface is rubbed upon, if it opens the fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be careful for any accidents in the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, extension, palsiness, fever, and the eyes are forced out and become red, and other similar symptoms more than usual, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any extraordinary accidents, and you hope for recovery, as soon as you begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when you come first to me, and it's in winter, it is fitting to withdraw the bone before the eighteenth day after the moon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in this state, so hastening to withdraw the bone before the seventh day, and thus making the flesh underneath the bone corrupt, and bringing on the accidents that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just next to the covering of the brain, it is fitting that you cut through the broken part thus: and when you take the head from the patient's hand, and uncover above the bone in all ways as you can, and on the shape of the wound so soft as you can, and if blood comes to uncovering the bone, or an abscess, then he needs what is necessary, and it is that you fill the hollow with moist drapes soaked in olive oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed, and be sure of no further bleeding; then start cutting under the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you copy the shape before the narrow cutting, and it's like this:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then after a second more extensive cutting than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have to cut with multiple tools of various sizes, some small and others large, pointed or flat, made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to hit the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is advised that you pierce through it, so that with tools you administer cuts with sharp edges, not by striking only once but repeatedly, lest the point go beyond the softness of the bone; and on the edge of the cutting tool, leave a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and have multiple tools, one for each joint, so that you cut through all bones with sharp edges; and this is the form of the three types of cuts:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	In the case of piercing through bone that is broken, put it there for a little while on the bone, and turn to your two sides until you know that the bone has been pierced; then put the tournure elsewhere after a little while, and do this all around, and afterwards cut at the incisures the space between the parts, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you take out the bone with your hand, or on one of the things that you have in such as pliers, nails; and be careful not to touch the brain or the skull.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut out the bone, if there is still some part that remains attached to the bone, but it cannot be removed with any other instrument like an incisor, it is better to make it more thin and subtle than the others; and if no small bones or scales remain, then take them lightly away from the instruments; afterwards cure the wound as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And other types of treatment are thus said by the Galenians, which is more so; and the oath is very strong, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone, at that place or where the fracture opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you put under the lower edge of this cut-out lens-like structure, because it is in this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut into one part, and the damaged part is on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then with a small hammer on top, so that you carefully copy the bone all around, and take care well of protecting yourself from the cloth below; if it is rough against the bone, carefully remove the bone, because removing the bone causes harm, and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the break of the bone is not pierced until just after the cloth, and the bone is hit only from above, with small pieces, it will cover again that roughness, and remove the scales at the subtle raspener which you must have different quantities for, in order to give to each one the most comfortable treatment, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have many coarser rasps and after more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary measurements and subtle fractures, it is necessary to treat according to its address; and this is a thing that no one can reply to he who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the syphilitic is uncovered, it is necessary to apply linen bandage according to its size, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another bandage doubled twice or thrice, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it over the first one; and do this more lightly than you can, lest you burden the syphilitic, and apply from above another binding, and do not tighten it too much until the wound is only soothed; and leave it for one or two days, until the abscesses are eased, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lion's root, flour of vermillion, incense powder, and ars alba, and similar things; and make a powder and apply it to the wound, and administer after-wards medicines with mastication, lest the pain be increased, for when bowels are assembled above the cloth of the brain, they will be corrupted and cause great malice in the patient; because when something mordant is applied on top of the syphilitic, it festers under it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Preventively then, if no accidents occur to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful in its presence of doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come through fire only because of the medicine that we have placed on it, which has virtue, then it is fitting to take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and in glue I wrap, and I place it on the wound; then apply the treatment of cures as needed, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two forearms are often broken in two pieces, or one piece alone, for these are two bones; and this below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is fractured or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two pieces is broken, it is fitting to put your little bone or piece of the nail into that break, and place it inside your finger joint, and in the pouchet (wrist) for safety, until the nail grows back according to its natural figure; and do this gently, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is in the upper part of the arm and it cannot be straightened, so that you put equal to the head of a stick one foot thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the fracture is in two parts, do it again and hurry to restore the first day if you can; but if not, after seven or ten days, when the abscesses are closed, then bind to the head of the bone with linen strips, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you bind the other part, if there is a fracture; and the linen strips are so thick that they fill up the holes of the bone.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said any restorer that you should moisten the linen in butter and move each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but it is likely that they are moist in the making of both wheat and powder of millen; then leave the tent, until the bones are hard, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And in no case do not put on or on nails of goose in its place, and if it is cold wrapped around, and holds the wound, and blows the patient with air; then see how you look.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working, apply a clot or cotton soaked in oil rose, or in one half of vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come, apply plaster beforehand, made from wheat flour, and powdered incense, mixed with wheat flour; then put on light stoves, and do not tie the nose; and if the wound at the nose is small, and it breaks into little pieces, then extract the instruments suitable for this, and cut the incision, and apply bandages, and ointments convenient for this; and if there is no injury inside the nose, apply the treatment of tents, and put plints in place, until he is cured.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the removal of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is removed below, and there is no wound to be found, and the fracture is absent except for swelling alone, without bruising in the marrow, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side, that you put your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left jawbone, put your index finger of the right hand, and insert the fracture gently, while holding back with the other hand, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is on both sides (II), it is necessary to administer an extension of II parts, so that it may be even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth have come about, or rotting, then tie up with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put on the broken mandible a hot cloth; and put on double drapels; and put on one large stethal well made, or piece of leather equal long and wide according to the mandible, and bind it above the muscle that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light viands.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, if you release it to four days, and then put back to its original shape; and apply plaster upon, with powder of mill ground with abundant oil or flour of sesame, after that which you have oiled the hot cloth; and apply the plaster linen lightweight, and when the plaster cools, and the patient's disposition does not change, let it remain so long as they are well. Many times they are well in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscessed foot comes, as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and a wound together, repair the no small piece of bone that is protruding; for such subtlety in the removal of the bone is useful to those.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then expand it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all those pieces of bone, and there is no remaining part, then dress the wound, if it is large, and put on suitable bandages to bind well, so that it may be healed.
de la forcele	of the fistula
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fistula breaks multiple times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and displaced twice, with fragments, and this is lighter to restore; or there is a fracture with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the surgeons are thus when the break is near an injury, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the aid with the feeling of the broken bone; and the other extends the arm towards the part; then put equal the break to your two hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there be no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have need to further extend, put on the patient an iron sphere of cloth or linen, round about the shoulder, so that it is as large as your necessity requires; and gently stretch the feeling, and hold tight the sphere with your hand, so that you put equal the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot treat the head of the feeling, because it comes into the very marrow, it is fitting that the patients lie on their hateful bed, and put under the shoulder a soft pillow, and have the ministers pour water down the back, until the bones of the feeling are raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the break to your two feet, and if you find any debris, it is advisable to cut them up; and take out the pieces lightly, and if the bones cannot join together for any swelling, if one of the incisors cuts through, but put on the forceps this instrument, in order to ward off the splinter:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not hair, and be as large as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, just like the roughness of the wound that you made when you broke the bones; and when you are sure that there is a large abscess, if the wound is small, or you doubt a large abscess, then apply the dressing of cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If a swelling comes upon the foot, so moistens the cloth in rose oil and in ash and in wine, and puts it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is filled with pain and swelling, is to put on the bone dressed with powder from the mill of flour and honey, and place light cloths over it, and if necessary, place a spear beneath; then take a great bandage of one palm in width, and place two cloths double on top of cloths, and the dressing; then take a fine needle three fingers thick and long, and pass it through the center of the bandage so that the head of the bandage is hanging; and put the needle over the break, and turn the bandage over the shoulder, and under the jointed limb; and pull each part, and when you see that the limb holds the break immediately, and you see clearly that the needle does not move above the broken bone, then reward each day, and when the ligament is stretched, bind it again; and have the patient lie on his back, and put a little oil below the joint, to lift the assistant up; so will alleviate the break of the shoulder by the tension of the shoulder blade, or you tie the arm to the collar, and do not untie if bad accidents come about, for twenty days; then reapply the dressing, if you see that it needs it, and bind and leave it thus, until he is restored; and she is restored in twenty-eight days, and less often than at other men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder breaks or becomes crooked, as long as it remains in place, and does not move because of pressure; if you appear according to the figure of the break, and straighten it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the patient powder from the mill with much oil and light strokes, and make a double bandage; then put on a large and subtle needle, one inch larger than the shoulder, and remove any hair at a point of the shoulder so that the needle enters smoothly, cutting through linen threads evenly; and then bind it tightly with a strong bandage, so that the needle does not move from its place, and inspect each bandage every day; whenever it loosens, rebind, and set the needle equal to itself, if it has moved out of its place, and relieve the patient on their chest; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, release it, and be sure, for it is not that the bone has entered easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and not below the level, then they do so, and put in, the bone, and do what we have said in breaking the abscess of the sharpness.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The piece is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; it breaks often without cause.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it inclines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and shortage of blood, and swelling, and sometimes vomiting blood, and opens up the veins in the broken bone, and the sensation becomes better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on their back, and you place a cloth between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring together the two ribs with your hands, and carefully put them in such a manner as they can be made to fit; then put on plaster casts and bandages over the subtle part of salt, or some lighter substance, and wrap it up in a square piece of cloth, and tie it tightly around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the knot round the back, and tighten it immediately, and reward each hour with a new cast, and if they loosen, you should tighten them; and if it pleases to untie them, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the patient, or pain or abscess, you hasten, and untie, and shave the plaster, and address those who came to visit in ways of cures; then remove the plaster, and bind them until they are sane.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the breast
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Which is that the breaking of the breast comes only from the weight on the large after the back, and in the chest within, and does not happen more because they are bony; and it feels very well when being inquired about the two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are such that you place equal the break, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and tie with a stake, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the breast inclines inward, the patient feels great pain, and point, as well as pleurisy, because the bone punctures the membrane; and they are inflamed with pus, and swollen, and vomit a lot of bloody matter, and it's due to illness, and the old ones have put much effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if to those who say it is fitting to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to ward off the fracture in advance.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless it has come from a source of flesh.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it is from a source, that it be pure.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one should not put poultices on the limb to cause bleeding, and it seems like reason; however, there is doubt that poultices do attract blood in excesses due to the weak state of the body.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the limb with a wet linen in hot oil, and put tourniquets between the ribs to keep the joint even, then either be cured of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain because of the bone which pierces the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is fitting to cut above the broken shoulder blade, and it is necessary to put on some instruments to guard the wound; and therefore one must drill into the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound if they are great, and cure with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the surface, then put moist cloth in oil on the surface of the abscess, and place it; cure until the abscess grows into what it should be on the costal side where it must be, so that it can drain onto the surface, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of a broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No bone ever breaks when the neck is bent, and little has happened when it cracks; and similarly at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens and you don't know if it will be cured or not, if you see that the hands are softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you press with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many types of conditions, and if they are silent and feel well when you restrict them with a point, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will recover from wounds, if they are put on treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you see whether it will be cured or not, take care if the feet are softened, and if accidents are in the hands, and if the vertebrae move suddenly and fall through with voluntary will; and when one has taken notice of his bowels, they make a movement with voluntary will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	When he is swollen on his back and it hurts him, if he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knowing that it is mortal: if one does not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this happens to him repeatedly, then it is the lighter condition.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward him if he has a hot abscess, putting oil of rose or oil of mouse on the spine, until it is appeased; then put on a comfortable and dry plaster, binding it with a bandage, and commanding the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are broken, it is to cover the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble both lips of the wound, if they are great, with a suture, then treat with ointment of juniper, until he is healed; and if the bone is fractured, which is called "broken knee", pour into the pouch of your left hand and put it equal to the right hand, then apply plaster and splint, if necessary; then bind him, and if there is a broken bone, make them up again, remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the femur
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	it happens that the femur bone is fractured, and if it is, then if it has caused only a slight inflammation in the head; and let it be long and curved, and come to the limb, causing the patient pain at the joint, pointing, and swelling as if broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above the fracture, until you are above the breakage; and you see which part is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only in the head alone, then you put an even cast, until it has taken on a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it curves inward, then you make the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture has been prepared.

When you have put it back in place even, then apply plaster, then apply a stake of wood or horn, and bind the break so that it does not move; and apply ointment on both sides of the bone, until it is set straight.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes up in the flesh, do not touch it until it is smoothed out, and apply the plaster as we said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as needed, without any other injury, for this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the arm and the head of the shoulder; and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of two methods. One method is that you take a stick made from the bone marrow in the form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.
