If the fracture is near the shoulder of the shoulder, so that you put a median ligature below the bone, and another to the side of the cut, then it is wise to put the lighter ligature gently under the wound, until the fracture is even on its own, and on the side; then put even the fracture, if possible, and tie it, so that the abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If the abscesses come, do not tighten it just yet for seven years, and put a linen bandage moistened with rose oil, until the abscesses are allayed; then tie it, and take care of the manner of tying it so that you put the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm to the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; put a dressing, and tie tightly on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, if no other thing prevents it, or if the bones are moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone moves, then use a needle, and place a larger and stronger needle than the others on the break one, and insert one inch between each needle, so each needle is as large as it passes through three parts of the break; then strain upon the needles, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter on the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the arrangement of the needles and the straining, as we have said, when you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess, leaving it for seven days, as we have said; then observe each one of three days the link, that inflammation does not set in, or any swelling comes to the limb, where there are signs coming from the needle because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If he is ill, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents happen, he should not be released until three days or more have passed, and the patient lies on his back, with his hands on his stomach, and puts on below the shoulder joint one cussin of plain linen evenly, and observes each hour of the day or night, whether the broken limb moves or is softened; for the patient will become ill by the virtue of medicine, and eat the meat that we have placed before him in this manner, so that the meat is soft at first; and when he comes to take food again, it becomes thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and joint should be treated for forty days in its entirety; therefore, he should be released and given a bath and administered remedies of ointments to relieve his illness.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is swollen and blocked, so it does not open after one or two days.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "forearm" (little bone) and the "humerus" (big bone), for this reason the one that forms the pouch is small, and it is this one; and the other is large, and it is located below, towards the little finger; by chance, only the big forearm was broken or only the small one, and by chance they broke both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small forearms are broken, the restoration is light, and healing; and when the big ones are broken, it is bad healing, and more grievous than when both were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's a broken little finger, they can make it stretch slightly lighter, and put it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If it's a big finger, they must pull it harder; and stretch it up to the wrist, and tighten the pouch of the hand higher than others, so that the small fingers go lower than others, and the patient crosses his own arm on himself, and looks at the same cussin (wrist) more upwards, so that the patient suffers no labor; then extend the two skilled hands to the part below the joint in the hand or at the wrist, one of them on each side.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put it in its proper place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If the break has pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no remaining deviation that can be taken to hold the cure, and it cannot be restored to its proper place, then cut out (remove) the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If there is an injury at the break, I have spoken to the singular healer about it; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration process the abscesses are not present, but glue and cloth made from cerote, oil of roses, and white wax is applied, it should not be too hard or too soft; and bind the cloth gently above, until the abscesses are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerote, and put on the plaster of flour ground with oil, mixed with a lot of water; and make it like an arrow, so that the arrow is set firmly and slightly wider than the others; and notice how many arrows you need, or more: whether the break is in one bone or two; and bind above the break more tightly than elsewhere, and always less when removing, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and make sure the cloths on top of the break are soft and moist, not too hard or harsh; and put in threads, which are strained with linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some evil accidents come to the limb, just as itching comes to the skin of the limb, it is necessary that you warm up the limb with hot water, until the itching is calmed down, and let the limb not be too cramped to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the binding, and if the joints are loosened and the bones deviated, and so similar, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling does not come back to the limb, because it is too strained, then you should loosen it a little, and let it stay that way for some days, until the swelling goes away, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If no such thing happens to the patient as we have said, so that he does not come to injury within 20 years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	wherein he holds his hands to the neck, and if his neck is even, he guards against movement and numbness, and sleeps on his back; and observes that this fracture will be restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps twenty days, according to the composition and nature of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of a hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Observes that on the back of the hand, and near the wrist, there is little fracture, but only a frequent pain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And if the finger of the hand is broken or sprained, it is prudent that the patient should cross his fingers and sit upright in a straight line; then he puts his hand on an extended palm, and extends the jointed bones, and makes them even with the joints, until they are well joined; and he applies plaster and splints, unless there comes any swelling to the abscess; then he sets an arrow according to the quantity of the wound; and so it is taken out in a bandage of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	In case of a fracture in the pelvis near the belly of the limb, make a splint from strips and instruct the patient to bind his broken limb with its own plant; then tie it with a long strip, so that it is as strong as the tendons of the hand, and the binding should be done as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the elbow, so it may be fitting to put a splint above and below in the limb, so that the wrist is straightened and set right, then tie everything together around the hand, and secure the joint between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of us in the two joints, so if it is swollen, make it even, as it may be fitting; and bind with the limb, and if you see that it is necessary to put a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and it does not move; and if the fracture is in other joints, such as in the index or the other one, so also make it even, binding it with the healthy joint that is next; or bind all of them together, whichever seems best, or putting on a splint, as the swelled one may be.
de la cuixe brisie	of the cross breaks
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bones of the cross are often broken and if one sees it when it is being turned in front and behind, and then the restoration is as if you tie the ligament above the break, and also below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients tie their face up with cloth, then each one extends his linen band equally; and this is when the break meets the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the cross, then it is one of the ligaments at the joint and the others are below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, and then it is either one of the ligaments near the joint or extension below; then put the tourniquet on the bone just as much as his two hands can hold it, so that it follows its natural shape, and then apply plaster, and ligament, lest abscesses come from this place.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If it has an abscess hot, then let him calm it down first, and he will return to his work and his cure; the cure is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap a bandage around the fracture for two or three times, and hold off the swelling; then turn the leg so that the toes reach to the root of the nail, and pour one long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the groin, and tie the chief with the thread above; then turn up the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then put stitches on the fracture, and put a stitch on the bone of the leg; then wrap soft cloth between the leg and the thigh to tighten evenly the constraint, then begin to form three or four turns around the fracture; and as you go higher up on the fracture, and less tightens it; then take out two threads that you have poured between the leg and the thigh, and tie three stitches that are above, then return below to the chief of the thread, until you see from under the foot; and if the constraint does not move from its place, then let him be so, but when there comes no more swelling or inflammation, nor any other sign.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is, then the dislocation and address it as we have said many times. And if he has pieces of bone that are caught, then they must be taken out, if possible; and if not possible, then they must be broken and extracted; and the cure should be done as we have said, until he is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is broken so that a stone can be placed inside, as in the shoulder and on the arm; all the time, in this way, the patient does not suffer from a broken bone.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is known that the bone is restored in three days, or less or more, according to the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the wound on the groin.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	The thing is broken near the groin but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	But if it breaks, then it's only a split or an opening, and there is great pain from the wound and the sensation of pain.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by setting equal what is broken into its two parts, until it is assembled then one can move; then put the plaster, and insert an oval needle if needed, and tie it as it should be; then follow all the dispositions we have said for other breaks, like a severe abscess and similar appearance; put on each case what he needs, until he is cured.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	There are two bones in the leg, one called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and every other fracture comes with it when it reaches the arm, and for that reason their restoration is like that of the arm, and all wounds are equal. And if the two bones break together, then turn the leg from all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then straighten them in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bones are broken, then feel great pain, and see it well; and straighten below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And so apply the extension, and set it equal, and tie the wires equally; but beware, if the break is ugly, and there are more pieces, then make the extension smaller and lighter, according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let all of his work be completed, then take two strips of cloth that tie around the leg from the knee down to the ankle; and tie them tight as well. Then wrap them around both sides of the leg and make sure they are not loose in either direction, and so it is fine; and no one should be given more than one strip of cloth around the leg, and if it is clothed, then put it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly do this when there is a break where he has been injured; and move each leg every day to see if there is an abscess or another accident; thus does the cure until he is safe.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the broken bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but at times with the two feet the bones come to a break and do a little damage, and there are only few cases of further damage.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it has broken the bones of the foot and you see these bones overlapping one over the other, if the sick person lays his foot on the ground, just like he wishes to walk, and then puts his foot on the side where the bones are raised, now put your foot on top of the bone so that they align themselves in their place; then apply plaster and poultices under the foot a small pad of two wooden pins, then tie the foot firmly afterwards, and other things which you may need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if you cut the ligament, because you will find the bones in their place, whether they are broken, dislocated, or misaligned.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If it has any broken bones, restore them, as we have said about the bones of the hand; then place a splint on the broken bone according to its length, and so that it is one inch larger, then put this little table under the foot that I have said, and the binding will be done; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then put a splint on each one according to its quantity, wrapped in an I-inch strip of linen, and bind the table under the foot; and while standing above the head of the table, covering the belly of the foot, so that it is held well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other breaks, since we have said them; and heal each accident as is fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of a bone in the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman is broken, if it swells, then incline it to the back of the shoulder, and hold it behind; then fill the bag with the natural juices of the sick person, and put in as much cotton as I have; then tie the woman's bow, and lift the shoulder bit by bit, and then pull out the cotton, until it comes into the opening of the nature, and the bone returns with its stool; and when she wants to urinate, if there is still some cotton, then put it in again, and when she has urinated, take it out, and do this for 7 days or so: and if you see it restored, take a vessel of wool, and tie a string around the perforated one, and pour all the vessel into the nature; then blow into the string tightly, until the vessel is emptied inside: nature will return to the broken bone; then fill with cotton again and leave it for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone at the joint of the arm is broken, or in the woman, so it is reset as we have said about the bone of the hedge; and these close breaks are not hidden from those who apply their study and use, and they attend my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaks signify a greater number of people on the right path of restoration: then so.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the female member is broken, take a goosegut and pour it into the wound; then wrap it tightly around, and let it be for three days or until it is tied up again, and it will quickly heal.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is great, as the bone of the shoulder or the humerus or something similar, that they should be healed immediately, if the healings that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the wound is clean, then apply vinegar to it. If you have no other option, then do it again on the same day, or the next day, unless an abscess appears on the site of the break.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess appears on the site of the break, then leave the restoration for the next new day, until the abscess is healed, and do not touch it or apply it again on the third day or the fourth, lest you will bring about a bad misfortune.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone is broken and appears near the joint uncovered, it would be fitting to put it at a lighter point in your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension is not suited for placing evenly in your hands, then use this instrument which is made of iron, with seven or eight inches in length, and the width is according to the size of the wound; it is the task of the surgeon that he grips three or four fingers on each such cure of a break; and it should be thin and not curved under compression on the limb at your work, and thick in front, and large from the midpoint towards the fore, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And call this "palainche", because it is fitting that the head of the curved bone be placed above the cheekbone of the skull; and blow with one breath until it returns, so that they are even in front and back.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the splints cannot firmly grasp the bone, so that it fits well, then you must copy the head of the bone, as long as the splints have a chance.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot set the bone as we have said, then copy it with an instrument that is suitable for the task, whether cutting or incising, to your best ability; and take back what has remained stuck in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set and the patient feels great pain after, recognize that it's not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is severe or large, and you doubt that greater accidents will occur, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, so it is not advisable to put splints on; but instead, wrap with hard cloth, and tie.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is healing because of what you put on it, and if you apply ointment to healing wounds, just as ointment has tetter (or tetanus) and similar afflictions.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary to move the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is softened and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limbs be covered in such a way that the wound heals quickly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day they trespass and it cannot heal but re-open with bleeding, see if there are small pieces of bone, because you must treat the wound with care, and remove all these unwanted things that make this pain come.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess comes to the joint, or another kind of corruption, it is fitting that you cure it, according to what he writes in his book previously.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens on the limb, like the bone of the shoulder or arm, and other large member bones, do not treat it yourself, because many times death comes from it, but let it heal until it gets well; perhaps it will pass through it after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can, otherwise leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come from the fire
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They come many times after the health of the wound, especially when it is near the joint, and behold what kind of thing is seen in the member; and by chance, the limbs do not take their proper shape.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care of the wound: if it is fresh, then administer medicinal medicines such as aloes, incense, and mirror, and vinegar, and other similar things; and when you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with medicinal wine or with a lot of oil, or with ash, and place them on the wound in suppositories, and tie it well, and do not untie it for days; and then remove it, and repeat another one until the nodules are removed; or you apply a piece of plaster well made; because the properties of the plaster so that it removes all inflammation from the members; and if the nodules have been converted into hardness like stone, and it is needed to be removed, so after the eighth day, and make the swelling apparent; or take away any razor, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	One weak member after the guard
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is restored and stays after the weak members are set in place, but due to many reasons: because one was too tightly bound and not as tightly bound as it should have been; or because there were too many ligatures, and the new movements could not come to the limb; or because of multiple arrow insertions; or because of too great movements, neither in its hour nor otherwise; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you will make the patient eat, and make its body pliable, until there are no more swellings in it; then administer a bath, and give it joy and delight. After that, put poultices on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great swelling to the member, and the arrow shoots out frequently with water, until the swelling comes to an end, and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	If the limb is twisted after healing, and the bone breaks open, and the form of the limb is distorted, there is no cure for its natural condition: do not believe false rumors that say we must break the limb anew; and many have done this in our land, and this treatment is reprehensible, and it comes to great harm, and sometimes death. For if there are knots and torture still fresh, it is best to let them be softened by warm water, or to cook herbs that soften like violets, and roots, and mallow, and similar things; and to apply the softening medicine, as aqua calida has done, and take the muscillagine of violets, and mix it with fat of geline or olive of samient, and let it be softened on it; or take figs greasy, and grind them with flour of rye, and similar medicines that ease the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the joint is dislocated due to continuous friction and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And so move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted turns are hardened and set like stone, and it needs to be opened with iron, if you think that covering just above the bone is best at the subtle incision lightly, then put a dressing and study on the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs, if you want to now move the joint again with care.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, and by chance if he is set on his bed; because this does not allow him to be moved until the swelling subsides: many times have brought forth spasm and other pains; wherever it happens, when it comes to treating the patient, then let him rest, until the swellings cease; then apply a hot, salty water, and oil, then move the limb lightly, and cure each member as the cure will come in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the physicians for treating dislocations of the shoulders with three fingers.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It has happened that the jaws have become dislocated and swollen inside, and there are two kinds of dislocations: either they have a little piece of bone loose in their joint, and softened a little; or they are entirely dislocated and hanging down towards the chin, and block the saliva from the mouth so it cannot be held in, nor can the mouth be closed, and the tongue is driven out with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, so too does the movement repeat itself according to its disposition.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it hastily, and do not delay; and in such a manner that the ministers apply the chief of the patient, and give him some powder from one of his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the mandible within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and with the other two fingers they are held apart, to make equal; and instruct the patient to relax his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he gives it equal, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns after being stiff, especially if they are both mandibles together, apply hot water and oil, until it relaxes lightly; do not delay in setting it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is closed well with softened meat, then put up moist cloths in cerote made from oil and wax, then tie it lightly with soft ligaments; and let the patient sleep on their back, and their limbs should be between two cushions, so that it does not move neither left nor right, neither does force itself to strain, but takes lightly meat, until the pains are gone, and the mandibles are closed; and then take what they want lightly, and do not work hard to open the mouth to eat and drink, until the mandibles are well closed and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be returned to their place in an hour, and are not converted to their own, then it comes with fever and sweating accustomed, and by chance, vomiting from the belly, and by chance, vomiting clear.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is death; and many times have those who have had this died in seven days.
de la forcelle	of the arm.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The arm cannot be dislocated from the breastbone inside and at the elbow, and it is never dislocated without great pain, and one can feel this always.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And restoration is that the patient must lie on his back until his swelling subsides, and then extend his arms; and then press down with his hands to his palm, and it will return; then put on the plaster and bandage, and bind it; and the shoulder joint which is towards the back cannot be dislocated if not; unless again, and if it becomes dislocated once, one must reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage, and bind it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and so also are restored the joints of the back, when they are set in their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways the shoulder joint is dislocated: 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men that percussion or crushing, and inflating the shoulder area of an abscess, and thinks it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they are displaced downwards towards the shoulder joint, and you will find a difference between the diseased and healthy shoulders, and you will find a manifest difference; and you will find a depression at the top of the shoulder, and under the shoulder, the top of the shoulder just like before; and it cannot be returned to its original position or moved from any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you will find it manifestly in the shoulder joint; and this type of dislocation is not hard to return when it is new, or if the patient is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And thus the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the patient above, then put the poultice below the bone, and lift the joint towards the healthy limb; and the ministers lift the hand and extend it upwards, since they place it underneath; if this happens soon.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said four times the previous days, so it is fitting that the patient be bathed in hot water; and he be anointed with a mollifying and soothing substance, like a decoction of altee, fenugrec, and malliolote in hot water, and also anoint him. Then put the patient on his back, and place a cloth of equal thickness neither too soft nor too hard under the bone, then put some linen over the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder properly, and treat the hand of the patient; and one other minister lifts the head of the patient if it does not move downwards; this shoulder will return all now, and you should see if he re-dislocates according to this manner: and thus you must make him be present with one man who is greater than the patient; and stand directly towards his side, and pour hot water onto the shoulder of the patient from under the bone, and lift the bone upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air; and one other minister treats the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so they are weighed with no heavy thing, and the dislocation comes back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And to fix it in another way: and it's like this - they put a long iron rod into the ground, whose joint is also level as a plow, neither too big nor too small; then it's placed under the patient, but only if they have soft skin above, and the patient has their arm bent back towards the stick; then the hand is stretched down from the other side in this way, and the joint returns to its place quickly; and if she does not return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a rod of two arms' length and four feet wide, whose head has an opening enough to fit into deep beneath the axles, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to lie under the head with a cloth wrapped around it, so that the injury may not be touched by the patient, then place it beneath the wound of the patient; and stretch out one arm over the fist of the long one, and bind the assistant above the fist, and the arm at the top of the hand, then place the arm above the bend of an inch-long sleeve, and so extend the hands down, and leave the body hanging from another part: the joint is now fixed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is thus fixed, in any manner whatsoever, it is necessary that you put down the wound with a spear of wool equal, then apply the plaster made of powdered flour of the mill, with incense and wolf fat, on all the shoulder and back; then pull out from below the wound immediately, and turn the bandage upon the plaster, and embrace the hand on its neck, so that the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is fitting that he mends the bone little by little, until the members are comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then he will mend more after five days or seven, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is cured.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen from moisture that has come upon it, or from another cause, it is fitting to administer cauterization three times, as with the cauterization tool in front of or on the cauterizing instrument.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all that, and after seven days the joint does not hold, nor can any arm be lifted upwards, then it seems that the nerves at the shoulder of the neck have been struck, stretched, or softened; and it seems that the joint has never returned to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The injury that is done to the shoulder joint and the knee, or behind, if it is made by force and stretching of hands, and it serves another wound; and treat until he becomes whole.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes greyness to the limb and late movement, then use the patient many times in baths until the greyness is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder cut
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Says that the joint of the shoulder is displaced at points, and returns to points; and if it has been displaced in all directions, and itself in front and behind, for dislocations do not come back, because one sees them well and feels them well; and displaces according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick with the healthy one, so you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For when the joint is swollen, and cannot flex the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is therefore necessary to reset it again so that the abscess comes out, because if an abscess comes out, then it will cause more pain in resetting; and by chance, it cannot be reset completely, especially when it is at the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance someone may die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if restoration is possible, when it can be reset as such that one can reset it, then you extend its hand to both of your hands; and its arms should spread out, and the fingers relaxed according to the shape of the hand, in front and behind, and press the joint into its sockets or at the base of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if a dislocation occurs, when he doubles his hand to his hand, and proud of the root of the palm, the wound is inflicted.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, administer great extension; and if two ministers stretch the arm, and two of them tie it with both hands, so that it does not move when extended; then turn the arm from each direction, after you have stretched a double cloth long and wide; and when the joint aligns itself with the joint, apply oil to ease the joint, then bend the joint tightly, until it becomes straight again; and when it is in its place, put on plastered binding with wool of yew, form the strain, and turn the arm towards the back of the patient, and leave it for some days, then set it free.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, then release the ligament and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, then reapply the plaster and the ligament, and let it be for some days, until it is firmly set; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is put back in place and it becomes stiff, then bathe him well and massage him, and press until he is relaxed; or you apply a fatty mutton shank to the joint, let it be for one day and night, then remove the bone, and let him enter into the bath; and when he sweats, then rub the joint temperately, put on the fatty mutton shank again, and then enter into the bath; and do this twice or three times until he is healed; and if you see, apply fien (fennel) to moist and hot water with lard, and strain it; then it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint in the hand is dislocated and it heals quickly, like all the others. It is recommended to bring it back to its place immediately, in the same hole where it was dislocated, so that the swelling goes down or the abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And if you bring it back in that way, then place the diseased hand on a board and stretch out the fingers of the hand, and straighten the wrist, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pound it till it comes to life. Always, look to see if it is well set; afterwards, put the patient's back against a board at extension and at bringing back.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure. And then you stick two stakes on the top of the patient's arm of great size, and above his feet, two others, and between each stake a space of an inch from above and below; and between them there should be one stake pierced or the turnip turns, and they are firmly grounded so that they do not move; and between the two stakes there should be two more stakes of an inch in length to make the turnip turn, because of the ties that turn; and after tying the tie that is between the joints on the turnip towards the top, and the other tie towards his feet on the other turnip, and each master makes their turnip turn along the entire joint, and the masters put the spine in an even position as we have said.

des dislocations de la hainche	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Those who have the shoulder joints and those of the elbow come only from dislocations, not from anything else; and the joint of the elbow is misaligned in four parts: inside and outside, and before and behind; and it is worse inside than outside, and less so before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of dislocations inside is that when you join the sick leg to the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knees are looser than those of the healthy person, and cannot double their knee movement over the heat; and is the swelling that is near the inflamed joint, because the head of the scaphoid bone comes into contact.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens on the foredoom, so is that this accident is contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it happens on the foredoom, so is that he stands well with his leg according to completion; all his joints are straight without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot do so before, and holds back his urine, and inflates his groin, and when he walks, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it happens behind, so is that he cannot spread his knees, nor bend them, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the femur is displaced below the lower ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this sign of dislocation are that you should return to the place where the dislocation is ancient, and it stays according to its disposition, if there is no cure; and it does not seem necessary that he has assumed.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	In those where the dislocation is fresh, and it's of four kinds, so hasten that you return the joint, and push it inside and forth, and the limb move at right hand and left; by chance if it comes back, and has no other need for a different treatment.

Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common among four types, and if a dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Injury and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When an injury comes with a dislocation, and you try to restore it, many patients die. Do not be presumptuous in your treatment, unless you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and delay things, do not force them. Use gentle methods at first, opening incisions carefully, and let the patient fall into God's hands, if you see no hope of recovery. When you see hope, then straighten the member now as much as possible, so that the incision heals quickly; when the limb is in its place, treat with soothing incisions, and heal the wound, as it should be done, with dried ointments; and if there is a break and small bones are broken, set them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, because that will bring you no profit, but according to your Creator's wisdom, and the skill with which you arm yourself and your body.
